class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chilingarov" title="Chilingarov">Chilingarov</a></span></div></td><td style="width:70px;text-align:center;:"></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_exploration" title="History of exploration">history of exploration</a> by citizens or subjects of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a> and other Russian predecessor states forms a significant part of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">history of Russia</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_world" title="History of the world">history of the world</a>. At 17,075,400 square kilometres (6,592,850&#160;sq&#160;mi), Russia is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_country_in_the_world" title="Largest country in the world">largest country in the world</a>, covering more than a ninth of the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>&#8217;s land mass. In the times of the Soviet Union and the Russian Empire the country\'s share in the world\'s land mass reached 1/6. Most of these territories were first discovered by Russian explorers (if indigenous peoples of inhabited territories are not counted). Contiguous exploration in <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> and the building of overseas colonies in <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a> were some of the primary factors in Russian territorial expansion.\n</p><p>Apart from their discoveries in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_North" title="Extreme North">Extreme North</a>, Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explorers" title="Explorers">explorers</a> have made significant contributions to the exploration of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a> islands, as well as <a href="/wiki/Deep-sea_exploration" title="Deep-sea exploration">deep-sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space</a> exploration.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r872693300">.mw-parser-output .tocright{float:right;clear:right;width:auto;background:none;padding:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em;margin-bottom:.5em}.mw-parser-output class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_Russian_exploration">History of Russian exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History of Russian exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_1000_C.E.">Before 1000 C.E.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Before 1000 C.E.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the settlement of <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Plain" title="Russian Plain">Russian Plain</a> in the middle of the 1st millennium BC, through the next thousand years, most of <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a> came into the sphere of Slavic cultural and political influence, and finally became a part of the Russian state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1000.E2.80.931500"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1000&#8211;1500">1000&#8211;1500</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1000&#8211;1500">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From the 11th century on, a group of Russians which settled the shores of the <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Sea</a> and became known as <a href="/wiki/Pomors" title="Pomors">Pomors</a> ("seaside-dwellers") began navigating in the freezing seas of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, gradually developing the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaking" title="Icebreaking">icebreaking</a> ships known as <a href="/wiki/Koch_(boat)" title="Koch (boat)">kochi</a>. As early as the 11th century Russians from the <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Republic" title="Novgorod Republic">Novgorod Republic</a> had occasionally penetrated into Siberia. In the 14th century the Novgorodians started exploring the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a> and the West-Siberian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Ob" title="River Ob">river Ob</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Russians were among those rare medieval Europeans who traveled deep into <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> or visited <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. Prince <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_II_of_Vladimir" title="Yaroslav II of Vladimir">Yaroslav II of Vladimir</a> and his sons <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Yaroslavich_Nevsky" title="Alexander Yaroslavich Nevsky">Alexander Yaroslavich Nevsky</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrey_Yaroslavich" title="Andrey Yaroslavich">Andrey Yaroslavich</a> traveled to <a href="/wiki/Karakorum" title="Karakorum">Karakorum</a>, the capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolian_Empire" title="Mongolian Empire">Mongolian Empire</a> in the 1240s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nevsky_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-nevsky-3">[3]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Afanasy_Nikitin" title="Afanasy Nikitin">Afanasy Nikitin</a>, a merchant from the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Tver" title="Principality of Tver">Principality of Tver</a>, traveled to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persia</a> and India in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Journey_Beyond_the_Three_Seas" title="A Journey Beyond the Three Seas">A Journey Beyond the Three Seas</a></i> in 1466-1472.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nikitin_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-nikitin-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1500.E2.80.931700"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1500&#8211;1700">1500&#8211;1700</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1500&#8211;1700">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, most of the former principalities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus" title="Kievan Rus">Kievan Rus</a> were re-integrated by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a>. Proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>, by the end of the 16th century the state had colonized the easternmost territories of Europe by conquering the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kazan" title="Khanate of Kazan">Khanate of Kazan</a> in 1552 and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Astrakhan" title="Khanate of Astrakhan">Khanate of Astrakhan</a> in 1556, thus gaining full control of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> valley. The road to Asia was opened, and in 1581 <a href="/wiki/Yermak_Timofeyevich" title="Yermak Timofeyevich">Yermak Timofeyevich</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> with a band of adventurers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Khanate_of_Siberia" title="Conquest of the Khanate of Siberia">defeated</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Khanate" title="Siberian Khanate">Siberian Khanate</a> and started the <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Siberia" title="Russian conquest of Siberia">Russian conquest of Siberia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yermak_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-yermak-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rapid <a href="/wiki/History_of_Siberia" title="History of Siberia">exploration of the vast territories of Siberia</a> was led primarily by <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a> and Pomors hunting for valuable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Furs" title="Furs">furs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spices" title="Spices">spices</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>. Explorers such as Pyanda, <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Beketov" title="Pyotr Beketov">Pyotr Beketov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurbat_Ivanov" title="Kurbat Ivanov">Kurbat Ivanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Moskvitin" title="Ivan Moskvitin">Ivan Moskvitin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasily_Poyarkov" title="Vasily Poyarkov">Vasily Poyarkov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yerofey_Khabarov" title="Yerofey Khabarov">Yerofey Khabarov</a> pushed eastward mostly along the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_River_Routes" title="Siberian River Routes">Siberian River Routes</a>, and by the mid-17th century there were Russian settlements in Eastern Siberia, on the <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukchi Peninsula</a>, along the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>, and on the Pacific coast. In 1648 the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a> between Asia and North America was passed through for the first time by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedot_Popov" title="Fedot Popov">Fedot Popov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a>. The journeys of <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Petlin" title="Ivan Petlin">Ivan Petlin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicolae_Milescu" title="Nicolae Milescu">Nicolae Milescu</a> established contacts between <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_China" title="Ming China">Ming China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petlin_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-petlin-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milescu_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-milescu-7">[7]</a></sup> By the early 18th century Russians under <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Atlasov" title="Vladimir Atlasov">Vladimir Atlasov</a> had colonised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1700s">1700s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1700s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mapping_expeditions">Mapping expeditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mapping expeditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, who turned the country into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in 1721, ordered the first instrumental mapping of Russia, and conceived the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a>, which was carried out after the Emperor\'s death with <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a> as the leader and main organizer. With over 3,000 people directly and indirectly involved, the expedition was one of the largest exploration enterprises in history by its geographic scale and results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Preceded by Bering\'s first voyage through the Bering Strait in 1728-1729 and the European discovery of Alaska by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Fyodorov_(navigator)" title="Ivan Fyodorov (navigator)">Ivan Fyodorov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gvozdev" title="Mikhail Gvozdev">Mikhail Gvozdev</a> in 1732,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gvozdev_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-gvozdev-9">[9]</a></sup> the achievements of the expedition included the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commander_Islands" title="Commander Islands">Commander Islands</a> by Bering and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Chirikov" title="Alexei Chirikov">Alexei Chirikov</a>, the mapping of most of the Russian Arctic coastline and part of the Pacific coast in 1733&#8211;1743 by teams led by <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Malygin" title="Stepan Malygin">Stepan Malygin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Ovtsyn" title="Dmitry Ovtsyn">Dmitry Ovtsyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Minin" title="Fyodor Minin">Fyodor Minin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semyon_Chelyuskin" title="Semyon Chelyuskin">Semyon Chelyuskin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasily_Pronchischev" title="Vasily Pronchischev">Vasily Pronchischev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khariton_Laptev" title="Khariton Laptev">Khariton Laptev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Laptev" title="Dmitry Laptev">Dmitry Laptev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The Academic Squad of the expedition, composed of the early members of the young <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerhard Friedrich M&#252;ller">Gerhard Friedrich M&#252;ller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Georg_Gmelin" title="Johann Georg Gmelin">Johann Georg Gmelin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Krasheninnikov" title="Stepan Krasheninnikov">Stepan Krasheninnikov</a>, inaugurated the first ethnographic, historic, and scientific research into Siberia and Kamchatka.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="America">America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Empire_(1867).svg"><img alt="Russian Empire at its peak in 1866" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Russian_Empire_%281867%29.svg/250px-Russian_Empire_%281867%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Russian_Empire_%281867%29.svg/375px-Russian_Empire_%281867%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Russian_Empire_%281867%29.svg/500px-Russian_Empire_%281867%29.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Empire_(1867).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> at its peak in 1866, including the spheres of influence; this territorial expansion largely corresponds to the extent of contiguous exploration by Russians.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Russian colonization of the Americas">Russian colonization of the Americas</a> followed in the late 18th and early 19th centuries, through the joint efforts of the state and private enterprises such as the <a href="/wiki/Russian-American_Company" title="Russian-American Company">Russian-American Company</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Shelikhov" title="Grigory Shelikhov">Grigory Shelikhov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolay_Rezanov" title="Nikolay Rezanov">Nikolay Rezanov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A._A._Baranov" title="A. A. Baranov">Alexander Baranov</a> and others. Russians mapped most of the Alaskan coasts and nearby islands, explored the inner areas of the peninsula, and went as far south as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Ross" title="Fort Ross">Fort Ross</a> in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baranov_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-baranov-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1800s">1800s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1800s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Circumnavigation">Circumnavigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Circumnavigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 1803&#8211;06 the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> was led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Kruzenshtern" title="Ivan Kruzenshtern">Ivan Kruzenshtern</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yury_Lisyansky" title="Yury Lisyansky">Yury Lisyansky</a>, partly with the aim of establishing direct marine communications between <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> and Russian America. More Russian circumnavigations followed, notably those led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_Kotzebue" title="Otto Kotzebue">Otto Kotzebue</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Wrangel" title="Ferdinand Wrangel">Ferdinand Wrangel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Golovnin" title="Vasily Golovnin">Vasily Golovnin</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fyodor_Litke" title="Fyodor Litke">Fyodor Litke</a>. These voyages brought multiple discoveries in Alaska and the Pacific. In 1820-1821 a round-the-world expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen" title="Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen">Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lazarev" title="Mikhail Lazarev">Mikhail Lazarev</a> on sloops <i><a href="/wiki/Vostok_(sloop-of-war)" title="Vostok (sloop-of-war)">Vostok</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mirny_(sloop-of-war)" title="Mirny (sloop-of-war)">Mirny</a></i> discovered the continent of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bellingshausen_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-bellingshausen-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 19th century the scientific exploration of the inner areas of Siberia intensified. The complex <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orographic" title="Orographic">orographic</a> systems of Central and Eastern Siberia were established by such scientists as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Middendorf" title="Alexander Middendorf">Alexander Middendorf</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Chersky" title="Ivan Chersky">Ivan Chersky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Obruchev" title="Vladimir Obruchev">Vladimir Obruchev</a>. In the middle of the century, around the time of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amur_Annexation" title="Amur Annexation">Amur Annexation</a>, the Russian government put much effort into exploration and colonisation of the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a> valley, <a href="/wiki/Primorsky_Krai" title="Primorsky Krai">Primorsky Krai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_Central_Asia">Conquest of Central Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Conquest of Central Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Central_Asia" title="Russian conquest of Central Asia">Russian conquest of Central Asia</a></div>\n<p>The Russian conquest of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> was accompanied by the penetration of many explorers into the depths of Eurasia, including <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jungaria" title="Jungaria">Jungaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>. Notable explorers in this direction included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chokan_Valikhanov" title="Chokan Valikhanov">Chokan Valikhanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky" title="Pyotr Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky">Pyotr Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Chikhachyov" title="Pyotr Chikhachyov">Pyotr Chikhachyov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Przhevalsky" title="Nikolay Przhevalsky">Nikolay Przhevalsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Grumm-Grzhimaylo" title="Grigory Grumm-Grzhimaylo">Grigory Grumm-Grzhimaylo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronislav_Grombchevsky" title="Bronislav Grombchevsky">Bronislav Grombchevsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Kozlov" title="Pyotr Kozlov">Pyotr Kozlov</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gombojab_Tsybikov" title="Gombojab Tsybikov">Gombojab Tsybikov</a> was the first European explorer in <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a>, but he travelled by the customary road of <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryat</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilgrims" title="Pilgrims">pilgrims</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1900s">1900s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1900s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polar_exploration">Polar exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Polar exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The late 19th century and the early 20th century was marked by a renewed interest in Arctic exploration. Many expeditions of that era met a tragic fate, like the voyages of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eduard_Toll" title="Eduard Toll">Eduard Toll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Brusilov" title="Georgy Brusilov">Georgy Brusilov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Rusanov" title="Vladimir Rusanov">Vladimir Rusanov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Sedov" title="Georgy Sedov">Georgy Sedov</a>, yet brought some valuable geographic results. Modern era polar icebreakers, dating from <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Makarov" title="Stepan Makarov">Stepan Makarov</a>\'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Yermak" title="Icebreaker Yermak">Yermak</a></i>, made  Arctic voyages safer and led to new attempts to explore the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a>. The last major unknown archipelago on Earth, <a href="/wiki/Severnaya_Zemlya" title="Severnaya Zemlya">Severnaya Zemlya</a>, was discovered by <a href="/wiki/Boris_Vilkitsky" title="Boris Vilkitsky">Boris Vilkitsky</a> during his expedition on the icebreakers <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Taymyr" title="Icebreaker Taymyr">Taymyr</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Vaygach" title="Icebreaker Vaygach">Vaygach</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vilkitsky_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-vilkitsky-13">[13]</a></sup> and later explored and mapped by <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Urvantsev" title="Nikolay Urvantsev">Nikolay Urvantsev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Ushakov" title="Georgy Ushakov">Georgy Ushakov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ushakov_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-ushakov-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> <a href="/wiki/Chief_Directorate_of_the_Northern_Sea_Route" title="Chief Directorate of the Northern Sea Route">Chief Directorate of the Northern Sea Route</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_Shmidt" title="Otto Shmidt">Otto Shmidt</a> completed the exploration of the Russian Arctic and established regular marine communications alongside Russia\'s northern shores in the 1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shmidt_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-shmidt-15">[15]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/North_Pole-1" title="North Pole-1">North Pole-1</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Drifting_ice_station" title="Drifting ice station">drifting ice station</a> populated by the team led by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Papanin" title="Ivan Papanin">Ivan Papanin</a>, became the first expedition of its kind in 1937&#8211;38, and inaugurated a succession of drifting polar research stations which continues to this day.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/International_Geophysical_Year" title="International Geophysical Year">International Geophysical Year</a> in 1957-1958 the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> established its presence in the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a>, starting <a href="/wiki/List_of_Soviet_Antarctic_expeditions" title="List of Soviet Antarctic expeditions">a series</a> of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Antarctic_Expedition" title="Soviet Antarctic Expedition">Soviet Antarctic Expeditions</a>. The first expeditions, led by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Somov" title="Mikhail Somov">Mikhail Somov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksei_Treshnikov" title="Aleksei Treshnikov">Aleksei Treshnikov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Tolstikov" title="Yevgeny Tolstikov">Yevgeny Tolstikov</a>, made multiple discoveries in the inner areas of Antarctica and reached the Southern <a href="/wiki/Pole_of_inaccessibility" title="Pole of inaccessibility">Pole of inaccessibility</a> and the Southern <a href="/wiki/Pole_of_Cold" title="Pole of Cold">Pole of Cold</a>. At the latter location, on the site of the <a href="/wiki/Vostok_Station" title="Vostok Station">Vostok Station</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Subglacial_lake" title="Subglacial lake">subglacial</a> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Vostok" title="Lake Vostok">Lake Vostok</a>, one of the last major geographical discoveries on Earth, was detected deep below the Antarctic ice shield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-appeal_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-appeal-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Age">Space Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Space Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">Space Age</a></div>\n<p>In 1957 the Soviet Union opened the <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">Space Age</a> by launching the first Earth-orbiting artificial <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a></i>. Many other Soviet and Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_exploration_records" title="Space exploration records">space exploration records</a> ensued: the first <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflight</a> performed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yury_Gagarin" title="Yury Gagarin">Yury Gagarin</a> on <a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok 1</a> in 1961; the first woman in space, <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Tereshkova" title="Valentina Tereshkova">Valentina Tereshkova</a>, in 1963; the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">spacewalk</a> by <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Leonov" title="Alexey Leonov">Alexey Leonov</a> in 1965; the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_exploration_rover" title="Space exploration rover">space exploration rover</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunokhod-1" title="Lunokhod-1">Lunokhod-1</a></i>, on the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> in 1970, and the first <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">Salyut 1</a></i>, launched in 1971.\n</p><p>The most recent exploration activities by Russians include expeditions on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIR_submersible" title="MIR submersible">MIR submersibles</a>, notably the investigations of the <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">RMS <i>Titanic</i></a> and the planting of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_flag" title="Russian flag">Russian flag</a> on the seabed under the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>, reached for the first time by the <i><a href="/wiki/Arktika_2007" title="Arktika 2007">Arktika 2007</a></i> expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Artur_Chilingarov" title="Artur Chilingarov">Artur Chilingarov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chilingarov_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-chilingarov-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alphabetical_list">Alphabetical list</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dt>Areas primarily explored</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A">A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albanov2.jpg"><img alt="Albanov" data-file-height="472" data-file-width="396" decoding="async" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Albanov2.jpg/100px-Albanov2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Albanov2.jpg/150px-Albanov2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Albanov2.jpg/200px-Albanov2.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Valerian_Albanov" title="Valerian Albanov">Valerian Albanov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1881&#8211;1919)<br/>Russian Navy lieutenant\n</td>\n<td>Albanov was one of the only two survivors of the ill-fated 1912&#8211;14 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brusilov_expedition" title="Brusilov expedition">Brusilov expedition</a>, the other being <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Konrad" title="Alexander Konrad">Alexander Konrad</a>. They left the ice-bound ship <i>St. Anna</i> and by ski, sledge, and kayak crossed the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a>, reached <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a> and were finally rescued by <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Sedov" title="Georgy Sedov">Georgy Sedov</a>\'s <i>Saint Phocas</i>. The data about ice drift of <i>St. Anna</i>, provided by Albanov, helped <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladimir_Vize" title="Vladimir Vize">Vladimir Vize</a> to calculate the coordinates of previously unknown <a href="/wiki/Vize_Island" title="Vize Island">Vize Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alb_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-alb-18">[18]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Either Albanov or Konrad is a prototype for a hero in the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Two_Captains" title="The Two Captains">The Two Captains</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Veniamin_Kaverin" title="Veniamin Kaverin">Veniamin Kaverin</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg"><img alt="St. Anna ship" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="760" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg/120px-S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg/180px-S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg/240px-S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S_S_Yacht_Blencathra.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Svyataya_Anna" title="Svyataya Anna">St. Anna</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pyotr_Anjou.jpeg"><img alt="Anjou" data-file-height="274" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Anjou" title="Pyotr Anjou">Pyotr Anjou</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1796&#8211;1869)<br/>Russian admiral, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Navarino" title="Battle of Navarino">Battle of Navarino</a>\n</td>\n<td>In 1820, as a lieutenant, Anjou described the coastline and the islands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Siberia" title="Eastern Siberia">Eastern Siberia</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Olenyok_River" title="Olenyok River">Olenek</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigirka" title="Indigirka">Indigirka</a> rivers and mapped the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a>. In 1825&#8211;26 he participated in describing the northeastern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> and the western coast of the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbd_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-rbd-19">[19]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anjou_Islands" title="Anjou Islands">Anjou Islands</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Siberian_Islands_map.png"><img alt="New Siberia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1219" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/120px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/180px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/240px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Siberian_Islands_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Danila_Antsiferov" title="Danila Antsiferov">Danila Antsiferov</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;1712)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Cossack" title="Siberian Cossack">Siberian Cossack</a> <a href="/wiki/Ataman" title="Ataman">ataman</a><b></b>\n</td>\n<td>Danila Antsiferov was elected Cossack ataman on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> after the death of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Atlasov" title="Vladimir Atlasov">Vladimir Atlasov</a>. He was one of the first Russians to visit the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a> and describe them in writing, including <a href="/wiki/Shumshu" title="Shumshu">Shumshu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paramushir_Island" title="Paramushir Island">Paramushir Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Antsiferov_Island" title="Antsiferov Island">Antsiferov Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:82px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paramushir,_Atlasov,_Shumshu_-_Landsat_7.jpg"><img title="Paramushir">Paramushir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlasov_Island" title="Atlasov Island">Atlasov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shumshu_Island" title="Shumshu Island">Shumshu Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#fff8e7;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AnuchinDN.jpg"><img alt="Anuchin" data-file-height="1352" data-file-width="1052" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/AnuchinDN.jpg/100px-AnuchinDN.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/AnuchinDN.jpg/150px-AnuchinDN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/AnuchinDN.jpg/200px-AnuchinDN.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Anuchin" title="Dmitry Anuchin">Dmitry Anuchin</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1843&#8211;1923)<br/>geographer, anthropologist, ethnographer, archaeologist\n</td>\n<td>In 1880 Anuchin researched <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valday_Hills" title="Valday Hills">Valday Hills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Seliger" title="Lake Seliger">Lake Seliger</a>. In 1894&#8211;95, joining the expedition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Tillo" title="Alexei Tillo">Alexei Tillo</a>, he again studied Valday. Anuchin finally determined the location of the source of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a>, the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_river" title="European river">European river</a>. He published a major work about the relief of <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a> and founded the Geography Museum at <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsb_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-dsb-21">[21]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anuchin_crater" title="Anuchin crater">Anuchin crater</a> (Moon), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anuchin_Island" title="Anuchin Island">Anuchin Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B8_20.jpg"><img alt="The source of the Volga" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="711" data-file-width="826" decoding="async" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B8_20.jpg/120px-%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B8_20.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B8_20.jpg/180px-%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B8_20.jpg 1.5x, width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B3%D0%B8_20.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The source of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VK_Arsenyev.jpg"><img alt="Arsenyev" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="496" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/VK_Arsenyev.jpg/100px-VK_Arsenyev.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/VK_Arsenyev.jpg/150px-VK_Arsenyev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/VK_Arsenyev.jpg/200px-VK_Arsenyev.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Arsenyev" title="Vladimir Arsenyev">Vladimir Arsenyev</a></b>*<br/>(1872&#8211;1930)<br/>military topographer, writer\n</td>\n<td>Arsenyev wrote a number of popular books about his journeys to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ussuri" title="Ussuri">Ussuri</a> basin in 1902&#8211;07, where he was accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Dersu_Uzala" title="Dersu Uzala">Dersu Uzala</a>, a native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nani_people" title="Nani people">Nanai</a> hunter. Arsenyev was the first to describe numerous species of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberian</a> flora; he produced some 60 works on the geography, wildlife and ethnography of the regions he traveled to. In 1975, the joint Japanese-Soviet movie <i><a href="/wiki/Dersu_Uzala_(1975_film)" title="Dersu Uzala (1975 film)">Dersu Uzala</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Akira_Kurosawa" title="Akira Kurosawa">Akira Kurosawa</a> won an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film">Best Foreign Language Film</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsenyev_(town)" title="Arsenyev (town)">Arsenyev (town)</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:82px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dersuuzala.jpg"><img alt="Dersu Uzala" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="607" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Dersuuzala.jpg/80px-Dersuuzala.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Dersuuzala.jpg/120px-Dersuuzala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Dersuuzala.jpg/160px-Dersuuzala.jpg 2x" width="80"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dersuuzala.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dersu_Uzala" title="Dersu Uzala">Dersu Uzala</a>, photo by Arsenyev</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg"><img alt="Atlasov" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="281" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg/110px-Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg/165px-Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Atlasov.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Atlasov" title="Vladimir Atlasov">Vladimir Atlasov</a></b>*<br/>(1661/64&#8211;1711)<br/>Siberian Cossack ataman\n</td>\n<td>Atlasov established the first permanent Russian settlements on <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">Kamchatka Peninsula</a> and led its colonisation. He was the first to present a detailed description of the region\'s nature and people, and also accounted on the lands near Kamchatka &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukotka</a> and Japan. Atlasov brought <a href="/wiki/Dembei" title="Dembei">Dembei</a>, a shipwrecked Japanese merchant, to Moscow, where he conducted the first <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language_education_in_Russia" title="Japanese language education in Russia">Japanese language education in Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Atlasov_Island" title="Atlasov Island">Atlasov Island</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlasov_volcano" title="Atlasov volcano">Atlasov volcano</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:82px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg"><img alt="Kamchatka" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="15666" data-file-width="9000" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg/80px-Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg/120px-Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg/160px-Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg 2x" width="80"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kamchatka_peninsula_topo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topography of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="B">B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: B">edit</a><span </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" 1.5x" width="140"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Babushkin" title="Mikhail Babushkin">Mikhail Babushkin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1893&#8211;1938)<br/>military and polar aviator, <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">Hero of the Soviet Union</a>\n</td>\n<td>Babushkin took part in an expedition to rescue <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Nobile" title="Umberto Nobile">Umberto Nobile</a> in 1928, and in the rescue of the <i><a href="/wiki/SS_Chelyuskin" title="SS Chelyuskin">SS Chelyuskin</a></i> crew in 1933. He performed the flights to the first drifting ice station <i><a href="/wiki/North_Pole-1" title="North Pole-1">North Pole-1</a></i> in 1937. In 1937&#8211;38 he participated in a search for <a href="/wiki/Sigizmund_Levanevsky" title="Sigizmund Levanevsky">Sigizmund Levanevsky</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babushkinsky_District_(Moscow)" title="Babushkinsky District (Moscow)">Babushkinsky District (Moscow)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babushkinskaya_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Babushkinskaya (Moscow Metro)">Babushkinskaya (Moscow Metro)</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg"><img alt="Chelyuskin" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="492" data-file-width="800" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg/180px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg/240px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" Chelyuskin</a></i> sinking</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg"><img alt="Konstantin Badigin" data-file-height="1417" data-file-width="2023" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg/140px-Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg/210px-Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg/280px-Badigin_Konstantin_Sergeevich.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Badygin" title="Konstantin Badygin">Konstantin Badygin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1910&#8211;1984)<br/>Soviet Navy captain, writer, scientist, Hero of the USSR<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(Badygin left, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sedov" title="Icebreaker Sedov"><i>Sedov</i></a>\'s mechanic D.G. Trofimov right)</span>\n</td>\n<td>In 1938 Badygin became the captain of the ice-captured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sedov" title="Icebreaker Sedov">icebreaker Sedov</a>, turned into a kind of <a href="/wiki/Drifting_ice_station" title="Drifting ice station">drifting ice station</a>. Most of the crew was evacuated, but 15 sailors and scientists, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladimir_Vize" title="Vladimir Vize">Vladimir Vize</a>, stayed aboard and carried out valuable scientific research in the course of 812 days. After drifting from <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a> across the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>, they were finally freed between <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a> by <a href="/wiki/Sibir_(1937_icebreaker)" title="Sibir (1937 icebreaker)">icebreaker Joseph Stalin</a> in 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G_SedovMarka.jpg"><img alt="Icebreaker Sedov" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="458" data-file-width="659" decoding="async" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/G_SedovMarka.jpg/120px-G_SedovMarka.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/G_SedovMarka.jpg/180px-G_SedovMarka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/G_SedovMarka.jpg/240px-G_SedovMarka.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G_SedovMarka.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sedov" title="Icebreaker Sedov">Icebreaker Sedov</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#fff8e7;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg"><img alt="Baer" data-file-height="781" data-file-width="606" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg/110px-Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg/165px-Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg/220px-Karl_Ernst_von_Baer_2.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Karl_Ernst_von_Baer" title="Karl Ernst von Baer">Karl Ernst von Baer</a></b>*<br/>(1792&#8211;1876)<br/>naturalist, a founder of <a href="/wiki/Embryology" title="Embryology">embryology</a>\n</td>\n<td>In 1830&#8211;40 Baer researched <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> meteorology. He was interested in the northern part of Russia and explored <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> in 1837 collecting specimens. Other travels led him to the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A1pmi_(area)" title="S&#225;pmi (area)">Lapland</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Cape,_Norway" title="North Cape, Norway">North Cape, Norway</a>. After his explorations of the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> he formulated the geological <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baer%27s_law" title="Baer\'s law">Baer\'s law</a></i>, stating that in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> occurs mostly on the right banks of rivers, and in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> on the left banks. Baer was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a> in 1845, and also a co-founder and the first President of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Entomological_Society" title="Russian Entomological Society">Russian Entomological Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dsb_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-dsb-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rgolibrary.jpg"><img alt="Library of the Russian Geographical Society" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="549" decoding="async" height="78" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Rgolibrary.jpg/120px-Rgolibrary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Rgolibrary.jpg/180px-Rgolibrary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Rgolibrary.jpg/240px-Rgolibrary.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rgolibrary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Library of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a> in 1916</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgiy_Baidukov" title="Georgiy Baidukov">Georgiy Baidukov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1904&#8211;1994)<br/>military and test pilot, Hero of the Soviet Union<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(<b>Baidukov</b>, Chkalov and Belyakov in 1937)</span>\n</td>\n<td>Baidukov was involved in a number of Soviet ultralong flights. In 1936 <a href="/wiki/Valery_Chkalov" title="Valery Chkalov">Valery Chkalov</a>, Baidukov and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Vasilyevich_Belyakov" title="Alexander Vasilyevich Belyakov">A.V.Belyakov</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ANT-25" title="ANT-25">ANT-25</a> flew 9,374&#160;km from Moscow through the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a> to follow-up <a href="/wiki/Chkalov_Island" title="Chkalov Island">Chkalov Island</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okhotsk_Sea" title="Okhotsk Sea">Okhotsk Sea</a>, which took 56 h 20&#160;min. In 1937, also on ANT-25, the same crew flew 8,504&#160;km from Moscow through the North Pole to <a href="/wiki/Vancouver,_Washington" title="Vancouver, Washington">Vancouver, Washington</a>, which was the first transpolar flight between Europe and North America by airplane, rather than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dirigible" title="Dirigible">dirigible</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Baydukov_Island" title="Baydukov Island">Baydukov Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chkalov1w.png"><img alt="Chkalov and Baydukov Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="894" data-file-width="1152" decoding="async" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Chkalov1w.png/120px-Chkalov1w.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Chkalov1w.png/180px-Chkalov1w.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Chkalov1w.png/240px-Chkalov1w.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chkalov1w.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chkalov_Island" title="Chkalov Island">Chkalov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baydukov_Island" title="Baydukov Island">Baydukov Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baranov_Alexandr.jpg"><img alt="Baranov" data-file-height="1086" data-file-width="899" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Baranov_Alexandr.jpg/110px-Baranov_Alexandr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Baranov_Alexandr.jpg/165px-Baranov_Alexandr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Baranov_Alexandr.jpg/220px-Baranov_Alexandr.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Andreyevich_Baranov" title="Alexander Andreyevich Baranov">Alexander Baranov</a></b>^<br/>(1746&#8211;1819)<br/>merchant, colonial administrator\n</td>\n<td>Baranov was hired to head the <a href="/wiki/Shelikhov-Golikov_Company" title="Shelikhov-Golikov Company">Shelikhov-Golikov Company</a>, which in 1799 was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Russian-American_Company" title="Russian-American Company">Russian-American Company</a>. Thus Baranov became the first governor of <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a> and held this post in 1799&#8211;1818. He explored the coast areas of northwestern North America, helped <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox" title="Russian Orthodox">Russian Orthodox</a> missionaries and improved relations with <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> natives. He established trade with China, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> and also with <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, where he founded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Ross" title="Fort Ross">Fort Ross</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baranov_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-baranov-11">[11]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Baranof_Island" title="Baranof Island">Baranof Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Ross_inside.jpg"><img alt="Fort Ross" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="1021" decoding="async" height="73" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Fort_Ross_inside.jpg/180px-Fort_Ross_inside.jpg 1.5x, title="California">California</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nikifor_Begichev_bust.jpg"><img alt="Begichev" data-file-height="604" data-file-width="436" decoding="async" height="139" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Nikifor_Begichev_bust.jpg/200px-Nikifor_Begichev_bust.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nikifor_Begichev" title="Nikifor Begichev">Nikifor Begichev</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (1874&#8211;1927)<br/>Russian Navy officer<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forensic" title="Forensic">forensic</a> facial reconstruction)</span>\n</td>\n<td>Begichev was the bosun of the ship <i><a href="/wiki/Zarya_(polar_ship)" title="Zarya (polar ship)">Zarya</a></i>, carrying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eduard_Toll" title="Eduard Toll">Eduard Toll</a>\'s expedition in 1900&#8211;03. In 1922, at the request of Norway, Begichev led a Soviet expedition in search of the lost crew members of <a href="/wiki/Roald_Amundsen" title="Roald Amundsen">Roald Amundsen</a>\'s 1918 expedition on the ship <i><a href="/wiki/Maud_(ship)" title="Maud (ship)">Maud</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tessem_and_Paul_Knutsen" title="Peter Tessem and Paul Knutsen">Peter Tessem and Paul Knutsen</a>, but was unsuccessful (remains were later found by <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Rybin" title="Georgy Rybin">Georgy Rybin</a>). In 1923&#8211;24 Begichev explored the <a href="/wiki/Taymyr_Peninsula" title="Taymyr Peninsula">Taymyr Peninsula</a> with <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Urvantsev" title="Nikolay Urvantsev">Nikolay Urvantsev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barr2_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barr2-27">[27]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Bolshoy_Begichev_Island" title="Bolshoy Begichev Island">Bolshoy Begichev Island</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maliy_Begichev_Island" title="Maliy Begichev Island">Maliy Begichev Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2BB.PNG"><img alt="Begichev Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="701" decoding="async" height="91" location</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Beketov" title="Pyotr Beketov">Pyotr Beketov</a></b>*<br/> (c. 1600&#8211;c. 1661)<br/>Siberian Cossack voevoda<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(a monument in <a href="/wiki/Chita,_Zabaykalsky_Krai" title="Chita, Zabaykalsky Krai">Chita, Zabaykalsky Krai</a>)</span>\n</td>\n<td>Beketov, initially a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strelets" title="Strelets">strelets</a>, was appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enisei" title="Enisei">Enisei</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voevoda" title="Voevoda">voevoda</a> in Siberia after 1627. He successfully carried out the voyage to collect taxes from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zabaykalye" title="Zabaykalye">Zabaykalye</a> <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryats</a>, becoming the first Russian to set foot in <a href="/wiki/Buryatia" title="Buryatia">Buryatia</a>. He founded the first Russian settlement there, Rybinsky <a href="/wiki/Ostrog_(fortress)" title="Ostrog (fortress)">ostrog</a>. Beketov was sent to the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a> in 1631, where in 1632 he founded <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsk</a>, a startpoint of further Russian expeditions eastward, southward and northward. He sent his Cossacks to explore the <a href="/wiki/Aldan_River" title="Aldan River">Aldan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kolyma_river" title="Kolyma river">Kolyma rivers</a>, to found new fortresses, and to collect taxes. In 1652 he launched another voyage to Buryatia, and in 1653 Beketov\'s Cossacks founded follow-up <a href="/wiki/Chita,_Zabaykalsky_Krai" title="Chita, Zabaykalsky Krai">Chita</a> and then future <a href="/wiki/Nerchinsk" title="Nerchinsk">Nerchinsk</a> in 1654.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Y-ostrog.jpg"><img alt="A tower of Yakutsky ostrog" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Y-ostrog.jpg/120px-Y-ostrog.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Y-ostrog.jpg/180px-Y-ostrog.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Y-ostrog.jpg/240px-Y-ostrog.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Y-ostrog.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tower of <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsky</a> <a href="/wiki/Ostrog_(fortress)" title="Ostrog (fortress)">ostrog</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Cherkassky_Bekovich.jpg"><img alt="Bekovich-Cherkassky" data-file-height="104" data-file-width="93" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8a/Alexander_Cherkassky_Bekovich.jpg" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Bekovich-Cherkassky" title="Alexander Bekovich-Cherkassky">Alexander Bekovich-Cherkassky</a></b>!<br/>(?&#8211;1717)<br/>Russian Army officer\n</td>\n<td>Bekovich-Cherkassky, a <a href="/wiki/Circassia" title="Circassia">Circassian</a> Muslim converted to Christianity, was made by <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsar</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a> the leader of the first Russian military expeditions into <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> in 1714&#8211;17, with the aim of conquering the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khanate of Khiva</a> and the golden sands of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxus" title="Oxus">Oxus</a> River. Bekovich received these orders in <a href="/wiki/Astrakhan" title="Astrakhan">Astrakhan</a>, where he was engaged in preparing the first Russian map of the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>. He commanded a preliminary expedition to Turkmenistan and set up the forts in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krasnovodsk" title="Krasnovodsk">Krasnovodsk</a> and Alexandrovsk. In 1717 he won the battle against Khivan Khan, but was tricked into separating his men, betrayed by the Khan, defeated and killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caspianseamap.png"><img alt="Caspian Sea" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="602" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Caspianseamap.png/120px-Caspianseamap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Caspianseamap.png/180px-Caspianseamap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Caspianseamap.png/240px-Caspianseamap.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caspianseamap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Admiral_Faddey_Faddeyevich_Bellingshausen.jpg"><img alt="Bellingshausen" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="449" decoding="async" height="141"
