</li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#FFFFFF;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gagarin_in_Sweden.jpg"><img alt="Gagarin" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="176" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Gagarin_in_Sweden.jpg/100px-Gagarin_in_Sweden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Gagarin_in_Sweden.jpg/150px-Gagarin_in_Sweden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/Gagarin_in_Sweden.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yury_Gagarin" title="Yury Gagarin">Yury Gagarin</a></b>$<br/> (1934&#8211;1968)<br/>Soviet Air Force pilot, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" title="Cosmonaut">cosmonaut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">Hero of the Soviet Union</a>\n</td>\n<td>On <a href="/wiki/Cosmonautics_Day" title="Cosmonautics Day">12 April 1961</a>, Gagarin became the first human to travel into space, launching into orbit aboard the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostok_program" title="Vostok program">Vostok 3KA-3</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok 1</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Gagarin,_Russia" title="Gagarin, Russia">Gagarin</a> (Russia), <a href="/wiki/Gagarin,_Armenia" title="Gagarin, Armenia">Gagarin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gagarinsky_(inhabited_locality)" title="Gagarinsky (inhabited locality)">Gagarinsky (inhabited locality)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gagarinsky_District" title="Gagarinsky District">Gagarinsky District</a>, <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Gagarinskaya_metro_station_(disambiguation)" title="Gagarinskaya metro station (disambiguation)">Gagarinskaya metro station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_(crater)" title="Gagarin (crater)">Gagarin crater</a> (Moon), asteroid <a href="/wiki/1772_Gagarin" title="1772 Gagarin">1772 Gagarin</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kosmonavt_Yuri_Gagarin" title="Kosmonavt Yuri Gagarin">Kosmonavt Yuri Gagarin</a></i> (ship), <a href="/wiki/Gagarin%27s_Start" title="Gagarin\'s Start">Gagarin\'s Start</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gagarin_Cosmonaut_Training_Center" title="Gagarin Cosmonaut Training Center">Gagarin Cosmonaut Training Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Air_Force_Academy" title="Gagarin Air Force Academy">Gagarin Air Force Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Cup" title="Gagarin Cup">Gagarin Cup</a>;  <a href="/wiki/Cosmonautics_Day" title="Cosmonautics Day">Cosmonautics Day</a> aka <a href="/wiki/Yuri%27s_Night" title="Yuri\'s Night">Yuri\'s Night</a> is a yearly celebration of Gagarin\'s flight on 12 April.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center">\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yakov_Gakkel" title="Yakov Gakkel">Yakov Gakkel</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1901&#8211;1965)<br/>oceanographer\n</td>\n<td>Gakkel was a director of the geography department of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_and_Antarctic_Research_Institute" title="Arctic and Antarctic Research Institute">Arctic and Antarctic Research Institute</a>. He participated in numerous <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> expeditions, including the ones on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sibiryakov" title="Icebreaker Sibiryakov">icebreaker Sibiryakov</a> in 1932 and on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chelyuskin_steamship" title="Chelyuskin steamship">Chelyuskin steamship</a> in 1934. He was the first to create a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bathymetric" title="Bathymetric">bathymetric</a> map of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Gakkel_Ridge" title="Gakkel Ridge">Gakkel Ridge</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IBCAO_betamap.jpg"><img alt="Arctic Ocean" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="868" data-file-width="762" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/IBCAO_betamap.jpg/120px-IBCAO_betamap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/IBCAO_betamap.jpg/180px-IBCAO_betamap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/IBCAO_betamap.jpg/240px-IBCAO_betamap.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IBCAO_betamap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bathymetric" title="Bathymetric">Bathymetric</a> map of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic</a> with <a href="/wiki/Gakkel_Ridge" title="Gakkel Ridge">Gakkel Ridge</a> on it</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Matvei_Gedenschtrom" title="Matvei Gedenschtrom">Matvei Gedenschtrom</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1780&#8211;1845)<br/>public servant, scientist\n</td>\n<td>Gedenschtrom was sent to serve in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> for his connection with a <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">smuggling</a> affair at <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a> <a href="/wiki/Customs" title="Customs">customs</a>. In 1809&#8211;10 together with <a href="/wiki/Yakov_Sannikov" title="Yakov Sannikov">Yakov Sannikov</a> he led the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartographic" title="Cartographic">cartographic</a> expedition to the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> shores of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yakutia" title="Yakutia">Yakutia</a>. They explored and named the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a> (earlier discovered by <a href="/wiki/Yakov_Permyakov" title="Yakov Permyakov">Yakov Permyakov</a>). This expedition established a theory about the existence of the legendary <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a> somewhere northwest of <a href="/wiki/Kotelny_Island" title="Kotelny Island">Kotelny Island</a>. Gedenschtrom discovered the presence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_polynya" title="Siberian polynya">Siberian polynya</a> (patches of open water at the edge of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drifting_ice" title="Drifting ice">drifting ice</a> and continental <a href="/wiki/Fast_ice" title="Fast ice">fast ice</a>). He charted the coastline between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yana_(river)" title="Yana (river)">Yana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma Rivers</a>. He made numerous trips across <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yakutia" title="Yakutia">Yakutia</a> and the areas east of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbd_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-rbd-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Siberian_Islands_map.png"><img alt="New Siberia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1219" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/120px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/180px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/240px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Siberian_Islands_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg"><img alt="Georgi" data-file-height="1388" data-file-width="864" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg/90px-Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg/135px-Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg/180px-Georgi_Johann_Gottlied_1729%E2%80%931802.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottlieb_Georgi" title="Johann Gottlieb Georgi">Johann Gottlieb Georgi</a></b>*<br/>(1729&#8211;1802)<br/>geographer, naturalist, ethnographer, physician, chemist\n</td>\n<td>Georgi accompanied both <a href="/wiki/Johan_Peter_Falk" title="Johan Peter Falk">Johan Peter Falk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Simon_Pallas" title="Peter Simon Pallas">Peter Simon Pallas</a> on their respective journeys through <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. In 1772 he mapped <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> and was the first to describe <a href="/wiki/Omul" title="Omul">omul</a> fish, as well as other fauna and flora of the Baikal region. He amassed a large collection of minerals and in 1776&#8211;80 published the first comprehensive work on the ethnography of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Russia" title="Indigenous peoples of Russia">indigenous peoples of Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Dahlia" title="Dahlia">Georgia</a> flower.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thymallus_baikalensis,_Baikal-Museum,_Listvyanka,_Irkutsk_Oblast,_Russia_-_20080405.jpg"><img alt="Omul fish" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1309" data-file-width="2213" decoding="async" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Thymallus_baikalensis%2C_Baikal-Museum%2C_Listvyanka%2C_Irkutsk_Oblast%2C_Russia_-_20080405.jpg/120px-Thymallus_baikalensis%2C_Baikal-Museum%2C_Listvyanka%2C_Irkutsk_Oblast%2C_Russia_-_20080405.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Thymallus_baikalensis%2C_Baikal-Museum%2C_Listvyanka%2C_Irkutsk_Oblast%2C_Russia_-_20080405.jpg/180px-Thymallus_baikalensis%2C_Baikal-Museum%2C_Listvyanka%2C_Irkutsk_Oblast%2C_Russia_-_20080405.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Thymallus_baikalensis%2C_Baikal-Museum%2C_Listvyanka%2C_Irkutsk_Oblast%2C_Russia_-_20080405.jpg/240px-Thymallus_baikalensis%2C_Baikal-Museum%2C_Listvyanka%2C_Irkutsk_Oblast%2C_Russia_-_20080405.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thymallus_baikalensis,_Baikal-Museum,_Listvyanka,_Irkutsk_Oblast,_Russia_-_20080405.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Omul" title="Omul">Omul</a> in an aquarium in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Baikal</a>-Museum in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Listvyanka,_Irkutsk_Oblast" title="Listvyanka, Irkutsk Oblast">Listvyanka</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg"><img alt="Gmelin" data-file-height="489" data-file-width="340" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg/90px-Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg/135px-Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg/180px-Gmelin_Johann_Georg_1709-1755.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Johann_Georg_Gmelin" title="Johann Georg Gmelin">Johann Georg Gmelin</a></b>*<br/>(1709&#8211;1755)<br/>naturalist, botanist, geographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1733&#8211;43 Gmelin participated in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> and made a number of journeys through <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, covering more than 34,000&#160;km in total. He discovered that the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> lies below sea level. He published two major works about his travels in Russia and the flora of Siberia, and described more than 500 previously unknown plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Gmelina" title="Gmelina">Gmelina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larix_gmelinii" title="Larix gmelinii">Larix gmelinii</a> plant genera.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg"><img alt="Gmelina plant" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="76" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg/120px-Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg/180px-Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg/240px-Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flowering_at_Canopy_I_IMG_3456.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Gmelina_arborea" title="Gmelina arborea">Gmelina arborea</a></i></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GolovninB%26W.jpg"><img alt="Golovnin" data-file-height="228" data-file-width="198" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GolovninB%26W.jpg/100px-GolovninB%26W.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/GolovninB%26W.jpg/150px-GolovninB%26W.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/GolovninB%26W.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vasily_Golovnin" title="Vasily Golovnin">Vasily Golovnin</a></b>^<br/>(1776&#8211;1831)<br/>Russian admiral, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>Golovnin made two <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigations</a> on the sloop <i>Diana</i> (1807&#8211;09) and the frigate <i><a href="/wiki/Russian_frigate_Kamchatka" title="Russian frigate Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a></i> (1817&#8211;19). In 1811 he described and mapped part of the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>. At that time he was taken prisoner for two years by the Japanese. He described his years in captivity, life in Japan, and his voyages around the world in books. Later he was the general <a href="/wiki/Quartermaster" title="Quartermaster">quartermaster</a> of the Russian Navy and supervised the building of the first Russian <a href="/wiki/Steamship" title="Steamship">steamships</a>. He tutored <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fyodor_Litke" title="Fyodor Litke">Fyodor Litke</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Wrangel" title="Ferdinand Wrangel">Ferdinand Wrangel</a> and other seafarers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Golovin,_Alaska" title="Golovin, Alaska">Golovin, Alaska</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golovninmap.jpg"><img alt="Golovnin\'s circumnavigations" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="953" data-file-width="1612" decoding="async" height="71" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Golovninmap.jpg/120px-Golovninmap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Golovninmap.jpg/180px-Golovninmap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Golovninmap.jpg/240px-Golovninmap.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golovninmap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Golovnin\'s <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigations</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg"><img alt="Gromchevsky" data-file-height="242" data-file-width="206" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg/100px-Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg/150px-Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg/200px-Bronislaw_Grabczewski.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronislav_Gromchevsky" title="Bronislav Gromchevsky">Bronislav Gromchevsky</a></b>!<br/>(1855&#8211;1926)<br/>Russian Army officer\n</td>\n<td>Gromchevsky participated in the Russian conquest of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and led reconnaissance expeditions in the surrounding regions. In 1885&#8211;86 he explored <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a>. In 1888&#8211;89 he explored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pamirs" title="Pamirs">Pamirs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kafiristan" title="Kafiristan">Kafiristan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> and northwestern <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> and went as far as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a>. He is regarded as the Russian counterpart to the British military-explorer <a href="/wiki/Francis_Younghusband" title="Francis Younghusband">Francis Younghusband</a>. The two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Game" title="Great Game">Great Game</a> rivals famously met in 1889 when they were exploring the <a href="/wiki/Hunza_Valley" title="Hunza Valley">Hunza Valley</a>. In 1900 Gromchevsky explored North Eastern China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica11_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-britannica11-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kashmir_region_2004.jpg"><img alt="Kashmir region" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1567" data-file-width="1579" decoding="async" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kashmir_region_2004.jpg/120px-Kashmir_region_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kashmir_region_2004.jpg/180px-Kashmir_region_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kashmir_region_2004.jpg/240px-Kashmir_region_2004.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kashmir_region_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> region</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GrumGrshmailo.jpg"><img alt="Grumm-Grzhimaylo" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="150" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/GrumGrshmailo.jpg/100px-GrumGrshmailo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/GrumGrshmailo.jpg 1.5x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Grigory_Grumm-Grzhimaylo" title="Grigory Grumm-Grzhimaylo">Grigory Grumm-Grzhimaylo</a></b>!<br/>(1860&#8211;1936)<br/>zoologist, entomologist, ethnographer, geographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1884 Grumm-Grzhimaylo started his first Pamir expedition on which he explored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alai_Mountains" title="Alai Mountains">Alai Mountains</a> and reached as far as <a href="/wiki/Karakul_(Tajikistan)" title="Karakul (Tajikistan)">Lake Karakul</a>. In 1885&#8211;87 he traveled extensively through <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, reaching the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Chatyr-Kul" title="Lake Chatyr-Kul">Lake Chatyr-Kul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a>. In 1889&#8211;90 he discovered the <a href="/wiki/Ayding_Lake" title="Ayding Lake">Ayding Lake</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_elevation_extremes_by_country" title="Table of elevation extremes by country">second lowest land point</a> on Earth, at 130&#160;m below sea level. He obtained two <a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_horse" title="Przewalski\'s horse">Przewalski\'s horses</a>, over 1000 bird specimens and tens of thousands of insects during his 8600&#160;km long travels. In 1903 he explored <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuva" title="Tuva">Tuva</a> and later traveled in the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica11_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-britannica11-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aydingkol1.jpg"><img alt="Stele at the Ayding Lake" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="484" data-file-width="740" decoding="async" height="78" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Aydingkol1.jpg/120px-Aydingkol1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Aydingkol1.jpg/180px-Aydingkol1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Aydingkol1.jpg/240px-Aydingkol1.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aydingkol1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stele at the <a href="/wiki/Ayding_Lake" title="Ayding Lake">Ayding Lake</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gvozdev" title="Mikhail Gvozdev">Mikhail Gvozdev</a></b>^<br/>(1700/04&#8211;after 1759)<br/>military <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geodesist" title="Geodesist">geodesist</a>\n</td>\n<td>Gvozdev took part in the 1st <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> expedition of <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a>. In 1732 together with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Fedorov_(navigator)" title="Ivan Fedorov (navigator)">Ivan Fedorov</a> aboard <i>Sviatoi Gavriil</i> (Bering\'s ship) they reached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dezhnev_Cape" title="Dezhnev Cape">Dezhnev Cape</a> (the easternmost point of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>), sailed east and soon discovered the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> mainland near the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Prince_of_Wales" title="Cape Prince of Wales">Cape Prince of Wales</a> (the westernmost point of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>). They charted that part of the Alaskan coast and discovered three new islands. Thus they completed the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>, once started by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedot_Popov" title="Fedot Popov">Fedot Popov</a> and continued by Bering. Subsequently, in 1741&#8211;42 Gvozdev participated in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> and mapped most of the western and southern shores of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okhotsk_Sea" title="Okhotsk Sea">Okhotsk Sea</a>, and the eastern shore of <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gvozdev_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-gvozdev-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png"><img alt="Sea of Okhotsk, Kamchatka, Alaska" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="903" data-file-width="990" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png/120px-Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png/180px-Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png/240px-Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sea_of_Okhotsk_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Pacific" title="North Pacific">North Pacific</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gagemester.jpg"><img alt="Hagemeister" data-file-height="816" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gagemester.jpg/90px-Gagemester.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gagemester.jpg/135px-Gagemester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gagemester.jpg/180px-Gagemester.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Ludwig_von_Hagemeister" title="Ludwig von Hagemeister">Ludwig von Hagemeister</a></b>^<br/>(1780&#8211;1833)<br/>Russian Navy captain, colonial administrator, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>After taking part in the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, in 1806&#8211;07 Hagemeister journeyed to <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> as captain of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_warship_Neva" title="Russian warship Neva">Neva</a></i> (former ship of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisyansky" title="Lisyansky">Lisyansky</a>). In 1808&#8211;09, he explored the shores of Alaska and the waters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Pacific" title="North Pacific">North Pacific</a>. In 1812&#8211;15 he supervised the building of the first <a href="/wiki/Tall_ship" title="Tall ship">tall ships</a> to sail on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a>. In 1816&#8211;19 he made a circumnavigation on <i>Kutuzov</i>, with a stop in Alaska, where he was a governor of <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a> in 1818&#8211;19. In 1828&#8211;29, Hagemeister made his second circumnavigation aboard <i>Krotky</i>. Among other islands, he surveyed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kwajalein" title="Kwajalein">Menshikov Atoll (Kwajalein)</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Hagemeister_Island" title="Hagemeister Island">Hagemeister Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapgagenmester.jpg"><img alt="Hagemeister\'s circumnavigations" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1407" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Mapgagenmester.jpg/120px-Mapgagenmester.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Mapgagenmester.jpg/180px-Mapgagenmester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Mapgagenmester.jpg/240px-Mapgagenmester.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapgagenmester.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hagemeister\'s <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigations</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a href="#B">B</a></li>\n<li><a href="#C">C</a></li>\n<li><a href="#D">D</a></li>\n<li><a href="#E">E</a></li>\n<li><a href="#F">F</a></li>\n<li><a href="#G">G</a></li>\n<li><a href="#H">H</a></li>\n<li><a href="#I">I</a></li>\n<li><a href="#J">J</a></li>\n<li><a href="#K">K</a></li>\n<li><a href="#L">L</a></li>\n<li><a href="#M">M</a></li>\n<li><a href="#N">N</a></li>\n<li><a href="#O">O</a></li>\n<li><a href="#P">P</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Q">Q</a></li>\n<li><a href="#R">R</a></li>\n<li><a href="#S">S</a></li>\n<li><a href="#T">T</a></li>\n<li><a href="#U">U</a></li>\n<li><a href="#V">V</a></li>\n<li><a href="#W">W</a></li>\n<li><a href="#X">X</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Y">Y</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Z">Z</a> </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Kurbat_Ivanov" title="Kurbat Ivanov">Kurbat Ivanov</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;1666)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Cossack" title="Siberian Cossack">Siberian Cossack</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voevoda" title="Voevoda">voevoda</a>\n</td>\n<td>In 1642, on the basis of explorations made by <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Moskvitin" title="Ivan Moskvitin">Ivan Moskvitin</a>, Ivanov made the earliest known map of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>. In 1643 with a group of Cossacks he sailed up the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a> from Verkholensky <a href="/wiki/Ostrog_(fortress)" title="Ostrog (fortress)">ostrog</a>, having decided to check the rumors of a large body of water to the south. They crossed the <a href="/wiki/Baikal_Mountains" title="Baikal Mountains">Baikal Mountains</a> by foot, descended down the <a href="/wiki/Sarma_River" title="Sarma River">Sarma River</a>, discovered <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> and visited its <a href="/wiki/Olkhon_Island" title="Olkhon Island">Olkhon Island</a>. Ivanov made the first chart and description of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Baikal</a>. In 1659&#8211;65 Ivanov was the next head of <a href="/wiki/Anadyrsk" title="Anadyrsk">Anadyrsky</a> ostrog after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a>. In 1660 he sailed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anadyr_Bay" title="Anadyr Bay">Anadyr Bay</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Dezhnyov" title="Cape Dezhnyov">Cape Dezhnyov</a>. He is credited with the creation of the early map of <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukotka</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>, which was the first to show on paper (schematically) the yet undiscovered <a href="/wiki/Wrangel_Island" title="Wrangel Island">Wrangel Island</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Diomede_Islands" title="Diomede Islands">Diomede Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lena_watershed.png"><img alt="Lena River and Lake Baikal" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Lena_watershed.png/120px-Lena_watershed.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Lena_watershed.png/180px-Lena_watershed.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Lena_watershed.png/240px-Lena_watershed.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lena_watershed.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Gerasim_Izmailov" title="Gerasim Izmailov">Gerasim Izmailov</a></b>^<br/>(c. 1745&#8211;after 1795)<br/>Russian Navy officer\n</td>\n<td>In 1771 Izmailov was caught up in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benevsky_mutiny" title="Benevsky mutiny">Benevsky mutiny</a> while serving on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>. After an attempt to break away from the mutineers he was marooned on <a href="/wiki/Simushir" title="Simushir">Simushir</a>, an uninhabited isle in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurils" title="Kurils">Kurils</a>. For a year he lived like <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Crusoe" title="Robinson Crusoe">Robinson Crusoe</a> before being rescued, tried on charges of mutiny and cleared. From 1775 he created the first detailed map of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a>. In 1778 he met with Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unalaska" title="Unalaska">Unalaska</a>. In 1783&#8211;85 Izmaylov and <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Shelikhov" title="Grigory Shelikhov">Grigory Shelikhov</a> founded the first permanent Russian settlement in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak Island</a>. In 1789 Izmaylov became the first to explore and map the <a href="/wiki/Kenai_Peninsula" title="Kenai Peninsula">Kenai Peninsula</a>. Later he helped <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Andreyevich_Baranov" title="Alexander Andreyevich Baranov">Alexander Andreyevich Baranov</a> to fight off the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tlingit_people" title="Tlingit people">Tlingit</a> natives and saved the lost crew of a Russian ship from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Paul_Island,_Alaska" title="Saint Paul Island, Alaska">Saint Paul Island, Alaska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png"><img alt="Aleutian Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1441" data-file-width="2610" decoding="async" height="66" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png/120px-Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png/180px-Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png/240px-Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_Hipsometryczna-Aleuty_i_R%C3%B3w_Aleucki.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a href="#N">N</a></li>\n<li><a href="#O">O</a></li>\n<li><a href="#P">P</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Q">Q</a></li>\n<li><a href="#R">R</a></li>\n<li><a href="#S">S</a></li>\n<li><a </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffe8d5;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yunker_vv.jpg"><img alt="Junker" data-file-height="431" data-file-width="294" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Yunker_vv.jpg/100px-Yunker_vv.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Yunker_vv.jpg/150px-Yunker_vv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Yunker_vv.jpg/200px-Yunker_vv.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Junker" title="Wilhelm Junker">Wilhelm Junker</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1840&#8211;1892)<br/>physician, ethnographer\n</td>\n<td>Born into the rich family of a <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> banker, Junker traveled a lot. He carried out a major exploration of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Africa" title="Eastern Africa">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Africa" title="Equatorial Africa">Equatorial Africa</a> in 1875&#8211;86, with <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a> and then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lado,_Sudan" title="Lado, Sudan">Lado</a> as bases for his expeditions. He researched <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_peoples" title="African peoples">African peoples</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Zande_people" title="Zande people">Zande people</a> from Niam-Niam, and collected plant and animal specimens. He explored the <a href="/wiki/Congo-Nile_Divide" title="Congo-Nile Divide">Congo-Nile Divide</a>, where he established the identity of the <a href="/wiki/Uele_River" title="Uele River">Uele</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi</a> rivers. The <a href="/wiki/Mahdi" title="Mahdi">Mahdist</a> uprising prevented his return to Europe through the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, and in 1884&#8211;86 he went south, traveled through <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tabora" title="Tabora">Tabora</a>, reached <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> and finally returned to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica11_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-britannica11-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png"><img alt="Congo basin" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="956" data-file-width="1150" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png/120px-CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png/180px-CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png/240px-CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CongoLualaba_watershed_topo.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> basin</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a href="#B">B</a></li>\n<li><a href="#C">C</a></li>\n<li><a href="#D">D</a></li>\n<li><a href="#E">E</a></li>\n<li><a href="#F">F</a></li>\n<li><a href="#G">G</a></li>\n<li><a href="#H">H</a></li>\n<li><a href="#I">I</a></li>\n<li><a href="#J">J</a></li>\n<li><a href="#K">K</a></li>\n<li><a href="#L">L</a></li>\n<li><a href="#M">M</a></li>\n<li><a href="#N">N</a></li>\n<li><a href="#O">O</a></li>\n<li><a href="#P">P</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Q">Q</a></li>\n<li><a href="#R">R</a></li>\n<li><a href="#S">S</a></li>\n<li><a </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg"><img alt="Kalvitsa" data-file-height="742" data-file-width="520" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg/100px-Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg/150px-Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg/200px-Otto_Kalvitsa.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Otto_Kalvitsa" title="Otto Kalvitsa">Otto Kalvitsa</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1888&#8211;1930)<br/>aviatior, polar explorer\n</td>\n<td>Finnish-born aviator who is one of the pioneers of the Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_aviation" title="Arctic aviation">Arctic aviation</a>. He explored the waters of <a href="/wiki/Matochkin_Strait" title="Matochkin Strait">Matochkin Strait</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Severny_Island" title="Severny Island">Severny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuzhny_Island" title="Yuzhny Island">Yuzhny Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> in order to survey ship routes for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeast_passage" title="Northeast passage">Northeast passage</a>. Kalvitsa also participated <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Ushakov" title="Georgy Ushakov">Georgy Ushakov</a>\'s expedition to the <a href="/wiki/Wrangel_Island" title="Wrangel Island">Wrangel Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Kalvitsa" title="Kalvitsa">Kalvitsa</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matochkin_Strait.svg"><img alt="Matochkin Strait" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="451" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Matochkin_Strait.svg/120px-Matochkin_Strait.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Matochkin_Strait.svg/180px-Matochkin_Strait.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Matochkin_Strait.svg/240px-Matochkin_Strait.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matochkin_Strait.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the <a href="/wiki/Matochkin_Strait" title="Matochkin Strait">Matochkin Strait</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov,_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg"><img alt="Khabarov monument" data-file-height="802" data-file-width="602" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov%2C_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg/100px-Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov%2C_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov%2C_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg/150px-Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov%2C_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov%2C_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg/200px-Monument_to_Yerofey_Khabarov%2C_Siberia_and_Amur_pioneer.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yerofey_Khabarov" title="Yerofey Khabarov">Yerofey Khabarov</a></b>*<br/>(1603&#8211;after 1671)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Cossack" title="Siberian Cossack">Siberian Cossack</a> leader\n</td>\n<td>A manager for the merchants <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stroganovs" title="Stroganovs">Stroganovs</a>, Khabarov went to Siberia and in 1641 founded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saltworks" title="Saltworks">saltworks</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a>. In 1649&#8211;50 he became the second Russian to explore the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amur_river" title="Amur river">Amur river</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Vassili_Poyarkov" title="Vassili Poyarkov">Vassili Poyarkov</a>). Through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olyokma" title="Olyokma">Olyokma</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tungur" title="Tungur">Tungur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shilka_River" title="Shilka River">Shilka Rivers</a> he reached Amur (<a href="/wiki/Transbaikal" title="Transbaikal">Dauria</a>), returned to <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsk</a> and then back to Amur with a larger force, where he engaged in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian-Manchu_border_conflicts" title="Russian-Manchu border conflicts">Russian-Manchu border conflicts</a>. He built winter quarters at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albazin" title="Albazin">Albazin</a>, then sailed down the Amur and found Achansk, which preceded the present-day <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">Khabarovsk</a>, defeating or evading large armies of Daurian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">Manchu</a> <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koreans" title="Koreans">Koreans</a> on his way. He charted the Amur in his <i>Draft of the Amur river</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dymytryshyn_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-dymytryshyn-61">[61]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">Khabarovsk</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amurrivermap.png"><img alt="Amur basin" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="779" data-file-width="989" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amurrivermap.png/120px-Amurrivermap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amurrivermap.png/180px-Amurrivermap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amurrivermap.png/240px-Amurrivermap.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amurrivermap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a> basin</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffdfff;">\n<th scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maria_Klenova.jpg"><img alt="Klenova" data-file-height="306" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ec/Maria_Klenova.jpg/120px-Maria_Klenova.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ec/Maria_Klenova.jpg/180px-Maria_Klenova.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ec/Maria_Klenova.jpg/240px-Maria_Klenova.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Maria_Klenova" title="Maria Klenova">Maria Klenova</a></b>&#167;<br/>(1898&#8211;1976)<br/>marine geologist\n</td>\n<td>Klenova was one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/Marine_geology" title="Marine geology">marine geology</a>. She began her career in 1925 aboard the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> research vessel <i>Persey</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a>, visiting <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spitsbergen" title="Spitsbergen">Spitsbergen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a>. In 1933 Klenova made the first complete seabed map of the Barents Sea. Her later work included the research of seabed geology in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> and the Antarctic, and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caspian_sea" title="Caspian sea">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Seas</a>. She was one of the earliest women explorers of the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barents_Sea_in_Bloom.jpg"><img alt="Barents Sea" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8996" data-file-width="8192" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Barents_Sea_in_Bloom.jpg/120px-Barents_Sea_in_Bloom.jpg" href="/wiki/File:Barents_Sea_in_Bloom.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a> as seen from space</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kolchak.jpg"><img alt="Kolchak" data-file-height="287" data-file-width="177" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/0a/Kolchak.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Kolchak" title="Aleksandr Kolchak">Aleksandr Kolchak</a></b>^<br/>(1874&#8211;1920)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_admiral" title="Russian admiral">Russian admiral</a>, hero of  the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, one of the leaders of the <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a>\n</td>\n<td>Kolchak joined the expedition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eduard_Toll" title="Eduard Toll">Eduard Toll</a> on the ship <i><a href="/wiki/Zarya_(polar_ship)" title="Zarya (polar ship)">Zarya</a></i> in 1900 as a hydrologist. He took part in two further <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> expeditions and explored the shores of <a href="/wiki/Taymyr_Peninsula" title="Taymyr Peninsula">Taymyr Peninsula</a>. He was nicknamed "Kolchak the Polar". He published a number of important works on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_ice" title="Arctic ice">Arctic ice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Kolchak_Island" title="Kolchak Island">Kolchak Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2TA.PNG"><img alt="Kolchak Island" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="701" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Kara_sea2TA.PNG/120px-Kara_sea2TA.PNG" class="image" href="/wiki/File:NNKolomeitsev.jpg"><img alt="Kolomeitsev" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="169" decoding="async" height="133" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Kolomeitsev" title="Nikolai Kolomeitsev">Nikolai Kolomeitsev</a></b>^<br/>(1867&#8211;1944)<br/>Russian admiral, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a>\n</td>\n<td>After several expeditions in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>, Kolomeitsev became a commander of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eduard_Toll" title="Eduard Toll">Eduard Toll</a>\'s ship <i><a href="/wiki/Zarya_(polar_ship)" title="Zarya (polar ship)">Zarya</a></i> during the <i>Russian Polar Expedition</i> in 1900. They aimed to explore the area north of the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a> and to find <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a>. There was a disagreement between Kolomeitsev and Toll over the treatment of the crew, and finally <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Matisen" title="Fyodor Matisen">Fyodor Matisen</a> was made captain, while Kolomeitsev was sent with <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Rastorguyev" title="Stepan Rastorguyev">Stepan Rastorguyev</a> to organize coal depots and carry the post to the mainland. They made a number of discoveries on the 800&#160;km long sledge trip over <a href="/wiki/Taymyr_Peninsula" title="Taymyr Peninsula">Taymyr Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barr_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barr-64">[64]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kolomeitsev_Islands" title="Kolomeitsev Islands">Kolomeitsev Islands</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_schooner_Zarya,_1910.jpg"><img alt="Zarya ship" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="520" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Russian_schooner_Zarya%2C_1910.jpg/120px-Russian_schooner_Zarya%2C_1910.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Russian_schooner_Zarya%2C_1910.jpg/180px-Russian_schooner_Zarya%2C_1910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Russian_schooner_Zarya%2C_1910.jpg/240px-Russian_schooner_Zarya%2C_1910.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_schooner_Zarya,_1910.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Polar ship <i><a href="/wiki/Zarya_(polar_ship)" title="Zarya (polar ship)">Zarya</a></i></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Konyukhov" title="Fyodor Konyukhov">Fyodor Konyukhov</a></b>&#167;<br/>(born 1951)<br/>yacht captain, traveler, painter, writer, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_(Moscow_Patriarchate)" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church (Moscow Patriarchate)">Orthodox</a> priest\n</td>\n<td>Konyukhov made more than 40 unique trips and climbs expressing his vision of the world in more than 3000 paintings and 9 books. He set a record for crossing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> on a single row-boat in 46 days. He also crossed 800&#160;km in a record 15 days and 22&#160;hours during a Trans-<a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> dog sleigh ride. He was the first Russian to complete the <a href="/wiki/Three_Poles_Challenge" title="Three Poles Challenge">Three Poles Challenge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Explorers_Grand_Slam" title="Explorers Grand Slam">Explorers Grand Slam</a>. He is the first and so far the only person in the world to have reached the five extreme <a href="/wiki/Geographical_pole" title="Geographical pole">Poles</a> of the planet: <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a> (3 times), <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">South Pole</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pole_of_inaccessibility" title="Pole of inaccessibility">Pole of inaccessibility</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Everest" title="Mt. Everest">Mt. Everest</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpinist" title="Alpinist">Alpinists</a> pole) and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">Cape Horn</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yachtsmen" title="Yachtsmen">Yachtsmen</a> pole). He set a record for the solo yacht circumnavigation of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> in 2008 (102 days).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div Korzhenevskiy">Nikolai Korzhenevskiy</a></b>!<br/>(1879&#8211;1958)<br/>Russian Army officer, geographer, glaciologist\n</td>\n<td>In 1903&#8211;28 Korzhenevskiy organized 11 expeditions to explore the <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir Mountains</a>. He discovered a number of glaciers and the highest peaks in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pamirs" title="Pamirs">Pamirs</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Peak_Korzhenevskaya" title="Peak Korzhenevskaya">Peak Korzhenevskaya</a> which he named after his wife Evgeniya. He discovered and named <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_Range" title="Academy of Sciences Range">Academy of Sciences Range</a> (in honor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_of_the_USSR" title="Academy of Sciences of the USSR">Academy of Sciences of the USSR</a>) and made a catalogue of all the glaciers in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, having discovered 70 of them himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:92px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peak_Korzhenevskoi_Pamir_from_Borodkina_ridge_at_sunset.jpg"><img alt="" href="/wiki/Otto_von_Kotzebue" title="Otto von Kotzebue">Otto von Kotzebue</a></b>^<br/> (1787&#8211;1846)<br/>Russian Navy captain, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>Kotzebue accompanied <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Krusenstern" title="Ivan Krusenstern">Ivan Krusenstern</a> on the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> in 1803&#8211;06. On the brig <i><a href="/wiki/Rurik" title="Rurik">Rurik</a></i> he led another Russian circumnavigation in 1815&#8211;18. He discovered the Romanzov Islands, Rurik Islands and <a href="/wiki/Tikehau" title="Tikehau">Krusenstern Islands</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a>, then moved towards <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and discovered and named <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue_Sound" title="Kotzebue Sound">Kotzebue Sound</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Krusenstern" title="Cape Krusenstern">Cape Krusenstern</a>. Returning south he discovered the <a href="/wiki/Mejit_Island" title="Mejit Island">New Year Island</a>. In 1823&#8211;26 he made another world cruise on the sloop "Enterprise" making more discoveries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica11_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-britannica11-32">[32]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue_Sound" title="Kotzebue Sound">Kotzebue Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue,_Alaska" title="Kotzebue, Alaska">Kotzebue, Alaska</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kozebuemap.jpg"><img alt="Kotzebue\'s circumnavigations" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1627" decoding="async" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Kozebuemap.jpg/180px-Kozebuemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Kozebuemap.jpg/240px-Kozebuemap.jpg 2x" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigations</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kozlov_01.jpg"><img alt="Kozlov" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="528" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kozlov_01.jpg/100px-Kozlov_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kozlov_01.jpg/150px-Kozlov_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Kozlov_01.jpg/200px-Kozlov_01.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Kozlov" title="Pyotr Kozlov">Pyotr Kozlov</a></b>!<br/>(1863&#8211;1935)<br/>Russian Army officer\n</td>\n<td>Kozlov started traveling in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Przhevalsky" title="Nikolai Przhevalsky">Nikolai Przhevalsky</a>, and after the death of his mentor he continued his work. From 1899 to 1901 he explored the upper reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">Yangtze</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mekong" title="Mekong">Mekong</a> rivers. He rivaled <a href="/wiki/Sven_Hedin" title="Sven Hedin">Sven Hedin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aurel_Stein" title="Aurel Stein">Aurel Stein</a> as the foremost researcher of <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> at the historical peak of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Game" title="Great Game">Great Game</a>. In 1907 he visited the <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulan_Bator" title="Ulan Bator">Urga</a>. In 1907&#8211;09, Kozlov explored the <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a> and discovered the remains of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Khara-Khoto" title="Khara-Khoto">Khara-Khoto</a>. He excavated the site and uncovered no less than 2,000 books in the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_language" title="Tangut language">Tangut language</a>. In 1923&#8211;26 he explored <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> and discovered an unprecedented number of <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> royal burials at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noin-Ula" title="Noin-Ula">Noin-Ula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:72px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mahasthamaprapta.jpg"><img alt="A silk painting from Khara-Khoto" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="745" data-file-width="328" decoding="async" height="159" 1.5x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Stepan_Krasheninnikov" title="Stepan Krasheninnikov">Stepan Krasheninnikov</a></b>*<br/> (1711&#8211;1755)<br/>naturalist, geographer\n</td>\n<td>Krashennikov was a classmate of <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a>. Krashennikov traveled in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> in 1733&#8211;36 and then on Kamchatka Peninsula in 1737&#8211;41, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Kamchatka_Expedition" title="Second Kamchatka Expedition">Second Kamchatka Expedition</a>. He gave the first full description of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> in his book <i>An Account of the Land of Kamchatka</i>, with detailed reports of the plants and animals of the region, and also the language and culture of the indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Itelmen" title="Itelmen">Itelmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koryaks" title="Koryaks">Koryaks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Krascheninnikovia" title="Krascheninnikovia">Krascheninnikovia</a> and other species.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Der_Berg_Kamtschatka_(aus_Krascheninnikow,_Opisanie_Zemli_Kamcatki).jpg"><img alt="Volcano drawing by Krasheninnikov" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="851" book</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Krenitsyn" title="Pyotr Krenitsyn">Pyotr Krenitsyn</a></b>^<br/>(1728&#8211;1770)<br/>Russian Navy captain\n</td>\n<td>In 1766&#8211;70 Krenitsyn led the "secret" expedition to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Pacific" title="North Pacific">North Pacific</a> together with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikhail_Levashov" title="Mikhail Levashov">Mikhail Levashov</a>, as ordered by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a>. They explored the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> and part of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> shore, discovering good haven in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unalaska" title="Unalaska">Unalaska</a> and many features of the Alaskan coast. Krenitsyn died by drowning in the <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_River" title="Kamchatka River">Kamchatka River</a>. On the basis of his explorations the first general map of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> was created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbd_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-rbd-19">[19]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Krenitzin_Islands" title="Krenitzin Islands">Krenitzin Islands</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" Islands">Aleutian Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#FFFFFF;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sergei_Konstantinovich_Krikalev.jpg"><img alt="Krikalev" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="125" href="/wiki/Sergei_Krikalyov" title="Sergei Krikalyov">Sergei Krikalyov</a></b>$<br/>(born 1958)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" title="Cosmonaut">cosmonaut</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineer" title="Mechanical engineer">mechanical engineer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">Hero of the Soviet Union</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hero_of_Russia" title="Hero of Russia">Hero of Russia</a>\n</td>\n<td>Krikalyov spent a record 803 days 9&#160;hours and 39&#160;minutes in <a href="/wiki/Space" title="Space">space</a> during his six spaceflights. As a <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> cosmonaut he traveled into space and back aboard <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-7" title="Soyuz TM-7">Soyuz TM-7</a></i> in 1988 and then launched aboard <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-12" title="Soyuz TM-12">Soyuz TM-12</a></i> in 1991, both times working on the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></i>. <i>"The last Citizen of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">USSR</a>"</i>, Krikalev landed back on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> aboard <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-13" title="Soyuz TM-13">Soyuz TM-13</a> in 1992 to turn into a Russian cosmonaut. He became the first Russian to travel on an American <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> during the <a href="/wiki/STS-60" title="STS-60">STS-60</a> mission to <i><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></i> in 1994, and then he made another Shuttle flight <a href="/wiki/STS-88" title="STS-88">STS-88</a>, which was the first Shuttle mission to the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. He again traveled to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">ISS</a> on <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-31" title="Soyuz TM-31">Soyuz TM-31</a> in 2000 and returned on <a href="/wiki/STS-102" title="STS-102">STS-102</a> in 2001. Again he traveled to ISS and back on <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-6" title="Soyuz TMA-6">Soyuz TMA-6</a> in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td station</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Kropotkin_circa_1900.jpg"><img //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Peter_Kropotkin_circa_1900.jpg/200px-Peter_Kropotkin_circa_1900.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyotr_Kropotkin" title="Pyotr Kropotkin">Pyotr Kropotkin</a></b>*<br/>(1842&#8211;1921)<br/>Russian Army officer, geographer, zoologist, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a> revolutionary\n</td>\n<td>While serving in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, in 1864 Kropotkin led a survey expedition crossing North <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transbaikalia" title="Transbaikalia">Transbaikalia</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>. Subsequently, he took part in the expedition which proceeded up the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sungari_River" title="Sungari River">Sungari River</a> into central Manchuria, yielding valuable geographic results. In 1871 he explored the glacial deposits of <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> and Sweden. He published several important works on the geography of Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Kropotkin,_Krasnodar_Krai" title="Kropotkin, Krasnodar Krai">Kropotkin, Krasnodar Krai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kropotkinskaya" title="Kropotkinskaya">Kropotkinskaya</a> (<a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a>).</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kruzenshtern_I_F.jpg"><img alt="Krusenstern" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1444" von Krusenstern">Adam Johann von Krusenstern</a></b>^<br/>(1770&#8211;1846)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_admiral" title="Russian admiral">Russian admiral</a>, circumnavigator, geographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1803&#8211;06, under the patronage of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I of Russia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Rumyantsev" title="Nikolai Rumyantsev">Nikolai Rumyantsev</a>, Krusenstern led the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> of the world aboard the <a href="/wiki/Nadezhda_(1802_Russian_ship)" title="Nadezhda (1802 Russian ship)"><i>Nadezhda</i></a> together with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuri_Lisianski" title="Yuri Lisianski">Yuri Lisianski</a> on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neva_(Russian_warship)" title="Neva (Russian warship)">Neva</a></i>. The purpose of the expedition was to establish trade with China and Japan, and examine <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> for a possible colony. They sailed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kronshtadt" title="Kronshtadt">Kronshtadt</a>, rounded <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">Cape Horn</a>, and reached the northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a>, making a number of discoveries. Krusenstern made an atlas of the Pacific, receiving an honorary membership in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Science" title="Russian Academy of Science">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> for the work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Adam_Johann_von_Krusenstern" title="Adam Johann von Krusenstern">Krusenstern Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Krusenstern" title="Cape Krusenstern">Cape Krusenstern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kruzenshtern_(ship)" title="Kruzenshtern (ship)">Kruzenshtern (ship)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krusenstern_(crater)" title="Krusenstern (crater)">Krusenstern (crater)</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image"
