title="Enlarge"></a></div>A coin dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aleksandr_kuchin.PNG"><img alt="Kuchin" data-file-height="258" data-file-width="187" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aleksandr_kuchin.PNG/100px-Aleksandr_kuchin.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Aleksandr_kuchin.PNG/150px-Aleksandr_kuchin.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/22/Aleksandr_kuchin.PNG 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Kuchin" title="Alexander Kuchin">Alexander Kuchin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1888&#8211;1913?)<br/>Russian Navy captain, oceanographer\n</td>\n<td>Kuchin\'s life was bound with Norway: he started as a seaman on a Norwegian ship, created a <i>Small Russian-Norwegian dictionary</i>, studied <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">oceanography</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bjorn_Helland-Hansen" title="Bjorn Helland-Hansen">Bjorn Helland-Hansen</a>, conducted oceanographic studies during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amundsen%27s_South_Pole_Expedition" title="Amundsen\'s South Pole Expedition">Amundsen\'s South Pole Expedition</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Fram" title="Fram">Fram</a></i>, when he became the first Russian to set foot on the land of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, and married Aslaug Poulson, a Norwegian. In 1912&#8211;13 he was the captain of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Rusanov" title="Vladimir Rusanov">Vladimir Rusanov</a>\'s expedition to <a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a> on their ship <i><a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">Hercules</a></i>. After the successful research of the coal reserves on Svalbard, without consultation with the Russian authorities they made an incredibly rash attempt to pass via the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a>, and were lost in the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a>. Relics of the <i>Herkules</i> were found near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kolosovykh_Islands" title="Kolosovykh Islands">Kolosovykh Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sv-map.png"><img alt="Svalbard" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="329" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Sv-map.png/120px-Sv-map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Sv-map.png/180px-Sv-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Sv-map.png/240px-Sv-map.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sv-map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a href="#B">B</a></li>\n<li><a href="#C">C</a></li>\n<li><a href="#D">D</a></li>\n<li><a href="#E">E</a></li>\n<li><a href="#F">F</a></li>\n<li><a href="#G">G</a></li>\n<li><a href="#H">H</a></li>\n<li><a href="#I">I</a></li>\n<li><a href="#J">J</a></li>\n<li><a href="#K">K</a></li>\n<li><a href="#L">L</a></li>\n<li><a href="#M">M</a></li>\n<li><a href="#N">N</a></li>\n<li><a href="#O">O</a></li>\n<li><a href="#P">P</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Q">Q</a></li>\n<li><a href="#R">R</a></li>\n<li><a href="#S">S</a></li>\n<li><a href="#T">T</a></li>\n<li><a href="#U">U</a></li>\n<li><a href="#V">V</a></li>\n<li><a href="#W">W</a></li>\n<li><a href="#X">X</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Y">Y</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Z">Z</a> </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffe8d5;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grigori-langsdorff.jpg"><img alt="Langsdorf" data-file-height="267" data-file-width="218" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Grigori-langsdorff.jpg/100px-Grigori-langsdorff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Grigori-langsdorff.jpg/150px-Grigori-langsdorff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Grigori-langsdorff.jpg/200px-Grigori-langsdorff.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Georg_von_Langsdorff" title="Georg von Langsdorff">Georg von Langsdorff</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1774&#8211;1852)<br/>physician, naturalist, consul general of Russia in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>\n</td>\n<td>Langsdorf participated as a naturalist and physician in the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> in 1803&#8211;05. Independently, he explored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleutians" title="Aleutians">Aleutians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sitka,_Alaska" title="Sitka, Alaska">Sitka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak Islands</a> in 1805&#8211;07. In 1813 he became <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">consul</a> general of Russia in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>. There he explored the flora, fauna and geography of the province of <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> with French naturalist <a href="/wiki/Augustin_Saint-Hilaire" title="Augustin Saint-Hilaire">Augustin Saint-Hilaire</a> in 1813&#8211;20. In 1821&#8211;22 he led an exploratory and scientific expedition from <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="S&#227;o Paulo">S&#227;o Paulo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A1" title="Par&#225;">Par&#225;</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a> via a fluvial route, accompanied by an international team of scientists. In 1826&#8211;29 he led a 6000&#160;km long expedition from <a href="/wiki/Porto_Feliz" title="Porto Feliz">Porto Feliz</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a> and back emassing huge scientific collections now deposited in <a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">Kunstkamera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg"><img alt="Minas Gerais province in Brazil" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="687" data-file-width="702" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg/120px-Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg/180px-Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg/240px-Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazil_State_MinasGerais.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a> province in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RR5111-0030R.gif"><img alt="D.Laptev on a commemorative coin" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="271" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/RR5111-0030R.gif/120px-RR5111-0030R.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/RR5111-0030R.gif/180px-RR5111-0030R.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/RR5111-0030R.gif/240px-RR5111-0030R.gif 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Laptev" title="Dmitry Laptev">Dmitry Laptev</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1701&#8211;1771)<br/>Russian admiral<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._Malygin" title="S. Malygin">Malygin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ovtsyn" title="Ovtsyn">Ovtsyn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._Chelyuskin" title="S. Chelyuskin">Chelyuskin</a>, Kh.Laptev and <b>D.Laptev</b> on a commemorative coin)</span>\n</td>\n<td>A cousin of Khariton Laptev, Dmitry Laptev led one of the parties of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> in 1739&#8211;42. He described the sea coastline from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a> to the Cape Bolshoy Baranov east of the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a>, the basin and the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Anadyr_River" title="Anadyr River">Anadyr River</a>, and the land route from the Anadyr fortress to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penzhin_Bay" title="Penzhin Bay">Penzhin Bay</a>. In 1741&#8211;42, Laptev surveyed the <a href="/wiki/Bolshoy_Anyuy_River" title="Bolshoy Anyuy River">Bolshoy Anyuy River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laptevs_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-laptevs-73">[73]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Laptev_Sea" title="Laptev Sea">Laptev Sea</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Laptev_Sea_map.png"><img alt="Laptev Sea" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="841" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Laptev_Sea_map.png/120px-Laptev_Sea_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Laptev_Sea_map.png/180px-Laptev_Sea_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Laptev_Sea_map.png/240px-Laptev_Sea_map.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Laptev_Sea_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Laptev_Sea" title="Laptev Sea">Laptev Sea</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RR5111-0030R.gif"><img alt="Kh.Laptev on a commemorative coin" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="271" decoding="async" height="120" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/RR5111-0030R.gif/240px-RR5111-0030R.gif 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Khariton_Laptev" title="Khariton Laptev">Khariton Laptev</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1700&#8211;1763)<br/>Russian Navy officer<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Stepan_Malygin" title="Stepan Malygin">Malygin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ovtsyn" title="Ovtsyn">Ovtsyn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._Chelyuskin" title="S. Chelyuskin">Chelyuskin</a>, <b>Kh.Laptev</b> and D.Laptev on a commemorative coin)</span>\n</td>\n<td>A cousin of Dmitry Laptev, Khariton Laptev led one of the parties of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> in 1739&#8211;42. Together with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semion_Chelyuskin" title="Semion Chelyuskin">Semion Chelyuskin</a>, N. Chekin, and G. Medvedev, Laptev described the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taimyr_Peninsula" title="Taimyr Peninsula">Taimyr Peninsula</a> from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Khatanga_River" title="Khatanga River">Khatanga River</a> to the mouth of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyasina" title="Pyasina">Pyasina</a> river and discovered several islands. He participated in the creation of the <i>"General Map of the <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> Coast"</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laptevs_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-laptevs-73">[73]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Laptev_Sea" title="Laptev Sea">Laptev Sea</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2TY.PNG"><img alt="Taimyr Peninsula" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="701" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Kara_sea2TY.PNG/120px-Kara_sea2TY.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Kara_sea2TY.PNG/180px-Kara_sea2TY.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Kara_sea2TY.PNG/240px-Kara_sea2TY.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2TY.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taimyr_Peninsula" title="Taimyr Peninsula">Taimyr Peninsula</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg"><img alt="A.Laxman" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="420" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg/100px-Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg/150px-Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg/200px-Adam_Kirillovich_Laksman.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Adam_Laxman" title="Adam Laxman">Adam Laxman</a></b>^<br/>(1766&#8211;1806?)<br/>Russian Army officer, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>Son of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kirill_Laxman" title="Kirill Laxman">Kirill Laxman</a>, Adam Laxman led a diplomatic mission to Japan in 1791&#8211;92, with the aim to return <a href="/wiki/Daikokuya_K%C5%8Dday%C5%AB" title="Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;">Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;</a> and another Japanese castaway in exchange for trade concessions from <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a>. He made valuable observations, but returned to Russia essentially empty-handed, though he possibly obtained the first official Japanese documents granting very limited permission to trade, to a nation other than China or the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg"><img alt="Map of Japan by Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1911" data-file-width="3730" decoding="async" height="61" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg/120px-Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg/180px-Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg/240px-Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Daikokoya_Kodayu_-_Landkarte_von_Japan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Japan by <a href="/wiki/Daikokuya_K%C5%8Dday%C5%AB" title="Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;">Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;</a> in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kirill_Laxman" title="Kirill Laxman">Kirill Laxman</a></b>*<br/>(1737&#8211;1796)<br/>clergyman, naturalist\n</td>\n<td>Kirill Laxman became a priest first in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a> and then in the <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberian</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Barnaul" title="Barnaul">Barnaul</a>. In 1764&#8211;68 he explored Siberia, reaching <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Baikal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kiakhta" title="Kiakhta">Kiakhta</a> and the border with China and researching the Siberian flora and fauna. In 1782 he founded the oldest museum in Siberia in Irkutsk, where he had settled earlier and was a business partner of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A._A._Baranov" title="A. A. Baranov">Alexander Baranov</a> (the future governor of <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a>). Laxman was engaged in attempts to establish relationships between Russia and Japan. He brought <a href="/wiki/Daikokuya_K%C5%8Dday%C5%AB" title="Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;">Daikokuya K&#333;day&#363;</a>, a Japanese castaway, to the court of empress <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-6"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center">\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B8%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B2.jpg"><img alt="Lazarev" data-file-height="888" data-file-width="660" decoding="async" height="135" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/%D0%9C%D0%B8%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B2.jpg/200px-%D0%9C%D0%B8%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B8%D0%BB_%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B2.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lazarev" title="Mikhail Lazarev">Mikhail Lazarev</a></b>&#167;<br/>(1788&#8211;1851)<br/>admiral, circumnavigator, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Navarino" title="Battle of Navarino">Battle of Navarino</a>, commander of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Russian Black Sea Fleet">Russian Black Sea Fleet</a>, tutor of admirals and war heroes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nakhimov" title="Nakhimov">Nakhimov</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V._Kornilov" title="V. Kornilov">V. Kornilov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V._Istomin" title="V. Istomin">V. Istomin</a>\n</td>\n<td>Lazarev thrice circumnavigated the globe. He led the 1813&#8211;16 <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigation</a> aboard the vessel <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suvorov" title="Suvorov">Suvorov</a></i> and discovered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suvorov_Atoll" title="Suvorov Atoll">Suvorov Atoll</a>. He commanded <i><a href="/wiki/Mirny_(sloop-of-war)" title="Mirny (sloop-of-war)">Mirny</a></i>, the second ship in the Russian circumnavigation of 1819&#8211;21 under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen" title="Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen">Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen</a> aboard <i><a href="/wiki/Vostok_(sloop-of-war)" title="Vostok (sloop-of-war)">Vostok</a></i> &#8211; this expedition was the first to discover the continent of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> on January 28, 1820 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Style" title="New Style">New Style</a>). They also discovered and named <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_Island" title="Peter I Island">Peter I Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zavodovski_Island" title="Zavodovski Island">Zavodovski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leskov_Island" title="Leskov Island">Leskov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visokoi_Island" title="Visokoi Island">Visokoi Islands</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antarctic_peninsula" title="Antarctic peninsula">Antarctic peninsula</a> mainland and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Island" title="Alexander Island">Alexander Island</a> (Alexander Coast), and made some discoveries in the tropical waters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a>. In 1822&#8211;25 Lazarev sailed around the globe for the third time on his frigate <i>Kreyser</i>.<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Lazarev_Bay" title="Lazarev Bay">Lazarev Bay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lazarev_atoll" title="Lazarev atoll">Lazarev atoll</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lazarevskoye" title="Lazarevskoye">Lazarevskoye</a> (settlement), <a href="/wiki/Novolazarevskaya_Station" title="Novolazarevskaya Station">Novolazarevskaya Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lazarev_Mountains,_Antarctica" title="Lazarev Mountains, Antarctica">Lazarev Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lazarev_Ice_Shelf" title="Lazarev Ice Shelf">Lazarev Ice Shelf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lazarev_Trough" title="Lazarev Trough">Lazarev Trough</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3660_Lazarev" title="3660 Lazarev">3660 Lazarev</a> (minor planet).</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div href="/wiki/World_cruise" title="World cruise">world cruise</a> on <i>Suvorov</i></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a Lebedev AKA <a class="extiw" href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=demidism" title="urbandict:demidism">Demidism</a>\n<p>(1996- )\n</p><p>Urban Explorer/Historian/God of Self Contentment\n</p>\n</th>\n<th>TBA\n</th>\n<th>\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#FFFFFF;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leonov_Alexei.png"><img alt="Leonov" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="331" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Leonov_Alexei.png/100px-Leonov_Alexei.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Leonov_Alexei.png/150px-Leonov_Alexei.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Leonov_Alexei.png/200px-Leonov_Alexei.png 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Leonov" title="Alexei Leonov">Alexei Leonov</a></b>$<br/>(born 1934)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" title="Cosmonaut">cosmonaut</a> and Soviet Air Force general, twice a <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">Hero of the Soviet Union</a>, painter, writer\n</td>\n<td>On March 18, 1965, connected to the spacecraft <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_2" title="Voskhod 2">Voskhod 2</a> by a 5.35&#160;meter tether, Leonov became the first person to make a spacewalk, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">extra-vehicular activity</a>. He was in open space for 12&#160;min 9 sec. At the end of the spacewalk, Leonov\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacesuit" title="Spacesuit">spacesuit</a> had inflated in the vacuum to the point where he could not reenter the airlock. He opened a valve to allow some of the suit\'s pressure to bleed off, and was barely able to get back inside the capsule, where his companion <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Belyayev" title="Pavel Belyayev">Pavel Belyayev</a> assisted him. Subsequently, Leonov made a second spaceflight on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_19" title="Soyuz 19">Soyuz 19</a>, a part of the <a href="/wiki/Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo&#8211;Soyuz Test Project">Apollo&#8211;Soyuz Test Project</a> in 1975. Thus Leonov participated in the first joint flight of the U.S. and Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_program" title="Space program">space programs</a>. He published several books and albums of paintings, some of which he created in space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: a fictional spaceship in <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke" title="Arthur C. Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a>\'s book <a href="/wiki/2010:_Odyssey_Two" title="2010: Odyssey Two">2010: Odyssey Two</a>, which was dedicated to Leonov.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center">\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikhail_Levashov" title="Mikhail Levashov">Mikhail Levashov</a></b>^<br/>(c. 1738&#8211;1774/76)<br/>Russian Navy officer\n</td>\n<td>In 1766&#8211;70 Levashov was second-in-command in the "secret" expedition to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Pacific" title="North Pacific">North Pacific</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Krenitsyn" title="Pyotr Krenitsyn">Pyotr Krenitsyn</a>, as ordered by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a>. They explored the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> and part of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> shore, discovering good haven in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unalaska" title="Unalaska">Unalaska</a> and many features of the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> coast. Levashov also explored and described the <a href="/wiki/Commander_Islands" title="Commander Islands">Commander Islands</a>. On the basis of their explorations the first general map of the Aleutian Islands was created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Commander_Islands_Map_-_Russian.png"><img alt="Kamchatka and the <a href="/wiki/Commander_Islands" title="Commander Islands">Commander Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuriy_Lisyansky_portrait_by_Vladimir_Borovikovsky.jpg"><img alt="Lisyansky" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1631" decoding="async" height="123" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yuriy_Lisyansky_portrait_by_Vladimir_Borovikovsky.jpg/200px-Yuriy_Lisyansky_portrait_by_Vladimir_Borovikovsky.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yuri_Lisyansky" title="Yuri Lisyansky">Yuri Lisyansky</a></b>^<br/>(1773&#8211;1837)<br/>Russian Navy officer, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>In 1803&#8211;06 Lisyansky, aboard the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neva_(Russian_warship)" title="Neva (Russian warship)">Neva</a></i>, together with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Krusenstern" title="Ivan Krusenstern">Ivan Krusenstern</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Nadezhda_(1802_Russian_ship)" title="Nadezhda (1802 Russian ship)"><i>Nadezhda</i></a>, led the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> of the world. The purpose of the expedition was to establish trade with China and Japan and to examine <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> for a possible colony. The ships split near <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> and Lisyanski headed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Alaska" title="Russian Alaska">Russian Alaska</a>, where the <i>Neva</i> became essential in defeating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tlingit_people" title="Tlingit people">Tlingit</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sitka" title="Battle of Sitka">Battle of Sitka</a>. Lisyansky was the first to describe the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_monk_seal" title="Hawaiian monk seal">Hawaiian monk seal</a> on the island which now bears his name. He met Krusenstern again in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, but they soon separated. Eventually, Lisyansky was the first to return to <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">Kronstadt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Lisianski_Island" title="Lisianski Island">Lisianski Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg"><img alt="Neva ship" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1267" decoding="async" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/120px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg" <a href="/wiki/Kodiak,_Alaska" title="Kodiak, Alaska">Kodiak</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Litkefp.jpeg"><img alt="Litke" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="524" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Litkefp.jpeg/120px-Litkefp.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Litkefp.jpeg/180px-Litkefp.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Litkefp.jpeg/240px-Litkefp.jpeg 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_von_L%C3%BCtke" title="Friedrich von L&#252;tke">Friedrich von L&#252;tke</a></b>^<br/>(1797&#8211;1882)<br/>Russian admiral, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>Litke took part in <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Golovnin" title="Vasily Golovnin">Vasily Golovnin</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_cruise" title="World cruise">world cruise</a> on the ship <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a></i> in 1817&#8211;19. In 1821&#8211;24, Litke explored the coastline of <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Sea</a>, and the eastern <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a>. In 1826&#8211;29, he led the circumnavigation on the ship <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_battleship_Admiral_Senyavin" title="Russian battleship Admiral Senyavin">Senyavin</a></i> and accompanied Mikhail Staniukovich on the sloop <i>Moller</i>. During this voyage they explored the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Pribilof_Islands" title="Pribilof Islands">Pribilof Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Matthew_Island" title="St. Matthew Island">St. Matthew Island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commander_Islands" title="Commander Islands">Commander Islands</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Bonin_Islands" title="Bonin Islands">Bonin Islands</a> off Japan, and the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Carolines</a>, discovering 12 new islands. Litke was a co-founder and the president of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Geographic_Society" title="Russian Geographic Society">Russian Geographic Society</a> in 1845&#8211;50 and 1857&#8211;72. He was the president of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> in 1864&#8211;82, and occupied a number of major military and state offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Lutke,_Alaska" title="Cape Lutke, Alaska">Cape Lutke, Alaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Litke_Strait" title="Litke Strait">Litke Strait</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Feodor_Litke" title="Icebreaker Feodor Litke">Icebreaker Feodor Litke</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Lutke" title="Cape Lutke">Cape Lutke</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Luzhin" title="Fyodor Luzhin">Fyodor Luzhin</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;1727)<br/>cartographer, geodesist\n</td>\n<td>In 1719&#8211;1721, together with <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Yevreinov" title="Ivan Yevreinov">Ivan Yevreinov</a>, Luzhin made the first instrumental mapping of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> and the first map of the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a> during the "secret expedition", as ordered by <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>. In 1723&#8211;24 he made surveys of different parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Siberia" title="East Siberia">East Siberia</a> near <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>. In 1725&#8211;27, Luzhin participated in the first Kamchatka Expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Luzhin_Strait" title="Luzhin Strait">Luzhin Strait</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kuril_islands.png"><img alt="Kuril Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="473" data-file-width="517" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kuril_islands.png/120px-Kuril_islands.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kuril_islands.png/180px-Kuril_islands.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Kuril_islands.png/240px-Kuril_islands.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kuril_islands.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Lyakhov" title="Ivan Lyakhov">Ivan Lyakhov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(?&#8211;c. 1800)<br/>merchant\n</td>\n<td>Lyakhov, a merchant, investigated the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a> in three expeditions on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dogsled" title="Dogsled">dogsleds</a> in 1770, 1773&#8211;74 and 1775. He hoped to find <a href="/wiki/Mammoth" title="Mammoth">mammoth</a> ivory there as he believed the islands were mainly formed by a substratum of bones and tusks of mammoths. He explored the follow-up <a href="/wiki/Lyakhovsky_Islands" title="Lyakhovsky Islands">Lyakhovsky Islands</a>, crossed the <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Strait" title="Sannikov Strait">Sannikov Strait</a> and discovered <a href="/wiki/Kotelny_Island" title="Kotelny Island">Kotelny Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Lyakhovsky_Islands" title="Lyakhovsky Islands">Lyakhovsky Islands</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Siberian_Islands_map.png"><img alt="New Siberia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1219" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/New_Siberian_Islands_map.png/120px-New_Siberian_Islands_map.png" class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Siberian_Islands_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffe8d5;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NF-40(Vladimir_Lysenko).jpg"><img alt="NF-40(Vladimir Lysenko).jpg" data-file-height="546" data-file-width="728" decoding="async" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/NF-40%28Vladimir_Lysenko%29.jpg/125px-NF-40%28Vladimir_Lysenko%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/NF-40%28Vladimir_Lysenko%29.jpg/188px-NF-40%28Vladimir_Lysenko%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/NF-40%28Vladimir_Lysenko%29.jpg/250px-NF-40%28Vladimir_Lysenko%29.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lysenko" title="Vladimir Lysenko">Vladimir Lysenko</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (born 1955)<br/>traveler, scientist, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>Dr. Vladimir Lysenko had three globe <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigations</a>: (1) in a car (1997-2002), crossed 62 countries; (2) on a bicycle, crossed 29 countries; (3) along the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>, from west to east, deviating no more than two degrees of latitude from the Equator &#8211; starting in Libreville (Gabon), Vladimir had successfully crossed (in a car, a motor boat, a yacht, a ship, a kayak, a bicycle, and by foot) <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> with finish in Libreville in 2012. He also completed project titled "From Earth\'s Bowels to Stratosphere". Vladimir rafted on rivers in 63 countries. He visited all 195 UN member and observer states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:V.Lysenko%27s_circumnavigations.jpg"><img alt="Lysenko\'s circumnavigations" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1633" data-file-width="2113" decoding="async" height="93" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigations</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="M">M</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: M">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SO_Makarov_01.jpg"><img alt="Makarov" data-file-height="479" data-file-width="338" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SO_Makarov_01.jpg/90px-SO_Makarov_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SO_Makarov_01.jpg/135px-SO_Makarov_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SO_Makarov_01.jpg/180px-SO_Makarov_01.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Stepan_Makarov" title="Stepan Makarov">Stepan Makarov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (1849&#8211;1904)<br/>Russian admiral, oceanographer, naval engineer and inventor, hero of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877&#8211;1878)">Russo-Turkish War (1877&#8211;1878)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a>, commander of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Pacific_Fleet" title="Russian Pacific Fleet">Russian Pacific Fleet</a>\n</td>\n<td>Makarov built and captained the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Torpedo_boat_tender" title="Torpedo boat tender">torpedo boat tender</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Velikiy_Knyaz_Konstantin_(ship)" title="Velikiy Knyaz Konstantin (ship)">Velikiy Knyaz Konstantin</a></i>. He was the first in the world to successfully launch torpedoes (against the <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkish</a> armed ship <i>Intibah</i> in 1877). He was one of the developers of the Russian <a href="/wiki/Flag_semaphore" title="Flag semaphore">Flag semaphore</a> system and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insubmersibility" title="Insubmersibility">insubmersibility</a> theory. Makarov directed two round-the-world oceanographic expeditions on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corvette_Vityaz" title="Corvette Vityaz">corvette Vityaz</a> in 1886&#8211;89 and in 1894&#8211;96. He built and commanded <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Yermak" title="Icebreaker Yermak">Yermak</a></i>, the world\'s first true <a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">icebreaker</a>, which was able to ride over and crash <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pack_ice" title="Pack ice">pack ice</a>. <i>Yermak</i> was tested in two <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> expeditions in 1899 and in 1901. Admiral Makarov was killed in action during the 1904&#8211;05 war with Japan after his battleship <a href="/wiki/Russian_battleship_Petropavlovsk_(1894)" title="Russian battleship Petropavlovsk (1894)"><i>Petropavlovsk</i></a> struck a <a href="/wiki/Naval_mine" title="Naval mine">naval mine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Makarov_(town)" title="Makarov (town)">Makarov (town)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Makarov_State_Maritime_Academy" title="Admiral Makarov State Maritime Academy">Admiral Makarov State Maritime Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Makarov_National_University_of_Shipbuilding" title="Admiral Makarov National University of Shipbuilding">Admiral Makarov National University of Shipbuilding</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_cruiser_Admiral_Makarov_(1906)" title="Russian cruiser Admiral Makarov (1906)">Russian cruiser Admiral Makarov (1906)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Admiral_Makarov" title="Icebreaker Admiral Makarov">Icebreaker Admiral Makarov</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yermak_icebreaker.jpg"><img alt="Icebreaker Yermak" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="861" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="81" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Yermak_icebreaker.jpg/120px-Yermak_icebreaker.jpg" Yermak</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RR5111-0030R.gif"><img alt="Malygin on a commemorative coin" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="271" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/RR5111-0030R.gif/120px-RR5111-0030R.gif" 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Stepan_Malygin" title="Stepan Malygin">Stepan Malygin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(?&#8211;1764)<br/>Russian Navy captain, navigator, cartographer<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(<b>Malygin</b>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ovtsyn" title="Ovtsyn">Ovtsyn</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._Chelyuskin" title="S. Chelyuskin">Chelyuskin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kh._Laptev" title="Kh. Laptev">Kh. Laptev</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D._Laptev" title="D. Laptev">D. Laptev</a> on a commemorative coin)</span>\n</td>\n<td>Malygin was the first to write a manual on <a href="/wiki/Navigation" title="Navigation">navigation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a> in 1733. In early 1736, he was appointed leader of the western unit of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a>. In 1736&#8211;37, two boats <i>Perviy</i> (First) and <i>Vtoroy</i> (Second) under the command of Malygin and A. Skuratov undertook a voyage from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolgiy_Island" title="Dolgiy Island">Dolgiy Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a> to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob River</a>. During this trip, Malygin for the first time described and mapped the part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Arctic" title="Russian Arctic">Russian Arctic</a> coastline between the <a href="/wiki/Pechora_River" title="Pechora River">Pechora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob Rivers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malygin_Strait" title="Malygin Strait">Malygin Strait</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Malygin_(1912)" title="Icebreaker Malygin (1912)">Icebreaker Malygin (1912)</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bely_Island.PNG"><img alt="Bely Island and Malygin Strait" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="379" width="110"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bely_Island.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bely_Island" title="Bely Island">Bely Island</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malygin_Strait" title="Malygin Strait">Malygin Strait</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A4%D1%91%D0%B4%D0%BE%D1%80_%D0%90%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD.jpg"><img alt="Matisen" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="389" decoding="async" height="121" 1.5x, 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Matisen" title="Fyodor Matisen">Fyodor Matisen</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1872&#8211;1921)<br/>Russian Navy officer, hydrographer\n</td>\n<td>Matisen replaced <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Kolomeitsev" title="Nikolai Kolomeitsev">Nikolai Kolomeitsev</a> as commander of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eduard_Toll" title="Eduard Toll">Eduard Toll</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Zarya_(polar_ship)" title="Zarya (polar ship)">Zarya</a></i> during the <i>Russian Polar Expedition</i> in 1900&#8211;03. He was the first to make a thorough geographical survey of the <a href="/wiki/Nordenski%C3%B6ld_Archipelago" title="Nordenski&#246;ld Archipelago">Nordenski&#246;ld Archipelago</a>, exploring it on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dogsled" title="Dogsled">dogsled</a> and discovering and naming 40 of its islands. Subsequently, Toll and Matisen led <i>Zarya</i> across the <a href="/wiki/Laptev_Sea" title="Laptev Sea">Laptev Sea</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a>. The ship was trapped in fast ice, and Toll and three companions went in search of the elusive <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a> on foot and kayaks, and were lost. When <i>Zarya</i> became able to set sail, Matisen made for the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a> delta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barr_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barr-64">[64]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nordenshelda2w.PNG"><img alt="Nordenski&#246;ld Archipelago" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="1742" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Nordenshelda2w.PNG/120px-Nordenshelda2w.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Nordenshelda2w.PNG/180px-Nordenshelda2w.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Nordenshelda2w.PNG/240px-Nordenshelda2w.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nordenshelda2w.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nordenski%C3%B6ld_Archipelago" title="Nordenski&#246;ld Archipelago">Nordenski&#246;ld Archipelago</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matyushkin_01.jpg"><img alt="Matyushkin" data-file-height="362" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Matyushkin_01.jpg/100px-Matyushkin_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Matyushkin_01.jpg/150px-Matyushkin_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Matyushkin_01.jpg/200px-Matyushkin_01.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Matyushkin" title="Fyodor Matyushkin">Fyodor Matyushkin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1799&#8211;1872)<br/>Russian admiral, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>Matyushkin studied in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsarskoselsky_College" title="Tsarskoselsky College">Tsarskoselsky College</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a>. He participated in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vassili_Golovnin" title="Vassili Golovnin">Vassili Golovnin</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_cruise" title="World cruise">world cruise</a> aboard the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a></i> in 1817&#8211;19. In 1820&#8211;24 he took part in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Wrangel" title="Ferdinand Wrangel">Ferdinand Wrangel</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> expedition to the <a href="/wiki/East_Siberian_Sea" title="East Siberian Sea">East Siberian Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Sea" title="Chukchi Sea">Chukchi Sea</a>. They explored and mapped the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medvyezhi_Islands" title="Medvyezhi Islands">Medvyezhi Islands</a>. Following this survey, Matyushkin on his own explored a vast <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> area east of the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a>. In 1825&#8211;27, he joined Wrangel in his world cruise aboard <i>Krotky</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbd_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-rbd-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Larix_gmelinii0.jpg"><img alt="Kolyma nature" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="479" decoding="async" height="70" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Larix_gmelinii0.jpg/100px-Larix_gmelinii0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Larix_gmelinii0.jpg/150px-Larix_gmelinii0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Larix_gmelinii0.jpg/200px-Larix_gmelinii0.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Larix_gmelinii0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kolyma" title="Kolyma">Kolyma</a> region nature</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Middendorff1.jpg"><img alt="Middendorf" data-file-height="198" data-file-width="146" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Middendorff1.jpg/100px-Middendorff1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Middendorff1.jpg 1.5x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Middendorf" title="Alexander Middendorf">Alexander Middendorf</a></b>*<br/>(1815&#8211;1894)<br/>zoologist, botanist, geographer, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippologist" title="Hippologist">hippologist</a>. agriculturalist\n</td>\n<td>In 1840 Middendorf took part in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karl_Baer" title="Karl Baer">Karl Baer</a>\'s expedition to the <a href="/wiki/Kola_Peninsula" title="Kola Peninsula">Kola Peninsula</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lapland_(region)" title="Lapland (region)">Lapland</a>. In 1843&#8211;45 he pioneered the scientific exploration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taimyr_Peninsula" title="Taimyr Peninsula">Taimyr Peninsula</a> and discovered the <a href="/wiki/Putorana_Plateau" title="Putorana Plateau">Putorana Plateau</a> on <a href="/wiki/Central_Siberian_Plateau" title="Central Siberian Plateau">Central Siberian Plateau</a>. Then he traveled along the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> and entered the lower <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a> valley. He studied the ethnography of Siberian peoples, and the climate, animals and plants of Siberia. He was a founder of <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a> science and the Vice President of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a>. He determined the southern border of the <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a> and explained the high <a href="/wiki/Sinuosity" title="Sinuosity">sinuosity</a> of the northern boundary of the <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a> zone. In 1870 he accompanied <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Alexei_Alexandrovich" title="Grand Duke Alexei Alexandrovich">Grand Duke Alexei Alexandrovich</a> to <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> and discovered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Cape,_Norway" title="North Cape, Norway">North Cape sea current</a> (a part of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Current" title="Norwegian Current">Norwegian Current</a>). In 1870 he also explored the <a href="/wiki/Baraba_steppe" title="Baraba steppe">Baraba steppe</a>, and in 1878 he travelled in <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Middendorff_Bay" title="Middendorff Bay">Middendorff Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middendorff%27s_grasshopper_warbler" title="Middendorff\'s grasshopper warbler">Middendorff\'s grasshopper warbler</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Location_Putoran_Mountains.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="696" decoding="async" height="74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Location_Putoran_Mountains.PNG/120px-Location_Putoran_Mountains.PNG" location</div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Circum-Arctic_Map_of_Permafrost_and_Ground_Ice_Conditions.png"><img alt="Permafrost in the North Hemisphere" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="766" data-file-width="683" Hemisphere</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffe8d5;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miklukho-Maklai.jpg"><img alt="Miklouho-Maclay" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="359" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Miklukho-Maklai.jpg/100px-Miklukho-Maklai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Miklukho-Maklai.jpg/150px-Miklukho-Maklai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Miklukho-Maklai.jpg/200px-Miklukho-Maklai.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Miklouho-Maclay" title="Nicholas Miklouho-Maclay">Nicholas Miklouho-Maclay</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1846&#8211;1888)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnologist" title="Ethnologist">ethnologist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthropologist" title="Anthropologist">anthropologist</a>, biologist\n</td>\n<td>Miklouho-Maclay visited north-eastern <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a> on a number of occasions starting in 1870, and for a long time he lived amongst the native <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceanian</a> tribes, studying their way of life and customs. One of the earliest followers of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, he was among the first to refute the then prevailing view that the different \'<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" title="Race (classification of human beings)">races</a>\' of mankind belonged to different species. He arrived in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> in 1878 and organised a zoological centre known as the <i>Marine Biological Station</i>, the first marine biological research institute in Australia. He married a daughter of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_New_South_Wales" title="Premier of New South Wales">Premier of New South Wales</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Robertson_(New_South_Wales_Premier)" title="John Robertson (New South Wales Premier)">John Robertson</a>, and returned to Russia. Being in poor health after the trip he died, and left his skull to the St. Petersburg Military and Medical Academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Macleay_Museum" title="Macleay Museum">Macleay Museum</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N._N._Miklukho-Maklai_Institute_of_Ethnology_and_Anthropology" title="N. N. Miklukho-Maklai Institute of Ethnology and Anthropology">N. N. Miklukho-Maklai Institute of Ethnology and Anthropology</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newguinea_topo.png"><img alt="Papua New Guinea" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1409" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="68" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Newguinea_topo.png/120px-Newguinea_topo.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Newguinea_topo.png/240px-Newguinea_topo.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newguinea_topo.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg"><img alt="Maklay among the Papuans" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="219" data-file-width="316" decoding="async" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg/120px-Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg/180px-Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg/240px-Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stamp_of_Ukraine_s111.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maklay among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papuans" title="Papuans">Papuans</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicolae_Milescu-Sp%C4%83taru_on_stamp.jpg"><img alt="Milescu" data-file-height="145" data-file-width="207" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Nicolae_Milescu-Sp%C4%83taru_on_stamp.jpg/140px-Nicolae_Milescu-Sp%C4%83taru_on_stamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cb/Nicolae_Milescu-Sp%C4%83taru_on_stamp.jpg 1.5x" width="140"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicolae_Milescu" title="Nicolae Milescu">Nicolae Milescu</a></b>*<br/>(1636&#8211;1708)<br/>writer, scientist, traveler, geographer, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>In 1671 Milescu went from <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> to Russia, where he became a diplomat. He wrote the first arithmetics textbook in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a>, <i>Arithmologion</i>. He led the Russian diplomatic mission to China in 1675&#8211;78, for the first time among Russian ambassadors travelling to <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Siberia" title="East Siberia">East Siberia</a> rather than through <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>. After his assistant Ignatiy Milovanov (sent beforehand) Milescu was the first known European to cross the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a> from the north and reach Beijing by that route. Milescu made the first detailed description of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> and all the rivers feeding the lake, and he was the first to point out Baikal\'s unfathomable depth. His travel notes also contain valuable descriptions of major Siberian rivers and the first ever <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orographic" title="Orographic">orographic</a> scheme of East Siberia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milescu_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-milescu-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg"><img alt="Milescue\'s route to China" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="459" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg/120px-Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg/180px-Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg/240px-Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spafarii_trip_stamp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Milescue and his route from <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> to China</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Minin" title="Fyodor Minin">Fyodor Minin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(c. 1709&#8211;after 1742)<br/>Russian Navy officer\n</td>\n<td>In the 1730s, Minin participated in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a>. In 1736, he joined the unit led by <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Ovtsyn" title="Dmitry Ovtsyn">Dmitry Ovtsyn</a>. In 1738 together with Dmitry Sterlegov he led the group that charted the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> coastline east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yenisei" title="Yenisei">Yenisei</a> river for some 250&#160;km. In 1738&#8211;42, Minin made several vain attempts to sail around the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taimyr_Peninsula" title="Taimyr Peninsula">Taimyr Peninsula</a>. He also mapped and described <a href="/wiki/Dikson_Island" title="Dikson Island">Dikson Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Minina_Skerries" title="Minina Skerries">Minina Skerries</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_seaMS.PNG"><img alt="Minina Skerries" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="710" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Kara_seaMS.PNG/120px-Kara_seaMS.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Kara_seaMS.PNG/180px-Kara_seaMS.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Kara_seaMS.PNG/240px-Kara_seaMS.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kara_seaMS.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the <a href="/wiki/Minina_Skerries" title="Minina Skerries">Minina Skerries</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Moskvitin" title="Ivan Moskvitin">Ivan Moskvitin</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;after 1645)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Cossack" title="Siberian Cossack">Siberian Cossack</a> leader\n</td>\n<td>Moskvitin came with ataman Dmitry Kopylov from <a href="/wiki/Tomsk" title="Tomsk">Tomsk</a> to <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsk</a> and then to a new fort on the <a href="/wiki/Aldan_River" title="Aldan River">Aldan River</a> in 1638. In 1639 Kopylov sent Moskvitin in command of 20 <a href="/wiki/Tomsk" title="Tomsk">Tomsk</a> Cossacks and 29 <a href="/wiki/Krasnoyarsk" title="Krasnoyarsk">Krasnoyarsk</a> Cossacks to look for silver ore to the east. Leading the party, Moskvitin became the first Russian to reach the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> and to discover the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a>, building a winter camp on its shore at the <a href="/wiki/Ulya_River" title="Ulya River">Ulya River</a> mouth. In 1640 the Cossacks apparently sailed south, explored the south-eastern shores of the Okhotsk Sea and probably reached the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>. On their way back they discovered the <a href="/wiki/Shantar_Islands" title="Shantar Islands">Shantar Islands</a>. Based on Moskvitin\'s account, <a href="/wiki/Kurbat_Ivanov" title="Kurbat Ivanov">Kurbat Ivanov</a> draw the first Russian map of the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a> in 1642. Moskvitin, presumably a native of <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, personally brought the news of the discovery of the eastern ocean to his native city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png"><img alt="Shantar Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="647" data-file-width="760" decoding="async" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png/120px-Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png/180px-Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png/240px-Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Okhotsk-Japan5SHA.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the <a href="/wiki/Shantar_Islands" title="Shantar Islands">Shantar Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller.jpg"><img alt="M&#252;ller" data-file-height="209" data-file-width="140" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller.jpg/90px-Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller.jpg/135px-Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Friedrich_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerhard Friedrich M&#252;ller">Gerhard Friedrich M&#252;ller</a></b>*<br/>(1705&#8211;1783)<br/>historian, ethnologist\n</td>\n<td>M&#252;ller came to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a> in 1725 and became a co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a>. In 1733&#8211;43 he participated in the Academic Squad of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> and traveled extensively through <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, studying its geography and peoples. M&#252;ller is considered to be one of the fathers of <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">ethnography</a>. He collected vernacular stories and archival documents about Russian explorers of Siberia, including <a href="/wiki/Pyanda" title="Pyanda">Pyanda</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedot_Popov" title="Fedot Popov">Fedot Popov</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a>. He was among the first to write a general account of Russian history based on extensive study of documentary sources. He put forth the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Normanist_theory" title="Normanist theory">Normanist theory</a>, a controversial accentuation of the role of Scandinavians and Germans in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">history of Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:124px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg"><img alt="Kunstkamera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1962" data-file-width="2998" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg/122px-Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg/183px-Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg/244px-Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg 2x" width="122"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Petersburg_Kunstkamera_view_from_the_front.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">Kunstkamera</a>, the first building of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png"><img alt="Muravyov-Amursky" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="492" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png/100px-Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png/150px-Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png/200px-Nikolay-Muravyov-Amursky.png 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Muravyov-Amursky" title="Nikolay Muravyov-Amursky">Nikolay Muravyov-Amursky</a></b>*<br/>(1809&#8211;1881)<br/>Russian Army general, statesman, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>In 1847 Muravyov became the governor general of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Siberia" title="Eastern Siberia">Eastern Siberia</a>. He pursued the Russian exploration and settlement of the territories north of the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>. He assisted in the organisation of <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Nevelskoy" title="Gennady Nevelskoy">Gennady Nevelskoy</a>\'s expeditions, which led to the Russian presence near Amur estuary and on <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>. In 1854 military troops sailed down the Amur, in 1855 the first settlers reached the river mouth, and in 1856 the city of <a href="/wiki/Blagoveshchensk" title="Blagoveshchensk">Blagoveshchensk</a> was founded. In 1858, Muravyov concluded the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aigun" title="Treaty of Aigun">Treaty of Aigun</a> with China, which recognised the Amur River as a border between the two countries and granted Russia easier access to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. The new territories acquired by Russia included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Priamurye" title="Priamurye">Priamurye</a> and most of the territories of modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primorsky_krai" title="Primorsky krai">Primorsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk_Krai" title="Khabarovsk Krai">Khabarovsk Krais</a>. For this achievement Muravyov was granted the title of Count Amursky. The Treaty of Aigun was confirmed and expanded the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Peking" title="Convention of Peking">Convention of Peking</a> of 1860, which granted Russia the right to the <a href="/wiki/Ussuri_krai" title="Ussuri krai">Ussuri krai</a> and the south of Primorsky Krai. To defend the new lands Muravyov created the <a href="/wiki/Amur_Cossacks" title="Amur Cossacks">Amur Cossacks</a> corps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brockhaus_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-brockhaus-91">[91]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Muravyov-Amursky_Peninsula" title="Muravyov-Amursky Peninsula">Muravyov-Amursky Peninsula</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png"><img alt="Muravyov\'s boats off Aigun" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png/120px-Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png/180px-Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png/240px-Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ravenstein-p118-Sverbeyev-View-of-Aigun-1854.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Muravyov\'s first expedition off <a href="/wiki/Aigun" title="Aigun">Aigun</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banknote_5000_rubles_(1997)_front.jpg"><img alt="Monument to Muravyov on 5000 ruble banknote" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1922" data-file-width="4408" decoding="async"
