href="/wiki/Ruble" title="Ruble">ruble</a> banknote)</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MushketovIV.jpg"><img alt="Mushketov" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="740" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/MushketovIV.jpg/110px-MushketovIV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/MushketovIV.jpg/165px-MushketovIV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/MushketovIV.jpg/220px-MushketovIV.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mushketov" title="Ivan Mushketov">Ivan Mushketov</a></b>!<br/>(1850&#8211;1902)<br/>geologist, geographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1873&#8211;79 Mushketov traveled extensively in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, discovering and cataloguing mineral deposits. He produced the first geological map of <a href="/wiki/Turkestan" title="Turkestan">Turkestan</a> (together with S. Romanovsky). Mushketov also started observations of earthquakes in <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, organized regular observation of the glaciers of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, and researched the gold mines of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urals" title="Urals">Urals</a>. He led the team that surveyed the territory for the future <a href="/wiki/Circum-Baikal_Railway" title="Circum-Baikal Railway">Circum-Baikal Railway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Central_Asia_Physical.jpg"><img alt="Central Asia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="391" data-file-width="646" decoding="async" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Central_Asia_Physical.jpg/120px-Central_Asia_Physical.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Central_Asia_Physical.jpg/180px-Central_Asia_Physical.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Central_Asia_Physical.jpg/240px-Central_Asia_Physical.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Central_Asia_Physical.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg"><img alt="Nagurski" data-file-height="1181" data-file-width="847" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg/90px-Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg/135px-Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg/180px-Nag%C3%B3rski_Jan.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Nagurski" title="Ivan Nagurski">Ivan Nagurski</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1888&#8211;1976)<br/>engineer, Russian Navy officer, pioneer of aviation, hero of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>\n</td>\n<td>Nagurski was among the first pilots of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">Russian Navy</a>. In 1914 he was tasked with the difficult mission of locating the expeditions of <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Sedov" title="Georgy Sedov">Georgy Sedov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Brusilov" title="Georgy Brusilov">Georgy Brusilov</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Rusanov" title="Vladimir Rusanov">Vladimir Rusanov</a> all lost in the Russian Arctic. He flew five missions, spending more than ten hours in the air and travelling more than a thousand kilometers over land and the <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a> reaching as far as the <a href="/wiki/76th_parallel_north" title="76th parallel north">76th parallel north</a>. He did not find the expeditions, but became the first polar aviator in history. Later he performed the first ever loop with a <a href="/wiki/Flying_boat" title="Flying boat">flying boat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nagurskoye" title="Nagurskoye">Nagurskoye</a> airfield.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg"><img alt="Nagurski\'s plane in the Arctic" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="444" data-file-width="702" decoding="async" height="76" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg/120px-1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg/180px-1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg/240px-1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1914._Nagorski_farman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nagurski\'s plane in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> off <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1989_CPA_6159.jpg"><img alt="Nevelskoy" data-file-height="1237" data-file-width="1697" decoding="async" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/1989_CPA_6159.jpg/120px-1989_CPA_6159.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/1989_CPA_6159.jpg/180px-1989_CPA_6159.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/1989_CPA_6159.jpg/240px-1989_CPA_6159.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Gennady_Nevelskoy" title="Gennady Nevelskoy">Gennady Nevelskoy</a></b>*<br/> (1813&#8211;1876)<br/>Russian admiral\n</td>\n<td>In 1848 Nevelskoy led the expedition in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>, exploring the area of <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Amur_Liman" title="Amur Liman">Amur Liman</a> (which he found possible to sail through on <a href="/wiki/Tall_ship" title="Tall ship">tall ships</a>). He proved that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatar_Strait" title="Tatar Strait">Tatar Strait</a> was not a gulf, but indeed a strait, connected to the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>\'s estuary by a narrow section later called <a href="/wiki/Nevelskoy_Strait" title="Nevelskoy Strait">Nevelskoy Strait</a>. Not knowing about the efforts of Japanese navigator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mamiya_Rinzo" title="Mamiya Rinzo">Mamiya Rinzo</a> who explored the same area earlier, Nevelskoy\'s report was taken as the first proof that Sakhalin was indeed an island. In 1850 Nevelskoy founded <a href="/wiki/Nikolayevsk-on-Amur" title="Nikolayevsk-on-Amur">Nikolayevsk-on-Amur</a>, the first Russian settlement in the lower Amur region. He also founded several military posts on <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Nevelskoy_Strait" title="Nevelskoy Strait">Nevelskoy Strait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevelsk" title="Nevelsk">Nevelsk</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:72px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strait_of_Tartary.PNG"><img alt="Nevelskoy Strait" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="712" data-file-width="340" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Strait_of_Tartary.PNG/70px-Strait_of_Tartary.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Strait_of_Tartary.PNG/105px-Strait_of_Tartary.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Strait_of_Tartary.PNG/140px-Strait_of_Tartary.PNG 2x" width="70"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strait_of_Tartary.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nevelskoy_Strait" title="Nevelskoy Strait">Nevelskoy Strait</a> is the narrowest part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatar_Strait" title="Tatar Strait">Tatar Strait</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffe8d5;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RR5110-0018R.gif"><img alt="Nikitin" data-file-height="269" data-file-width="270" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/RR5110-0018R.gif/120px-RR5110-0018R.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/RR5110-0018R.gif/180px-RR5110-0018R.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/RR5110-0018R.gif/240px-RR5110-0018R.gif 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Afanasy_Nikitin" title="Afanasy Nikitin">Afanasy Nikitin</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (?&#8211;1472)<br/>merchant, writer\n</td>\n<td>In 1466, Nikitin left his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Tver" title="Tver">Tver</a> on a commercial trip to India. He traveled down the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a>, reached <a href="/wiki/Derbent" title="Derbent">Derbent</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" title="Persian Empire">Persian Empire</a> by crossing the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, where he lived for a year. In 1469 Nikitin arrived in <a href="/wiki/Ormus" title="Ormus">Ormus</a> and then, crossing the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a>, reached the sultanate of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahmani" title="Bahmani">Bahmani</a>, where he lived for 3 years. On his way back, Nikitin visited the <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> continent (<a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trabzon" title="Trabzon">Trabzon</a> and in 1472 arrived at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feodosiya" title="Feodosiya">Feodosiya</a> by crossing the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. Thus Nikitin became one of the first <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europeans</a> to travel to and to document his visit to India. He described his trip in a narrative known as <i><a href="/wiki/A_Journey_Beyond_the_Three_Seas" title="A Journey Beyond the Three Seas">A Journey Beyond the Three Seas</a></i>, which is a valuable study of the 15th century India, its social system, government, military (Nikitin witnessed war-games featuring <a href="/wiki/War_elephant" title="War elephant">war elephants</a>), its economy, religion and lifestyles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nikitin_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-nikitin-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:97px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iran_topo_en.jpg"><img alt="Persia" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1291" data-file-width="1400" decoding="async" height="88" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Iran_topo_en.jpg/95px-Iran_topo_en.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Iran_topo_en.jpg/143px-Iran_topo_en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Iran_topo_en.jpg/190px-Iran_topo_en.jpg 2x" width="95"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iran_topo_en.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persia</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:97px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:India_Geographic_Map.jpg"><img alt="India" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1388" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/India_Geographic_Map.jpg/95px-India_Geographic_Map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/India_Geographic_Map.jpg/143px-India_Geographic_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/India_Geographic_Map.jpg/190px-India_Geographic_Map.jpg 2x" width="95"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:India_Geographic_Map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>India</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a href="#B">B</a></li>\n<li><a href="#C">C</a></li>\n<li><a href="#D">D</a></li>\n<li><a href="#E">E</a></li>\n<li><a href="#F">F</a></li>\n<li><a href="#G">G</a></li>\n<li><a href="#H">H</a></li>\n<li><a href="#I">I</a></li>\n<li><a href="#J">J</a></li>\n<li><a href="#K">K</a></li>\n<li><a href="#L">L</a></li>\n<li><a href="#M">M</a></li>\n<li><a href="#N">N</a></li>\n<li><a href="#O">O</a></li>\n<li><a href="#P">P</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Q">Q</a></li>\n<li><a href="#R">R</a></li>\n<li><a href="#S">S</a></li>\n<li><a href="#T">T</a></li>\n<li><a href="#U">U</a></li>\n<li><a href="#V">V</a></li>\n<li><a href="#W">W</a></li>\n<li><a href="#X">X</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Y">Y</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Z">Z</a> </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_A._Obruchev_(timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique).jpg"><img alt="Obruchev" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="524" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Vladimir_A._Obruchev_%28timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique%29.jpg/110px-Vladimir_A._Obruchev_%28timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Vladimir_A._Obruchev_%28timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique%29.jpg/165px-Vladimir_A._Obruchev_%28timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Vladimir_A._Obruchev_%28timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique%29.jpg/220px-Vladimir_A._Obruchev_%28timbre_sovi%C3%A9tique%29.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Obruchev" title="Vladimir Obruchev">Vladimir Obruchev</a></b>*<br/>(1863&#8211;1956)<br/>geologist, geographer, science fiction author\n</td>\n<td>Having graduated from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petersburg_Mining_Institute" title="Petersburg Mining Institute">Petersburg Mining Institute</a> in 1886, Obruchev went to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. He studied gold-mining and assisted in constructing the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Asian_Railway" title="Central Asian Railway">Central Asian Railways</a>. In Central Asia he explored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kara_Kum" title="Kara Kum">Kara Kum</a> Desert, the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a> River, and the old riverbeds of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uzbois" title="Uzbois">Uzbois</a>. In 1892&#8211;94 Obruchev took part in <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Potanin" title="Grigory Potanin">Grigory Potanin</a>\'s expedition to <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">North China</a>. He explored the <a href="/wiki/Transbaikal" title="Transbaikal">Transbaikal</a> area, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dzhungaria" title="Dzhungaria">Dzhungaria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Altai_Mountains" title="Altai Mountains">Altai Mountains</a>. Having spent half a century in exploring Siberia and Inner Asia, Obruchev summarized his findings in the extensive work <i>The Geology of Siberia</i>. He studied the origins of <a href="/wiki/Loess" title="Loess">loess</a>, the ice formation and <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">tectonics</a> of Siberia. All together, he authored over a thousand scientific works. Obruchev is also known as the author of two popular science fiction novels, <i><a href="/wiki/Hollow_Earth" title="Hollow Earth">Plutonia</a></i> (1915) and <i><a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a></i> (1924). These stories, imitating the pattern of <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a>\'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Lost_World_(Arthur_Conan_Doyle)" title="The Lost World (Arthur Conan Doyle)">The Lost World</a></i>, depict in vivid detail the discovery of an isolated world of prehistoric animals in hitherto unexplored large islands in the Arctic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Obruchev_Hills" title="Obruchev Hills">Obruchev Hills</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obruchev_crater" title="Obruchev crater">Obruchev crater</a> (Moon), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3128_Obruchev" title="3128 Obruchev">3128 Obruchev</a> (asteroid), <a href="/wiki/Obruchevsky_District" title="Obruchevsky District">Obruchevsky District</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:107px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siberian_craton_location.jpg"><img alt="Siberian craton" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Siberian_craton_location.jpg/105px-Siberian_craton_location.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Siberian_craton_location.jpg/158px-Siberian_craton_location.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Siberian_craton_location.jpg/210px-Siberian_craton_location.jpg 2x" width="105"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siberian_craton_location.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Siberia_(continent)" title="Siberia (continent)">Siberian craton</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Ovtsyn.jpg"><img alt="Ovtsyn" data-file-height="210" data-file-width="170" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Dmitry_Ovtsyn.jpg/100px-Dmitry_Ovtsyn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Dmitry_Ovtsyn.jpg/150px-Dmitry_Ovtsyn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/61/Dmitry_Ovtsyn.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Ovtsyn" title="Dmitry Ovtsyn">Dmitry Ovtsyn</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(?&#8211;after 1757)<br/>Russian Navy officer, hydrographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1737&#8211;38 Ovtsyn led one of the units of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> that charted the coastline of the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a> east of the <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob River</a>, making the first hydrographic description of the large <a href="/wiki/Gydan_Peninsula" title="Gydan Peninsula">Gydan Peninsula</a> and part of the <a href="/wiki/Taymyr_Peninsula" title="Taymyr Peninsula">Taymyr Peninsula</a>. In 1741&#8211;42 Ovtsyn took part in <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a>\'s voyage to the shores of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_seaGY.PNG"><img alt="Gydan Peninsula" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="710" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Kara_seaGY.PNG/120px-Kara_seaGY.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Kara_seaGY.PNG/180px-Kara_seaGY.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Kara_seaGY.PNG/240px-Kara_seaGY.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kara_seaGY.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gydan_Peninsula" title="Gydan Peninsula">Gydan Peninsula</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="P">P</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: P">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a href="#B">B</a></li>\n<li><a href="#C">C</a></li>\n<li><a href="#D">D</a></li>\n<li><a href="#E">E</a></li>\n<li><a href="#F">F</a></li>\n<li><a href="#G">G</a></li>\n<li><a href="#H">H</a></li>\n<li><a href="#I">I</a></li>\n<li><a href="#J">J</a></li>\n<li><a href="#K">K</a></li>\n<li><a href="#L">L</a></li>\n<li><a href="#M">M</a></li>\n<li><a href="#N">N</a></li>\n<li><a href="#O">O</a></li>\n<li><a href="#P">P</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Q">Q</a></li>\n<li><a href="#R">R</a></li>\n<li><a href="#S">S</a></li>\n<li><a </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg"><img alt="Pakhtusov" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="2660" decoding="async" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg/120px-Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg/180px-Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg/240px-Pahtusov_kronstadt.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Pakhtusov" title="Pyotr Pakhtusov">Pyotr Pakhtusov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1800&#8211;1835)<br/>Russian Navy officer, hydrographer<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(a monument in <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">Kronstadt</a>)</span>\n</td>\n<td>A participant of the earlier explorations by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fyodor_Litke" title="Fyodor Litke">Fyodor Litke</a>, Pakhtusov led two expeditions to <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> in 1832 and 1835. He twice wintered on the islands and took detailed meteorological observations. Together with fellow explorer and cartographer <a href="/wiki/Avgust_Tsivolko" title="Avgust Tsivolko">Avgust Tsivolko</a>, Pakhtusov made the first reliable maps of Novaya Zemlya\'s southern shores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG"><img alt="Novaya Zemlya" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="710" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG/120px-Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG/180px-Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG/240px-Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pechora_sea4NZ.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#fff8e7;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png"><img alt="Pallas" data-file-height="615" data-file-width="510" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png/105px-Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png/158px-Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png/210px-Pallas_Peter_Simon_1741-1811.png 2x" width="105"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Peter_Simon_Pallas" title="Peter Simon Pallas">Peter Simon Pallas</a></b>~<br/>(1741&#8211;1811)<br/>naturalist, zoologist, botanist, geographer\n</td>\n<td>Born in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, Pallas was invited by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> to become a professor at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Petersburg_Academy_of_Sciences" title="St Petersburg Academy of Sciences">St Petersburg Academy of Sciences</a>. In 1768&#8211;74, he led an academic expedition to the <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">Central Russia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Povolzhye" title="Povolzhye">Povolzhye</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urals" title="Urals">Urals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, reaching as far east as <a href="/wiki/Transbaikal" title="Transbaikal">Transbaikal</a>. Pallas sent regular reports to St. Petersburg covering the topics of geology, native peoples, new plants and animals. He became a favourite of Catherine II and was provided with the specimens collected by other naturalists to compile the <i>Flora Rossica</i> (publ. 1784&#8211;1815) and <i>Zoographica Rosso-Asiatica</i> (1811&#8211;31). He also published an account of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Anton_G%C3%BCldenst%C3%A4dt" title="Johann Anton G&#252;ldenst&#228;dt">Johann Anton G&#252;ldenst&#228;dt</a>\'s travels in the Caucasus and the journals of <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Steller" title="Georg Wilhelm Steller">Georg Wilhelm Steller</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>. In 1793&#8211;94 Pallas led an expedition to southern Russia, visiting the <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper" title="Dnieper">Dnieper</a>. He discovered and described a large number of new species and amassed a vast natural history collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Pallasite" title="Pallasite">pallasite</a> (meteorite type), <a href="/wiki/Pallasovka_(town)" title="Pallasovka (town)">Pallasovka (town)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/21087_Petsimpallas" title="21087 Petsimpallas">21087 Petsimpallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pallas%27s_cat" title="Pallas\'s cat">Pallas\'s cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pallas%27s_squirrel" title="Pallas\'s squirrel">Pallas\'s squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pallas%27s_gull" title="Pallas\'s gull">Pallas\'s gull</a> and other species.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg"><img alt="Krasnojarsk meteorite" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="274" data-file-width="367" decoding="async" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg/120px-Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg/180px-Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg/240px-Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Krasnojarsk_meteorite_old.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Krasnojarsk_(meteorite)" title="Krasnojarsk (meteorite)">Krasnojarsk</a></i>, the first known <a href="/wiki/Pallasite" title="Pallasite">pallasite</a> meteorite</div></div></div></div> <div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pallas_cat.JPG"><img alt="Pallas\'s cat" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Pallas_cat.JPG/120px-Pallas_cat.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Pallas_cat.JPG/180px-Pallas_cat.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Pallas_cat.JPG/240px-Pallas_cat.JPG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pallas_cat.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pallas%27s_cat" title="Pallas\'s cat">Pallas\'s cat</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Papanin" title="Ivan Papanin">Ivan Papanin</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (1894&#8211;1986)<br/>Soviet admiral, scientist, twice a <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">Hero of the Soviet Union</a>\n</td>\n<td>In 1931 Papanin took part in the expedition on <a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">icebreaker</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Malygin_(1912)" title="Icebreaker Malygin (1912)">Malygin</a></i> to <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a>, where in 1932&#8211;33 he was the chief of a polar expedition on the <a href="/wiki/Hooker_Island" title="Hooker Island">Hooker Island</a>. In 1934&#8211;35 he was the head of a polar station on <a href="/wiki/Cape_Chelyuskin" title="Cape Chelyuskin">Cape Chelyuskin</a>. In 1937&#8211;38 he was the head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manned_drifting_ice_station" title="Manned drifting ice station">manned drifting ice station</a> <a href="/wiki/North_Pole-1" title="North Pole-1">North Pole-1</a>, the world\'s first expedition of its kind. Together with <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Krenkel" title="Ernst Krenkel">Ernst Krenkel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Konstantinovich_Fyodorov" title="Yevgeny Konstantinovich Fyodorov">Yevgeny Fyodorov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Shirshov" title="Pyotr Shirshov">Pyotr Shirshov</a> he landed on the Arctic drifting ice-floes in an airplane flown by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Vodopyanov" title="Mikhail Vodopyanov">Mikhail Vodopyanov</a>. For 234 days the team carried out a wide range of scientific observations in the near-polar zone, until taken back. In 1939&#8211;46 Papanin became the head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glavsevmorput" title="Glavsevmorput">Glavsevmorput</a>, an establishment that oversaw operations on the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a>. In 1940 he organized the expedition that rescued the ice-trapped <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sedov" title="Icebreaker Sedov">icebreaker Sedov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Papanin_with_flag.jpg"><img alt="Papanin on North Pole-1" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="787" data-file-width="498" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Papanin_with_flag.jpg/100px-Papanin_with_flag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Papanin_with_flag.jpg/150px-Papanin_with_flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Papanin_with_flag.jpg/200px-Papanin_with_flag.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Papanin_with_flag.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Papanin on <a href="/wiki/North_Pole-1" title="North Pole-1">North Pole-1</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Maksim_Perfilyev" title="Maksim Perfilyev">Maksim Perfilyev</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;after 1638)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Cossack" title="Siberian Cossack">Siberian Cossack</a> leader\n</td>\n<td>In 1618&#8211;19 Perfilyev became a co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Yeniseysk" title="Yeniseysk">Yeniseysky</a> ostrog, the first Russian fortress on the central <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yenisey_River" title="Yenisey River">Yenisey River</a> and a major standpoint for further expeditions eastward. In 1618&#8211;27 Perfilyev made several journeys on the <a href="/wiki/Angara_River" title="Angara River">Angara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilim_River" title="Ilim River">Ilim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitim_River" title="Vitim River">Vitim</a> rivers, and built several new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ostrogs" title="Ostrogs">ostrogs</a>. In 1631 he founded <a href="/wiki/Bratsk" title="Bratsk">Bratsky</a> ostrog (follow-up Bratsk). In 1638 he became the first Russian to set foot in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transbaikalia" title="Transbaikalia">Transbaikalia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yeniseirivermap.png"><img alt="Yenisey basin" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="988" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Yeniseirivermap.png/120px-Yeniseirivermap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Yeniseirivermap.png/180px-Yeniseirivermap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Yeniseirivermap.png/240px-Yeniseirivermap.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yeniseirivermap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yenisey" title="Yenisey">Yenisey</a> basin</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yakov_Permyakov" title="Yakov Permyakov">Yakov Permyakov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (?&#8211;1712)<br/>Siberian Cossack, seafarer, merchant\n</td>\n<td>In 1710, while sailing from the Lena River to the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a>, Permyakov discovered the <a href="/wiki/Medvezhyi_Islands" title="Medvezhyi Islands">Medvezhyi Islands</a>, siting them from afar. In 1712, Permyakov and his companion <a href="/wiki/Merkury_Vagin" title="Merkury Vagin">Merkury Vagin</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Yana_Bay" title="Yana Bay">Yana Bay</a> from the mouth of the Yana over the ice and explored <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshoy_Lyakhovsky" title="Bolshoy Lyakhovsky">Bolshoy Lyakhovsky</a> island, the southernmost of the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a>, thus initiating the exploration of the archipelago. On their way back Permyakov and Vagin were murdered by mutineering expedition members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medvezhy.PNG"><img alt="Medvyezhi Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="499" data-file-width="719" decoding="async" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Medvezhy.PNG/120px-Medvezhy.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Medvezhy.PNG/180px-Medvezhy.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Medvezhy.PNG/240px-Medvezhy.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medvezhy.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medvyezhi_Islands" title="Medvyezhi Islands">Medvyezhi Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Petlin" title="Ivan Petlin">Ivan Petlin</a></b>!<br/> (?&#8211;after 1619)<br/>Siberian Cossack, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>Petlin was the first Russian to reach China on an official diplomatic mission in 1618&#8211;19. His expedition may have been the second European expedition to reach China from the west by an overland route (after that of <a href="/wiki/Bento_de_G%C3%B3is" title="Bento de G&#243;is">Bento de G&#243;is</a>) since the fall of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuan_Dynasty" title="Yuan Dynasty">Yuan Dynasty</a>. Together with Andrey Mundov and 10 other men, Petlin went south up the <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob River</a>, crossed the <a href="/wiki/Abakan_Range" title="Abakan Range">Abakan Range</a>, went south to <a href="/wiki/Tuva" title="Tuva">Tuva</a> and rounding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uvs_Nuur" title="Uvs Nuur">Uvs Nuur</a> reached the court of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Altan_Khan_of_the_Khotgoid" title="Altan Khan of the Khotgoid">Altan Khan of the Khotgoid</a>. Then they passed through Mongolia to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peking" title="Peking">Peking</a>. He was not allowed to see the <a href="/wiki/Wanli_Emperor" title="Wanli Emperor">Wanli Emperor</a> because of not bringing proper tribute. He brought back a letter in Chinese inviting Russians to open trade, but no one in Russia was able to read it until 1675. An account of Petlin\'s expedition was translated into English and published in <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Purchas" title="Samuel Purchas">Samuel Purchas</a>\'s <i>Pilgrims</i> in 1625, and then translated into other European languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petlin_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-petlin-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dymytryshyn_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-dymytryshyn-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russia_China_Locator.png"><img alt="Russia and China on a world map" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="56" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Russia_China_Locator.png/120px-Russia_China_Locator.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Russia_China_Locator.png/180px-Russia_China_Locator.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Russia_China_Locator.png/240px-Russia_China_Locator.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russia_China_Locator.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Petlin\'s expedition established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russia-China_relations" title="Russia-China relations">Russia-China relations</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#FFFFFF;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Valeri_Polyakov" title="Valeri Polyakov">Valeri Polyakov</a></b>$<br/>(born 1942)<br/>cosmonaut and physician, Hero of the Soviet Union, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hero_of_Russia" title="Hero of Russia">Hero of Russia</a>\n</td>\n<td>Polyakov holds the world record for the longest continuous spaceflight in history, 437 days 18&#160;hours (more than 14 months), which he spent aboard <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-18" title="Soyuz TM-18">Soyuz TM-18</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-20" title="Soyuz TM-20">Soyuz TM-20</a></i> in 1994&#8211;95. With his earlier expedition to <i>Mir</i> on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-6" title="Soyuz TM-6">Soyuz TM-6</a></i> and back on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-7" title="Soyuz TM-7">Soyuz TM-7</a></i> in 1988&#8211;89, his combined space experience is more than 22 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg"><img alt="Mir space station with Soyuz TM-20" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="412" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg/120px-Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg/180px-Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg/240px-Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mir_as_seen_from_Discovery_during_STS-63.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">SS</a> with <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-20" title="Soyuz TM-20">Soyuz TM-20</a> at the top</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RR5217-0027R.gif"><img alt="Popov" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="250" decoding="async" 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedot_Popov" title="Fedot Popov">Fedot Popov</a></b>^<br/>(?&#8211;1648/54)<br/>merchant\n</td>\n<td>An agent of <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> merchant Alexey Usov, Fedot Popov came to <a href="/wiki/Srednekolymsk" title="Srednekolymsk">Srednekolymsk</a> in Siberia in 1645. There he organized an expedition eastward, and brought in <a href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnev" title="Semyon Dezhnev">Semyon Dezhnev</a>. In 1648 they sailed down to the Arctic and became the first to pass through the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a> and to discover <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukchi Peninsula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a>. All their <a href="/wiki/Koch_(boat)" title="Koch (boat)">kochi</a> and most of their men (including Popov himself) were lost in storms and clashes with the natives. A small group led by Dezhnyov reached the <a href="/wiki/Anadyr_River" title="Anadyr River">Anadyr River</a>. In 1653&#8211;54, while fighting with <a href="/wiki/Koryaks" title="Koryaks">Koryaks</a> near <a href="/wiki/Anadyrsk" title="Anadyrsk">Anadyrsk</a>, Dezhnyov captured Popov\'s <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakut</a> wife, who confirmed him dead. When <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Atlasov" title="Vladimir Atlasov">Vladimir Atlasov</a> came to conquer Kamchatka in 1697, he heard from the locals about a certain <i>Fedotov</i>, who had lived with his men near <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_River" title="Kamchatka River">Kamchatka River</a> and had married local women &#8211; so the <i>Fedotov legend</i> appeared. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G._F._M%C3%BCller" title="G. F. M&#252;ller">G. F. M&#252;ller</a> thought Fedotov was Fedot\'s son, while <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Krasheninnikov" title="Stepan Krasheninnikov">Stepan Krasheninnikov</a> thought he was Fedot himself, thus deeming Popov to be the possible discoverer of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfisher_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-rfisher-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kitchen-21-Russia-Chukotka-2823.jpg"><img alt="Route of Popov and Dezhnyov on the 1773 map" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kitchen-21-Russia-Chukotka-2823.jpg/180px-Kitchen-21-Russia-Chukotka-2823.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kitchen-21-Russia-Chukotka-2823.jpg/240px-Kitchen-21-Russia-Chukotka-2823.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kitchen-21-Russia-Chukotka-2823.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1773 map of <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukchi Peninsula</a>, showing the 1648 route of Popov and Dezhnyov</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Posyet.jpg"><img alt="Posyet" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="275" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Posyet.jpg/105px-Posyet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Posyet.jpg/158px-Posyet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Posyet.jpg/210px-Posyet.jpg 2x" width="105"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Posyet" title="Konstantin Posyet">Konstantin Posyet</a></b>^<br/>(1819&#8211;1899)<br/>Russian admiral, military writer, statesman, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>In 1852&#8211;54, Posyet journeyed on the frigate <i>Pallada</i> to Japan under the command of admirals <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yevfimy_Putyatin" title="Yevfimy Putyatin">Yevfimy Putyatin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Unkovsky" title="Ivan Unkovsky">Ivan Unkovsky</a>. Accompanied also by novelist <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Goncharov" title="Ivan Goncharov">Ivan Goncharov</a> and inventor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Mozhaisky" title="Alexander Mozhaisky">Alexander Mozhaisky</a>, Posyet explored and mapped the northern coastline of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>, including the follow-up <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Possiet_Bay" title="Possiet Bay">Possiet Bay</a>. In 1856 he carried to Japan the news of the ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Shimoda" title="Treaty of Shimoda">Treaty of Shimoda</a>. Possiet\'s journeys and published observations made him an expert on Japan in Russia. Having become Minister of Ways and Communications, he negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint_Petersburg_(1875)" title="Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1875)">Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1875)</a> with <a href="/wiki/Enomoto_Takeaki" title="Enomoto Takeaki">Enomoto Takeaki</a>, which brought the entire <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakhalin_Island" title="Sakhalin Island">Sakhalin Island</a> into the Russian fold. He prepared the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a> and was a leading advocate for the restoration of the white-blue-red <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Russia" title="Flag of Russia">flag of Russia</a> in 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Possiet_Bay" title="Possiet Bay">Possiet Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Posyet" title="Posyet">Posyet</a> port.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Furugelm_sat.jpg"><img alt="Possiet Bay" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Furugelm_sat.jpg/120px-Furugelm_sat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Furugelm_sat.jpg/180px-Furugelm_sat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Furugelm_sat.jpg/240px-Furugelm_sat.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Furugelm_sat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Possiet_Bay" title="Possiet Bay">Possiet Bay</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Potanin.jpg"><img alt="Potanin" data-file-height="307" data-file-width="250" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Potanin.jpg/110px-Potanin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Potanin.jpg/165px-Potanin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Potanin.jpg/220px-Potanin.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Grigory_Potanin" title="Grigory Potanin">Grigory Potanin</a></b>!<br/>(1835&#8211;1920)<br/>geographer, ethnographer, botanist\n</td>\n<td>Potanin traveled extensively through <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, studying its nature and peoples, once accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Yadrintsev" title="Nikolai Yadrintsev">Nikolai Yadrintsev</a>. In 1876 and 1879 Potanin led two expeditions into Mongolia. In 1884&#8211;86 Potanin explored Northern China and <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, returning to Russia through the <a href="/wiki/Qilian_Mountains" title="Qilian Mountains">Qilian Mountains</a> and Mongolia. He encountered the <a href="/wiki/Salar_people" title="Salar people">Salar people</a> and made other ethnographic and geographic discoveries, including the first account of the East and West <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uighur_language" title="Uighur language">Uighur languages</a>. In 1989 Potanin became one of the founders of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tomsk_University" title="Tomsk University">Tomsk University</a>, the first university in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Russia" title="Asian Russia">Asian Russia</a>. In 1892&#8211;93 he again explored Northern China and <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> accompanied by geologist <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Obruchev" title="Vladimir Obruchev">Vladimir Obruchev</a>. Before reaching Tibet, Potanin was forced to turn back because of the illness and death of his wife Alexandra, who was the first woman member of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a>. In 1899 Potanin travelled to <a href="/wiki/Greater_Khingan" title="Greater Khingan">Greater Khingan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Potanin_Glacier" title="Potanin Glacier">Potanin Glacier</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9915_Potanin" title="9915 Potanin">9915 Potanin</a> (asteroid).</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png"><img alt="Tibetan Plateau" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1012" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="81" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png/120px-Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png/180px-Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png/240px-Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tibet_Karte_Topograpisch.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Plateau" title="Tibetan Plateau">Tibetan Plateau</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RR5216-0032R.gif"><img alt="Poyarkov" data-file-height="267" data-file-width="267" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/RR5216-0032R.gif/120px-RR5216-0032R.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/RR5216-0032R.gif/180px-RR5216-0032R.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/RR5216-0032R.gif/240px-RR5216-0032R.gif 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vassili_Poyarkov" title="Vassili Poyarkov">Vassili Poyarkov</a></b>*<br/> (?&#8211;after 1668) <br/>Siberian Cossack ataman\n</td>\n<td>In 1643, Poyarkov was sent with 133 men from <a href="/wiki/Yakutsk" title="Yakutsk">Yakutsk</a> to explore the new lands south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanovoy_Ridge" title="Stanovoy Ridge">Stanovoy Ridge</a>. He reached the upper <a href="/wiki/Zeya_River" title="Zeya River">Zeya River</a> in the country of the <a href="/wiki/Daur_people" title="Daur people">Daur people</a>, who were paying tribute to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">Manchu</a> Chinese. After wintering, in 1644 Poyarkov pushed down the Zeya and became  the first Russian to reach the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>. He descended to the <a href="/wiki/Nivkh_people" title="Nivkh people">Nivkh people</a> country and discovered the mouth of the Amur River from land. Since his Cossacks provoked the enmity of the locals they passed, Poyarkov chose a different way back. They built boats and in 1645 sailed along the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> coast to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulia_River" title="Ulia River">Ulia River</a> and spent the next winter in the huts that had been built by explorer <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Moskvitin" title="Ivan Moskvitin">Ivan Moskvitin</a> six years earlier. In 1646 they returned to Yakutsk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amurrivermap.png"><img alt="Amur basin" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="779" data-file-width="989" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amurrivermap.png/120px-Amurrivermap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amurrivermap.png/180px-Amurrivermap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amurrivermap.png/240px-Amurrivermap.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amurrivermap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a> basin</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Gavriil_Pribylov" title="Gavriil Pribylov">Gavriil Pribylov</a></b>^<br/>(?&#8211;1796)<br/>navigator\n</td>\n<td>Pribylov, commanding the ship <i>St. George</i>, led an expedition funded jointly by <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Shelikhov" title="Grigory Shelikhov">Grigory Shelikhov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Lebedev-Lastochkin" title="Pavel Lebedev-Lastochkin">Pavel Lebedev-Lastochkin</a> with an aim to find the lucrative breeding grounds of fur seals, long sought by Siberian merchants. He discovered <a href="/wiki/St._George_Island_(Alaska)" title="St. George Island (Alaska)">St. George Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a> in 1786, by following the sounds of barking <a href="/wiki/Northern_fur_seal" title="Northern fur seal">northern fur seals</a> and possibly hinted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleut_people" title="Aleut people">Aleut people</a>. A year later in 1787, Pribylov discovered <a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul_Island_(Alaska)" title="Saint Paul Island (Alaska)">St. Paul Island</a> to the north of St. George.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Pribilof_Islands" title="Pribilof Islands">Pribilof Islands</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PribilofIslands.jpg"><img alt="Pribilof Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="565" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/PribilofIslands.jpg/110px-PribilofIslands.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/PribilofIslands.jpg/165px-PribilofIslands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/PribilofIslands.jpg/220px-PribilofIslands.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PribilofIslands.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pribilof_Islands" title="Pribilof Islands">Pribilof Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg"><img alt="Pronchishchev" data-file-height="469" data-file-width="355" decoding="async" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg/90px-Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg/135px-Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg/180px-Pronchishchev_Vasili.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vasili_Pronchishchev" title="Vasili Pronchishchev">Vasili Pronchishchev</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1702&#8211;1736)<br/>Russian Navy officer<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forensic" title="Forensic">forensic</a> facial reconstruction)</span>\n</td>\n<td>In 1735&#8211;36 Pronchishchev led one of the units of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a> that discovered and mapped more than 500&#160;miles of the Arctic shore to the west of the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a>. He took his wife <a href="/wiki/Maria_Pronchishcheva" title="Maria Pronchishcheva">Maria Pronchishcheva</a> with him aboard the sloop <i>Yakutsk</i>. Despite the difficulties, they reached <a href="/wiki/Taymyr_Peninsula" title="Taymyr Peninsula">Taymyr Peninsula</a> in 1736, having discovered the follow-up <a href="/wiki/Faddey_Islands" title="Faddey Islands">Faddey Islands</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Komsomolskoy_Pravdy_Islands" title="Komsomolskoy Pravdy Islands">Komsomolskoy Pravdy Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Islands" title="Saint Peter Islands">Saint Peter Islands</a>, and the east <a href="/wiki/Byrranga_Mountains" title="Byrranga Mountains">Byrranga Mountains</a> on Taymyr. Pronchishchev and his wife died from illness on the way back and were buried at the mouth of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olenek_River" title="Olenek River">Olenek River</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pronchiscev-chelyuskin_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-pronchiscev-chelyuskin-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2KP.PNG"><img alt="Komsomolskaya Pravda Islands" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="701" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Kara_sea2KP.PNG/120px-Kara_sea2KP.PNG" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2KP.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the <a href="/wiki/Komsomolskaya_Pravda_Islands" title="Komsomolskaya Pravda Islands">Komsomolskaya Pravda Islands</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg"><img alt="Pronchischeva" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="324" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg/90px-Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg/135px-Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg/180px-Pronchischeva_Maria.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Maria_Pronchishcheva" title="Maria Pronchishcheva">Maria Pronchishcheva</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1710&#8211;1736)<br/>first female Arctic explorer<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(forensic facial reconstruction)</span>\n</td>\n<td>Maria Pronchishcheva (or Tatiana according to some sources) accompanied her husband <a href="/wiki/Vasili_Pronchishchev" title="Vasili Pronchishchev">Vasili Pronchishchev</a> in 1735&#8211;36, during the Great Northern Expedition, when they explored the coastline west of the mouth of the Lena River, making many discoveries. She is considered to be the first known female explorer of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>. Maria died from illness on the way back, only 14 days after the death of her husband Vasili.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pronchiscev-chelyuskin_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-pronchiscev-chelyuskin-38">[38]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Maria_Pronchishcheva_Bay" title="Maria Pronchishcheva Bay">Maria Pronchishcheva Bay</a></span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea2MP.PNG"><img alt="Maria Pronchishcheva Bay" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="701" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Kara_sea2MP.PNG/120px-Kara_sea2MP.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Kara_sea2MP.PNG/180px-Kara_sea2MP.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Kara_sea2MP.PNG/240px-Kara_sea2MP.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" Bay</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg"><img alt="Przhevalsky" data-file-height="789" data-file-width="628" decoding="async" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg/100px-Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg/150px-Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg/200px-Nikolay_Przhevalsky_photoportrait_and_signature.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Przhevalsky" title="Nikolai Przhevalsky">Nikolai Przhevalsky</a></b>!<br/> (1839&#8211;1888)<br/>Russian Army general, geographer, naturalist\n</td>\n<td>In 1867&#8211;69 Przhevalsky led an expedition to the basin of the <a href="/wiki/Ussuri_River" title="Ussuri River">Ussuri River</a>. Subsequently, he made four major journeys to largely unknown parts of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, in total covering more than 40,000&#160;km in length. In 1870&#8211;73 he crossed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gobi" title="Gobi">Gobi</a> desert to <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, explored the upper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a>, and crossed into Tibet, surveying over 18,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> and collecting some 5,000 plant species, 1,000 birds, 3,000 insects, 70 reptiles and the skins of 130 different mammals. In 1876&#8211;77, travelling through southern <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tian_Shan_range" title="Tian Shan range">Tian Shan range</a>, he visited Lake <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lop_Nor" title="Lop Nor">Lop Nor</a>. In 1879&#8211;80 he traveled via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hami_City" title="Hami City">Hami City</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qaidam" title="Qaidam">Qaidam</a> basin to Lake <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koko_Nor" title="Koko Nor">Koko Nor</a>. Passing over <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> into Tibet, he was 260&#160;km from <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a> before being turned back by Tibetan officials. In 1883&#8211;85 Przhevalsky traveled across Gobi to <a href="/wiki/Alashan,_Kyrgyzstan" title="Alashan, Kyrgyzstan">Alashan</a> and Tian Shan, then back to Koko Nor, and westwards to Lake <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul" title="Issyk Kul">Issyk Kul</a>. His journeys opened a new era for the study of the geography, fauna and flora of Central Asia. He was the first to report on the wild population of <a href="/wiki/Bactrian_camel" title="Bactrian camel">Bactrian camels</a>, to describe the <a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_gazelle" title="Przewalski\'s gazelle">Przewalski\'s gazelle</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_horse" title="Przewalski\'s horse">Przewalski\'s horse</a> (the only extant <a href="/wiki/Wild_horse" title="Wild horse">wild horse</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brockhaus_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-brockhaus-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_gazelle" title="Przewalski\'s gazelle">Przewalski\'s gazelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_horse" title="Przewalski\'s horse">Przewalski\'s horse</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Przhevalsk" title="Przhevalsk">Przhevalsk</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Przhevalskoye" title="Przhevalskoye">Przhevalskoye</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg"><img alt="Przewalski\'s horse" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1579" data-file-width="2366" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg/120px-Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg/180px-Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg/240px-Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Przewalski%27s_Horse_at_The_Wilds.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Przewalski%27s_horse" title="Przewalski\'s horse">Przewalski\'s horse</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%83_%D0%B2_%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%83_2.jpg"><img title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Putyatin.jpg"><img alt="Putyatin" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="270" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Putyatin.jpg/100px-Putyatin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Putyatin.jpg/150px-Putyatin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Putyatin.jpg/200px-Putyatin.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yevfimy_Putyatin" title="Yevfimy Putyatin">Yevfimy Putyatin</a></b>^<br/>(1803&#8211;1883)<br/>Russian admiral, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>In 1822&#8211;25 Putyatin sailed with <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lazarev" title="Mikhail Lazarev">Mikhail Lazarev</a> around the world aboard the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suvorov" title="Suvorov">Suvorov</a></i>. Later he led diplomatic missions to <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>. Together with Admiral <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Unkovsky" title="Ivan Unkovsky">Ivan Unkovsky</a> he led a scientific round-the-world expedition on the frigate <i>Pallada</i> to Japan in 1852&#8211;55. This expedition contributed many important discoveries in oceanography. One of the results achieved was the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Shimoda" title="Treaty of Shimoda">Treaty of Shimoda</a> with Japan. In 1857&#8211;58 Putyatin twice traveled to both Japan and China and explored <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great_Gulf" title="Peter the Great Gulf">Peter the Great Gulf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russky_Island" title="Russky Island">Russky Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bosphorus" title="Eastern Bosphorus">Eastern Bosphorus</a> and other features of the Russian shores of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbd_19-5"><a href="#cite_note-rbd-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png"><img alt="Peter the Great Gulf" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="677" data-file-width="775" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png/120px-Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png/180px-Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png/240px-Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bay_of_Peter_the_Great.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great_Gulf" title="Peter the Great Gulf">Peter the Great Gulf</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Demid_Pyanda" title="Demid Pyanda">Demid Pyanda</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;after 1637)<br/>Siberian Cossack ataman\n</td>\n<td>Coming from <a href="/wiki/Mangazeya" title="Mangazeya">Mangazeya</a>, Demid Pyanda was a hunter for Siberian furs. Starting his long journey from <a href="/wiki/Turukhansk" title="Turukhansk">Turukhansk</a>, in three and a half years from 1620 to 1624 Pyanda passed a total of 8000&#160;km of hitherto unknown large Siberian rivers. He explored some 2300&#160;km of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Tunguska" title="Lower Tunguska">Lower Tunguska</a> (Nizhnyaya Tunguska in the Russian language) and, having reached the upper part of Tunguska, he discovered the great Siberian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Lena" title="River Lena">river Lena</a> and explored some 2400&#160;km of its length. When doing this, he became the first Russian to reach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yakutia" title="Yakutia">Yakutia</a> and meet the <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakuts</a>. He returned up Lena until it became too rocky and shallow, and by land reached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angara" title="Angara">Angara</a>. On his way, Pyanda became the first Russian to meet the <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryats</a>. He built new boats and explored some 1400&#160;km of the Angara, finally discovering that the Angara (a Buryat name) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Tunguska" title="Upper Tunguska">Upper Tunguska</a> (Verkhnyaya Tunguska, as known by Russians) are one and the same river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siberiariverroutemap.png"><img alt="Siberian river routes" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="72" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Siberiariverroutemap.png/120px-Siberiariverroutemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Siberiariverroutemap.png/180px-Siberiariverroutemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Siberiariverroutemap.png/240px-Siberiariverroutemap.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siberiariverroutemap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_river_routes" title="Siberian river routes">Siberian river routes</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="R">R</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: R">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div style="margin:auto;white-space:nowrap;display:inline-block;">\n<ul><li><a href="#top">Top</a></li>\n<li><a href="#0&#8211;9">0&#8211;9</a></li>\n<li><a href="#A">A</a></li>\n<li><a
