</li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Semyon_Remezov" title="Semyon Remezov">Semyon Remezov</a></b>*<br/>(c. 1642&#8211;after 1720)<br/>cartographer, geographer, historian<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(a monument in the <a href="/wiki/Tobolsk_Kremlin" title="Tobolsk Kremlin">Tobolsk Kremlin</a>)</span>\n</td>\n<td>In 1683&#8211;1710 Remezov described and mapped the Tobolsk region, where he was born. He wrote the <i><a href="/wiki/Remezov_Chronicle" title="Remezov Chronicle">Remezov Chronicle</a></i>, one of the earliest historical accounts of Siberia and its exploration, a part of the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Chronicles" title="Siberian Chronicles">Siberian Chronicles</a>. In 1699&#8211;1701 he created the <i>Chart book of Siberia</i>, the first large format cartographic atlas of Siberia. In total, he made more than 200 charts and maps of eastern Russian regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IstSib005_3.jpg"><img alt="A drawing from the Remezov Chronicle" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="637" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/IstSib005_3.jpg/120px-IstSib005_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/IstSib005_3.jpg/180px-IstSib005_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/IstSib005_3.jpg/240px-IstSib005_3.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IstSib005_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_peoples" title="Siberian peoples">Siberian peoples</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Remezov_Chronicle" title="Remezov Chronicle">Remezov Chronicle</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rezanov_np.jpg"><img alt="Rezanov" data-file-height="577" data-file-width="425" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Rezanov_np.jpg/100px-Rezanov_np.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Rezanov_np.jpg/150px-Rezanov_np.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Rezanov_np.jpg/200px-Rezanov_np.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Rezanov" title="Nikolai Rezanov">Nikolai Rezanov</a></b>^<br/>(1764&#8211;1807)<br/>statesman, diplomat\n</td>\n<td>Rezanov was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Russian-American_Company" title="Russian-American Company">Russian-American Company</a> in 1799, based on the earlier <a href="/wiki/Shelikhov-Golikov_Company" title="Shelikhov-Golikov Company">Shelikhov-Golikov Company</a>. In 1803&#8211;06, he was made an ambassador to Japan by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I of Russia</a>, and co-led the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> of the world, aboard the <a href="/wiki/Nadezhda_(1802_Russian_ship)" title="Nadezhda (1802 Russian ship)"><i>Nadezhda</i></a> under the captaincy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Krusenstern" title="Ivan Krusenstern">Ivan Krusenstern</a>. Rezanov was in command as far as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>. After his embassy to Japan failed, he was made an inspector of <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian colonies in America</a>. In 1806 he managed to open trade with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_California" title="Spanish California">Spanish California</a>, conclude a treaty, and become engaged with <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_Arg%C3%BCello" title="Concepci&#243;n Arg&#252;ello">Concepci&#243;n Arg&#252;ello</a>, the daughter of the comandante of <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>. Rezanov died in Siberia, however, on a journey back to St. Petersburg while carrying the treaty to the capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Rezanov\'s love affair with <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_Arg%C3%BCello" title="Concepci&#243;n Arg&#252;ello">Concepci&#243;n Arg&#252;ello</a> inspired a ballad by the San Francisco author, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_Bret_Harte" title="Francis Bret Harte">Francis Bret Harte</a>, and a 1937 novel, <i>Rez&#225;nov and Do&#241;a Concha</i>, by another SF author, <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Atherton" title="Gertrude Atherton">Gertrude Atherton</a>, as well as a very successful 1979 Russian <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Juno_and_Avos_(opera)" title="Juno and Avos (opera)">Juno and Avos</a></i> by the composer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Rybnikov" title="Alexei Rybnikov">Alexei Rybnikov</a> and the poet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrey_Voznesensky" title="Andrey Voznesensky">Andrey Voznesensky</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trading_post_at_Old_Sitka_(1).jpg"><img alt="Russian trading post in Sitka, Alaska" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2580" data-file-width="1720" decoding="async" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Trading_post_at_Old_Sitka_%281%29.jpg/150px-Trading_post_at_Old_Sitka_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Trading_post_at_Old_Sitka_%281%29.jpg/200px-Trading_post_at_Old_Sitka_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trading_post_at_Old_Sitka_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A replica of Russian trading post in <a href="/wiki/Sitka,_Alaska" title="Sitka, Alaska">Sitka, Alaska</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg"><img alt="Rimsky-Korsakov" data-file-height="941" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg/100px-Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg/150px-Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg/200px-Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Voin_Rimsky-Korsakov" title="Voin Rimsky-Korsakov">Voin Rimsky-Korsakov</a></b>*<br/> (1822&#8211;1871)<br/>Russian Navy officer, hydroghafer and geographer\n</td>\n<td>An elder brother of <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Rimsky-Korsakov" title="Nikolai Rimsky-Korsakov">Nikolai Rimsky-Korsakov</a> (the composer and conductor), in the 1850s and 1860s Voin Rimsky-Korsakov explored the area of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ussuri_Krai" title="Ussuri Krai">Ussuri Krai</a>, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakhalin_Island" title="Sakhalin Island">Sakhalin Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Amur_Liman" title="Amur Liman">Amur Liman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Tartary" title="Strait of Tartary">Strait of Tartary</a>. Later he also surveyed the shores of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Rimsky-Korsakov_Archipelago" title="Rimsky-Korsakov Archipelago">Rimsky-Korsakov Archipelago</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png"><img alt="Rimsky-Korsakov Archipelago" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1880" data-file-width="1880" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png/100px-Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png/150px-Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png/200px-Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rimskogo-Korsakova_archipelago.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rimsky-Korsakov_Archipelago" title="Rimsky-Korsakov Archipelago">Rimsky-Korsakov Archipelago</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:N_Roerich.jpg"><img alt="Roerich" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/N_Roerich.jpg/100px-N_Roerich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/N_Roerich.jpg/150px-N_Roerich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/N_Roerich.jpg/200px-N_Roerich.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Roerich" title="Nicholas Roerich">Nicholas Roerich</a></b>!<br/> (1874&#8211;1947)<br/>painter, philosopher, archeologist, writer, public figure, traveler\n</td>\n<td>Roerich emigrated to the U. S. after the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>. By the sale of his paintings and writings, and the gains from the activity of his cultural and enlightener organizations, Roerich was able to collect the finance and lead a major expedition to Central Asia in 1924&#8211;28, in which his family, including his wife <a href="/wiki/Helena_Roerich" title="Helena Roerich">Helena Roerich</a>, participated. The expedition went through <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">Sikkim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ladakh" title="Ladakh">Ladakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, Siberia, Altai, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>, and unstudied areas of the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>. Archeological and ethnographical investigations were conducted, dozens of new mountain peaks and passes were marked on maps, rare manuscripts were found, and some of the best series of Roerich\'s paintings were created. In 1934&#8211;35 Roerich conducted an expedition in <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> and China, collecting nearly 300 species of xerophytes, herbs, manuscripts and archeological relics. Roerich was an author and initiator of an international pact for the protection of artistic and academic institutions and historical  sites (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roerich%E2%80%99s_Pact" title="Roerich&#8217;s Pact">Roerich&#8217;s Pact</a>, 1935) and  a founder of an international movement for the defence of culture. He created about 7,000 paintings and founded a number of scientific and cultural institutions in the U. S., Europe and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roerich%E2%80%99s_Pact" title="Roerich&#8217;s Pact">Roerich&#8217;s Pact</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4426_Roerich" title="4426 Roerich">4426 Roerich</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg"><img alt="Peaks and passes named after the Roerichs in the Altai" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg/120px-Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg/180px-Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg/240px-Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Altai._Peaks_and_passes_named_in_honor_of_the_family_Roerich.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Peaks and passes named after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roerichs" title="Roerichs">Roerichs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Altai_Mountains" title="Altai Mountains">Altai Mountains</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Urusvati_base.jpg"><img alt="Institute of Himalayan studies founded by the Roerichs" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="297" data-file-width="411" decoding="async" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Urusvati_base.jpg/120px-Urusvati_base.jpg" href="/wiki/File:Urusvati_base.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Institute of <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayan</a> studies "Urusvati", founded by the Roerichs</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Newski.jpg"><img alt="Alexander Nevsky" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="292" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Alexander_Newski.jpg/90px-Alexander_Newski.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Alexander_Newski.jpg/135px-Alexander_Newski.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Alexander_Newski.jpg/180px-Alexander_Newski.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky" title="Alexander Nevsky">Alexander Nevsky</a></b>! <span style="font-size:85%;">(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rurikid" title="Rurikid">Rurikid</a>)</span><br/>(1220&#8211;1263)<br/>Grand <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Novgorod" title="Prince of Novgorod">Prince of Novgorod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Vladimir</a>, national hero and <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of Russia\n</td>\n<td>Prince Alexander Yaroslavich Nevsky traveled to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolian_Empire" title="Mongolian Empire">Mongolian</a> capital <a href="/wiki/Karakorum" title="Karakorum">Karakorum</a> in Central Asia, between 1247&#8211;49, accompanied by his brother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrey_Yaroslavich" title="Andrey Yaroslavich">Andrey Yaroslavich</a>. They were summoned there by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genghisid" title="Genghisid">Genghisid</a> <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khans</a> who had conquered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rus%27_(region)" title="Rus\' (region)">Rus\'</a> a few years before. Unlike their father <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_II_of_Vladimir" title="Yaroslav II of Vladimir">Yaroslav II of Vladimir</a>, who had come into Karakorum in 1245&#8211;46 and was poisoned by the Mongols, Alexander and Andrey were able to get back to Rus\', confirmed in power by their new overlords. Russian princes were among the first known Europeans to travel so far into Asia, making their journey around the same time as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italia" title="Italia">Italian</a> monk <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plano_Carpini" title="Plano Carpini">Plano Carpini</a> traveled to Mongolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nevsky_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-nevsky-3">[3]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Alexander_Nevsky" title="Order of Alexander Nevsky">Order of Alexander Nevsky</a>, numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Cathedral_(disambiguation)" title="Alexander Nevsky Cathedral (disambiguation)">Alexander Nevsky Cathedrals</a>, churches, monasteries.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center">\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Rusanov" title="Vladimir Rusanov">Vladimir Rusanov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (1875&#8211;1913?)<br/>geologist\n</td>\n<td>In 1909&#8211;11 Rusanov carried out explorations in the <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> archipelago. In 1912 he commanded a government expedition to <a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a> to investigate its coal reserves. They sailed on the small ship <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Herkules_(motor_schooner)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Herkules (motor schooner) (page does not exist)">Herkules</a></i> under Captain <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Kuchin" title="Alexander Kuchin">Alexander Kuchin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amundsen%27s_South_Pole_expedition" title="Amundsen\'s South Pole expedition">Amundsen\'s South Pole expedition</a> navigator. Concluding the work, part of the expedition returned to Russia, while the rest, without consultation with the authorities, set off with Rusanov in an incredibly rash attempt at reaching the Pacific via the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a>, and disappeared in the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a>. The relics of the expedition were found in 1937 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kolosovykh_Islands" title="Kolosovykh Islands">Kolosovykh Islands</a>. Soviet coal mining on Svalbard began in 1932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Rusanov and his expedition are among the prototypes for the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Two_Captains" title="The Two Captains">The Two Captains</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Veniamin_Kaverin" title="Veniamin Kaverin">Veniamin Kaverin</a>, where the search proceedings for fictional captain Tatarinov resemble the search for Rusanov.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg"><img alt="Hercules ship" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="596" decoding="async" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg/120px-Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg/180px-Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg/240px-Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hercules_schooner_Rusanov.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">Hercules</a></i> schooner</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S">S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Russian_explorers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">\n<div class="toctitle" id="toctitle" style="text-align:center;display:inline-block;"><span id="tocheading" style="font-weight:bold;">Contents:&#160;</span></div>\n<div </li></ul>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n</div></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ccc;">\n<th scope="col" width="18%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="22%">Person\n</th>\n<th scope="col" width="60%">Achievements\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Image\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg"><img alt="Sagalevich" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg/120px-Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg/180px-Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg/240px-Vladimir_Putin_21_February_2008-10.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Sagalevich" title="Anatoly Sagalevich">Anatoly Sagalevich</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(born 1938)<br/>oceanographer, submersible pilot, Hero of Russia<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(right in photo with <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>)</span>\n</td>\n<td>From 1979 Sagalevich has been the head of the Deepwater Submersibles Laboratory at the <a href="/wiki/Shirshov_Institute_of_Oceanology" title="Shirshov Institute of Oceanology">Shirshov Institute of Oceanology</a>. He took part in the construction of the Pisces VIII, Pisces IX and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIR_submersible" title="MIR submersible">MIR</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_Submergence_Vehicle" title="Deep Submergence Vehicle">Deep Submergence Vehicles</a> and completed more than 300 submersions as the chief pilot of DSVs. He piloted MIRs during expeditions to <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">RMS Titanic</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_battleship_Bismarck" title="German battleship Bismarck">German battleship Bismarck</a>, Soviet and Russian submarines <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K-278_Komsomolets" title="K-278 Komsomolets">K-278 Komsomolets</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K-141_Kursk" title="K-141 Kursk">K-141 Kursk</a></i>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_submarine_I-52_(1943)" title="Japanese submarine I-52 (1943)">Japanese submarine I-52</a>. Sagalevich holds the world record for the deepest fresh water dive at 1637&#160;m in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> aboard a Pisces in 1990. On August 2, 2007, he was the pilot of the MIR-1 DSV that reached the seabed at the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Arktika_2007" title="Arktika 2007">Arktika 2007</a> expedition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1990_CPA_6263.jpg"><img alt="MIR submersible" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1295" data-file-width="2790" decoding="async" height="56" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/1990_CPA_6263.jpg/120px-1990_CPA_6263.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/1990_CPA_6263.jpg/180px-1990_CPA_6263.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/1990_CPA_6263.jpg/240px-1990_CPA_6263.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1990_CPA_6263.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIR_submersible" title="MIR submersible">MIR submersible</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rudolf_Samoylovich.jpg"><img alt="Samoylovich" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="449" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Rudolf_Samoylovich.jpg/150px-Rudolf_Samoylovich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Rudolf_Samoylovich.jpg/200px-Rudolf_Samoylovich.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Samoylovich" title="Rudolf Samoylovich">Rudolf Samoylovich</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1881&#8211;1940?)<br/>geographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1912 Samoylovich took part in <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Rusanov" title="Vladimir Rusanov">Vladimir Rusanov</a>\'s geological expedition to <a href="/wiki/Spitsbergen" title="Spitsbergen">Spitsbergen</a>. He was one of the initiators and the first director of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_and_Antarctic_Research_Institute" title="Arctic and Antarctic Research Institute">Arctic and Antarctic Research Institute</a>. In 1928 he was the head of the rescue party on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krasin_(1916_icebreaker)" title="Krasin (1916 icebreaker)"><i>Krasin</i></a> icebreaker, that saved most of the crew of the <i><a href="/wiki/Airship_Italia" title="Airship Italia">Airship Italia</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Nobile" title="Umberto Nobile">Umberto Nobile</a>. He participated in the polar flight of <a href="/wiki/LZ_127_Graf_Zeppelin" title="LZ 127 Graf Zeppelin">LZ 127 Graf Zeppelin</a> in 1931 and headed expeditions on the icebreakers <i>Vladimir Rusanov</i> (1932), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgy_Sedov_(icebreaker)" title="Georgy Sedov (icebreaker)">Georgy Sedov</a></i> (1934), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sadko" title="Icebreaker Sadko"><i>Sadko</i></a> (1936 and 1937&#8211;38).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center">\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yakov_Sannikov" title="Yakov Sannikov">Yakov Sannikov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (1780&#8211;after 1812)<br/>merchant\n</td>\n<td>Exploring the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a>, in 1800 Sannikov discovered and charted <a href="/wiki/Stolbovoy_Island" title="Stolbovoy Island">Stolbovoy Island</a>, and then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faddeyevsky_Island" title="Faddeyevsky Island">Faddeyevsky Island</a> in 1805. In 1809&#8211;1810, he took part in the expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Matvei_Gedenschtrom" title="Matvei Gedenschtrom">Matvei Gedenschtrom</a>. He discovered <a href="/wiki/Bunge_Land" title="Bunge Land">Bunge Land</a> and suggested that there was a vast land north of <a href="/wiki/Kotelny_Island" title="Kotelny Island">Kotelny Island</a>, thus introducing a theory about the existence of the legendary <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Strait" title="Sannikov Strait">Sannikov Strait</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siberia_DL.png"><img alt="De Long Islands and the deemed Sannikov Land location" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="710" decoding="async" height="69" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Siberia_DL.png/120px-Siberia_DL.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Siberia_DL.png/180px-Siberia_DL.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Siberia_DL.png/240px-Siberia_DL.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siberia_DL.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/De_Long_Islands" title="De Long Islands">De Long Islands</a>, beyond which the <a href="/wiki/Sannikov_Land" title="Sannikov Land">Sannikov Land</a> was deemed to exist</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg"><img alt="Sarychev" data-file-height="333" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b0/Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg/110px-Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b0/Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg/165px-Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b0/Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg/220px-Gavriil_Sarychev.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gavriil_Sarychev" title="Gavriil Sarychev">Gavriil Sarychev</a></b>^<br/>(1763&#8211;1831)<br/>Russian admiral, cartographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1785&#8211;94 Sarychev took part in the expedition sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> and led by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Billings" title="Joseph Billings">Joseph Billings</a>. Commanding the ship <i>Slava Rossii</i> (Glory of Russia), he mapped the coastline of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> from <a href="/wiki/Okhotsk" title="Okhotsk">Okhotsk</a> to <a href="/wiki/Aldoma" title="Aldoma">Aldoma</a> and many of the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> (especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unalaska" title="Unalaska">Unalaska</a>). He also described the <a href="/wiki/Pribilof_Islands" title="Pribilof Islands">Pribilof Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Matthew_Island" title="St. Matthew Island">St. Matthew Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_Island" title="St. Lawrence Island">St. Lawrence Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diomede_Islands" title="Diomede Islands">Gvozdev</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Island,_Alaska" title="King Island, Alaska">King Island</a>. He was in charge of hydrographic research in Russia from 1808 and led the compilation of the <i>Atlas of the Northern Part of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a></i> in 1826.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Sarychev_Peak" title="Sarychev Peak">Sarychev Peak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Sarichef_Airport" title="Cape Sarichef Airport">Cape Sarichef Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarichef_Island" title="Sarichef Island">Sarichef Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Unalaska_church.jpg"><img alt="Russian Orthodox Church in Unalaska" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="90" Savitskaya">Svetlana Savitskaya</a></b>$<br/> (born 1948)<br/>female cosmonaut, aviator, twice a Hero of the Soviet Union, politician<br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">(Savitskaya with her 1982 crew fellows <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Popov" title="Leonid Popov">Popov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Serebrov" title="Aleksandr Serebrov">Serebrov</a>)</span>\n</td>\n<td>Savitskaya was the second woman in space (after <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Tereshkova" title="Valentina Tereshkova">Valentina Tereshkova</a>) and the first woman to conduct an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">extra-vehicular activity</a>. She achieved this during the two successful expeditions to the <a href="/wiki/Salyut_7" title="Salyut 7">Salyut 7</a> space station in 1982 and 1984, making her spacewalk on July 25, 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a width="9"/><br/>(1802&#8211;1880)<br/>admiral, ship designer, explorer\n</td>\n<td>Finnish-born admiral of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Imperial_Navy" title="Russian Imperial Navy">Russian Imperial Navy</a> who circumnavigated the globe as the commander of the Imperial Navy ship <i>America</i> in 1834&#8211;1836. He rediscovered the <a href="/wiki/Wotho_Atoll" title="Wotho Atoll">Wotho Atoll</a>, originally discovered by the Spanish expedition of <a href="/wiki/Ruy_L%C3%B3pez_de_Villalobos" title="Ruy honor: Schantz Islands (now <a href="/wiki/Wotho_Atoll" title="Wotho Atoll">Wotho Atoll</a>).</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Otto_Schmidt.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="193" decoding="async" height="162" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a8/Otto_Schmidt.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Otto_Schmidt" title="Otto Schmidt">Otto Schmidt</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1891&#8211;1956)<br/>mathematician, astronomer, geophysicist, statesman, Hero of the Soviet Union\n</td>\n<td>In 1932&#8211;39 Schmidt was the head of the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Directorate_of_the_Northern_Sea_Route" title="Chief Directorate of the Northern Sea Route">Chief Directorate of the Northern Sea Route</a>. In 1929&#8211;30, travelling on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sedov" title="Icebreaker Sedov">icebreaker Sedov</a>, he established the first research station on <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a>, explored the northwestern <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a> and western <a href="/wiki/Severnaya_Zemlya" title="Severnaya Zemlya">Severnaya Zemlya</a>, discovering a few islands. In 1932 his expedition on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sibiryakov" title="Icebreaker Sibiryakov">Icebreaker Sibiryakov</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_Vladimir_Voronin" title="Captain Vladimir Voronin">Captain Vladimir Voronin</a> made the first non-stop voyage through the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a> from <a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">Arkhangelsk</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a> without wintering. In 1933&#8211;34 Schmidt and Voronin led the voyage on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steamship_Cheliuskin" title="Steamship Cheliuskin">steamship Cheliuskin</a>, that resulted in the loss of the ship and evacuation of the crew. In 1937 Schmidt supervised an airborne expedition that established the first ever <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drift-ice_station" title="Drift-ice station">drift-ice station</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/North_Pole-1" title="North Pole-1">North Pole-1</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shmidt_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-shmidt-15">[15]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2108_Otto_Schmidt" title="2108 Otto Schmidt">2108 Otto Schmidt</a> (minor planet).</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northernsearoute.PNG"><img alt="Northern Sea Route" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="534" decoding="async" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Northernsearoute.PNG/120px-Northernsearoute.PNG" href="/wiki/File:Northernsearoute.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leopold_von_Schrenck.jpg"><img alt="Schrenck" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="158" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Leopold_von_Schrenck" title="Leopold von Schrenck">Leopold von Schrenck</a></b>*<br/>(1826&#8211;1894)<br/>zoologist, geographer, ethnographer\n</td>\n<td>Schrenck explored the fauna of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amurland" title="Amurland">Amurland</a> between 1853&#8211;54, and on <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a> in 1854&#8211;55, discovering a number of animals. Later he turned to the study of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_peoples_of_Russia" title="Native peoples of Russia">native peoples of Russia</a>. He coined the term <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paleo-Asiatic" title="Paleo-Asiatic">Paleo-Asiatic</a> peoples</i> and was a director of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great_Museum_of_Anthropology_and_Ethnography" title="Peter the Great Museum of Anthropology and Ethnography">Peter the Great Museum of Anthropology and Ethnography</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Petersburg" title="St Petersburg">St Petersburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brockhaus_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-brockhaus-91">[91]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amur_sturgeon" title="Amur sturgeon">Amur sturgeon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchurian_black_water_snake" title="Manchurian black water snake">Manchurian black water snake</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schrenki.JPG"><img alt="Manchurian black water snake" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sedow_georgy.jpg"><img alt="Sedov" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="576" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sedow_georgy.jpg/100px-Sedow_georgy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sedow_georgy.jpg/150px-Sedow_georgy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sedow_georgy.jpg/200px-Sedow_georgy.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Georgy_Sedov" title="Georgy Sedov">Georgy Sedov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/> (1877&#8211;1914)<br/>Russian Navy captain\n</td>\n<td>In 1909 Sedov led the expedition that described the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a>. In 1910 he explored the Krestovaya Bay on <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a>. He suggested an expedition to the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a> and found private sponsors. In 1912 Sedov\'s ship <i>"Svyatoy Muchenik Foka" (Saint Martyr Foka)</i> sailed north but had to stay for the winter near Novaya Zemlya because of impassable ice. <i>Sv. Foka</i> reached <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a> then, but had to stop for another winter due to lack of coal. In early 1914, Sedov, sick with scurvy, set off with two companions for the North Pole with the draft dogs. Sedov died near <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Island" title="Rudolf Island">Rudolf Island</a> and was buried there, at Cape Auk. On the way back, at Franz Josef Land, the <i>Sv. Foka</i> rescued the two survivors of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brusilov_expedition" title="Brusilov expedition">Brusilov expedition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valerian_Albanov" title="Valerian Albanov">Valerian Albanov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Konrad" title="Alexander Konrad">Alexander Konrad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-7"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sedov" title="Icebreaker Sedov">Icebreaker Sedov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Sedov" title="Georgy Sedov">Sedov</a> (sailing ship). He and his last expedition are among the prototypes for the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Two_Captains" title="The Two Captains">The Two Captains</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Veniamin_Kaverin" title="Veniamin Kaverin">Veniamin Kaverin</a>, where the fictional captain Tatarinov has Sedov-like appearance and shares his passion for Arctic exploration.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1912._Sedov_Foka_Arkhangelsk.jpg"><img alt="Sedov amid the crew of St. Foka" class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1912._Sedov_Foka_Arkhangelsk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sedov amid the crew of <i>St. Foka</i></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea_ZFJ.PNG"><img alt="Franz Josef Land" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="534" data-file-width="710" 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kara_sea_ZFJ.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg"><img alt="Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky" data-file-height="761" data-file-width="553" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg/100px-Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg/150px-Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg/200px-Portrait_of_P._Semenov-Tien-Shansky.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky" title="Pyotr Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky">Pyotr Semyonov-Tyan-Shansky</a></b>!<br/>(1827&#8211;1914)<br/>geographer, statistician, entomologist\n</td>\n<td>In 1856&#8211;57 Semyonov passed through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Altay_Mountains" title="Altay Mountains">Altay Mountains</a>, visited the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul" title="Issyk Kul">Issyk Kul</a> and came to the then largely unknown <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tian_Shan_Mountains" title="Tian Shan Mountains">Tian Shan Mountains</a>. He was the first European to see the peak of <a href="/wiki/Khan_Tengri" title="Khan Tengri">Khan Tengri</a>. He disproved <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Humboldt" title="Alexander Humboldt">Alexander Humboldt</a>\'s earlier claims about Tian Shan\'s supposed volcanic origins. In 1858, he published the first systematic description of the Tian Shan. Half a century later <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II of Russia</a> authorized him to add the epithet "Tian-Shansky" to his last name. For many years Semyonov served as chairman of Russia\'s Central Committee for Statistics, where he organized the first <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census" title="Russian Empire Census">Russian Empire Census</a> held in 1897. Semyonov amassed a large collection of the old Dutch masters, which now belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a>, and an insect collection of c. 700,000 specimens. He was a member of 53 learned societies and headed the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a> for 40 years from 1873 until his death, using this position to encourage the exploration of inland <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, notably by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Przhevalsky" title="Nikolai Przhevalsky">Nikolai Przhevalsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Kozlov" title="Pyotr Kozlov">Pyotr Kozlov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-8"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brockhaus_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-brockhaus-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seidenstrasse_GMT_Ausschnitt_Zentralasien.jpg"><img alt="Tian Shan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a style="background:#ffe8d5;">\n<th align="center" scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yuri_Senkevich" title="Yuri Senkevich">Yuri Senkevich</a></b><img alt="dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1937&#8211;2003)<br/>physician, scientist, traveler, TV anchorman\n</td>\n<td>Senkevich participated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/12th_Soviet_Antarctic_expedition" title="12th Soviet Antarctic expedition">12th Soviet Antarctic expedition</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vostok_station" title="Vostok station">Vostok station</a> in 1966&#8211;67. In 1969 he sailed with <a href="/wiki/Thor_Heyerdahl" title="Thor Heyerdahl">Thor Heyerdahl</a> on the <i>Ra</i> <a href="/wiki/Papyrus" title="Papyrus">papyrus</a> boat, and later on the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ra_II" title="Ra II">Ra II</a></i> across the Atlantic Ocean in 1970. He also sailed with Heyerdahl on another <a href="/wiki/Reed_(plant)" title="Reed (plant)">reed</a> boat the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigris_(boat)" title="Tigris (boat)">Tigris</a></i> across the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> in 1978. In 1973&#8211;2003, Senkevich was a host of the <i>"Travelers\' Club"</i> show on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Television" title="Soviet Television">Soviet Television</a> for a record 30 years, making it into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_Records" title="Guinness Book of Records">Guinness Book of Records</a>. He visited more than 200 countries as a journalist and TV anchorman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RaII.InMuseum.jpg"><img alt="Ra II boat" class="thumbimage" Museum">Kon-Tiki Museum</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffffd0;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Severtzov_ru_WP.jpg"><img alt="Severtzov" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="409" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Severtzov_ru_WP.jpg/100px-Severtzov_ru_WP.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Severtzov_ru_WP.jpg/200px-Severtzov_ru_WP.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Severtzov" title="Nikolai Severtzov">Nikolai Severtzov</a></b>!<br/>(1827&#8211;1885)<br/>naturalist\n</td>\n<td>In 1857&#8211;58, on an expedition to <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syr Darya</a> in Central Asia, Severtzov was captured by <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">Kokand</a> bandits and severely wounded. He was freed after a month by the Russian military and continued his studies. In 1865&#8211;68 he explored the <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> and Lake <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Issyk_Kul" title="Issyk Kul">Issyk Kul</a>. In 1877&#8211;78 he explored the unknown areas of the <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir Mountains</a> following a route close to the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pamir_Highway" title="Pamir Highway">Pamir Highway</a> as far as Lake Yashil Kul on the Ghunt River. Severtzov wrote a major study of <a href="/wiki/Turkestan" title="Turkestan">Turkestan</a> zoology called <i>Vertical and horizontal distribution of Turkestan wildlife</i> (1873), which included the first description of a number of animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brockhaus_91-4"><a href="#cite_note-brockhaus-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Argali.jpg"><img alt="Argali" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="288" data-file-width="334" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Argali.jpg/180px-Argali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Argali.jpg/240px-Argali.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Argali.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Argali" title="Argali">Argali</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grigory_Shelikov.jpg"><img alt="Shelikhov" data-file-height="479" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Grigory_Shelikov.jpg/110px-Grigory_Shelikov.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Grigory_Shelikov.jpg/220px-Grigory_Shelikov.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Grigory_Shelikhov" title="Grigory Shelikhov">Grigory Shelikhov</a></b>^<br/> (1747&#8211;1795)<br/>seafarer, merchant\n</td>\n<td>Shelikhov organized commercial trips of merchant ships to the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a> starting in 1775. Together with Ivan Golikov, he founded the precursor of the <a href="/wiki/Russian-American_Company" title="Russian-American Company">Russian-American Company</a> (the name appeared in 1799 after Shelikhov\'s death). In 1783&#8211;86, he led an expedition to the shores of <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">Russian America</a>, during which he founded the first permanent Russian settlement in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> in <a href="/wiki/Three_Saints_Bay" title="Three Saints Bay">Three Saints Bay</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak Island</a>. In 1790 he hired <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A._A._Baranov" title="A. A. Baranov">Alexander Baranov</a> to manage fur enterprise in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;"> Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shelikhov_Bay" title="Shelikhov Bay">Shelikhov Bay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shelikhov_Strait" title="Shelikhov Strait">Shelikhov Strait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shelekhov" title="Shelekhov">Shelekhov</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shelikhov_settlement.jpg"><img alt="Shelikhov\'s settlement on Kodiak" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="337" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="74" href="/wiki/File:Shelikhov_settlement.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The settlement of Shelikhov on <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f0f8ff;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Petr_Shirshov.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="169" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Petr_Shirshov.JPG/110px-Petr_Shirshov.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Petr_Shirshov.JPG/165px-Petr_Shirshov.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Petr_Shirshov.JPG 2x" width="110"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Shirshov" title="Pyotr Shirshov">Pyotr Shirshov</a></b><img alt="double-dagger" data-file-height="14" data-file-width="9" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f9/Double-dagger-14-plain.png" width="9"/><br/>(1905&#8211;1953)<br/>oceanographer, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrobiologist" title="Hydrobiologist">hydrobiologist</a>, statesman, Hero of the Soviet Union\n</td>\n<td>Shirshov participated in numerous Arctic expeditions, including the ones on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icebreaker_Sibiryakov" title="Icebreaker Sibiryakov">icebreaker Sibiryakov</a> (1932) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steamship_Chelyuskin" title="Steamship Chelyuskin">steamship Chelyuskin</a> (1934). He was among the crew of the <a href="/wiki/Drifting_ice_station" title="Drifting ice station">drifting ice station</a> <i><a href="/wiki/North_Pole-1" title="North Pole-1">North Pole-1</a></i> in 1937&#8211;38. In 1942&#8211;48, Shirshov was a Maritime Minister of the Soviet Union. In 1946&#8211;53, he became the founder and the first director of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_of_Oceanology_of_the_Soviet_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Institute of Oceanology of the Soviet Academy of Sciences">Institute of Oceanology of the Soviet Academy of Sciences</a>. He wrote numerous works about plankton in the polar regions and proved that there is life in the high latitudes of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bse_20-9"><a href="#cite_note-bse-20">[20]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Shirshov_Institute_of_Oceanology" title="Shirshov Institute of Oceanology">Shirshov Institute of Oceanology</a></span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_Ocean_-_en.png"><img alt="Arctic Ocean" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="329" decoding="async" height="120" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Gleb_Shishmaryov" title="Gleb Shishmaryov">Gleb Shishmaryov</a></b>^<br/> (1781&#8211;1835)<br/>Russian Navy officer, circumnavigator\n</td>\n<td>In 1815&#8211;18 Shishmaryov accompanied <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Kotzebue" title="Otto von Kotzebue">Otto von Kotzebue</a> on his circumnavigation on <i>Rurik</i>, including the visit to <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, when they discovered the <a href="/wiki/Shishmaref_Inlet" title="Shishmaref Inlet">Shishmaref Inlet</a>. In 1820 he returned to Alaska accompanied by Lt. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ensign_Mikhail_Vasiliev" title="Ensign Mikhail Vasiliev">Mikhail Vasiliev</a>. They explored the coast of Alaska from <a href="/wiki/Kotzebue_Sound" title="Kotzebue Sound">Kotzebue Sound</a> to <a href="/wiki/Icy_Cape,_Alaska" title="Icy Cape, Alaska">Icy Cape</a> and later from <a href="/wiki/Norton_Sound" title="Norton Sound">Norton Sound</a> to Cape Newenham. <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_Island" title="St. Lawrence Island">St. Lawrence Island</a> was mapped on the return voyage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rbd_19-6"><a href="#cite_note-rbd-19">[19]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Shishmaref,_Alaska" title="Shishmaref, Alaska">Shishmaref, Alaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shishmaref_Inlet" title="Shishmaref Inlet">Shishmaref Inlet</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AKMap-doton-Savoonga.png"><img alt="St. Lawrence Island" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="186" title="Alaska">Alaska</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shkot_n_y.jpg"><img alt="Shkot" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Shkot_n_y.jpg/150px-Shkot_n_y.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Shkot_n_y.jpg/200px-Shkot_n_y.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Shkot" title="Nikolay Shkot">Nikolay Shkot</a></b>*<br/>(1829&#8211;1870)<br/>Russian Navy officer\n</td>\n<td>After being wounded in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1854%E2%80%931855)" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1854&#8211;1855)">Siege of Sevastopol (1854&#8211;1855)</a>, Shkot served in the Far East. In 1856&#8211;63 he explored <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moneron_Island" title="Moneron Island">Moneron Island</a> and the coast of <a href="/wiki/Primorsky_Krai" title="Primorsky Krai">Primorsky Krai</a> in the area of <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great_Gulf" title="Peter the Great Gulf">Peter the Great Gulf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nakhodka_Bay" title="Nakhodka Bay">Nakhodka Bay</a>, making a number of discoveries. He founded a hydrographic post in what is now modern <a href="/wiki/Nakhodka" title="Nakhodka">Nakhodka</a>, and was one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a> in 1860.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Shkot_Island" title="Shkot Island">Shkot Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shkotovo" title="Shkotovo">Shkotovo</a> (village), <a href="/wiki/Shkotovka_River" title="Shkotovka River">Shkotovka River</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" East</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#fff8e7;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shokalsky.jpg"><img alt="Shokalsky" data-file-height="802" data-file-width="530" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Shokalsky.jpg/100px-Shokalsky.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Shokalsky.jpg/150px-Shokalsky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Shokalsky.jpg/200px-Shokalsky.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Yuly_Shokalsky" title="Yuly Shokalsky">Yuly Shokalsky</a></b>~<br/>(1856&#8211;1940)<br/>Russian Navy officer, oceanographer, meteorologist, cartographer, geographer\n</td>\n<td>In 1897&#8211;1901 Shokalsky researched <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ladoga" title="Lake Ladoga">Lake Ladoga</a>. From 1907 he supervised all oceanographic works in Russia. He coined the term <i><a href="/wiki/World_Ocean" title="World Ocean">World Ocean</a></i>. In 1919 he headed the commission that set up <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_zones_in_Russia" title="Time zones in Russia">time zones in Russia</a>. In 1918&#8211;31 he was the head of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Geographical_Society" title="Russian Geographical Society">Russian Geographical Society</a> and contributed widely to <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> exploration at this post.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a href="/wiki/Shokalsky_Strait" title="Shokalsky Strait">Shokalsky Strait</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shokalskogo_Island" title="Shokalskogo Island">Shokalskogo Island</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Empire_Map.jpg"><img alt="A map of Russia by Shokalsky" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6048" data-file-width="8397" decoding="async" height="86" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Empire_Map.jpg/120px-Russian_Empire_Map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Empire_Map.jpg/180px-Russian_Empire_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Empire_Map.jpg/240px-Russian_Empire_Map.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Empire_Map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> by Shokalsky</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#FFFFFF;">\n<th align="center" scope="row"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg"><img alt="Solovyev" data-file-height="270" data-file-width="233" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg/100px-Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg/150px-Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg/200px-Anatoly_Solovyev_portraitlike.jpeg 2x" width="100"/></a>\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Solovyev" title="Anatoly Solovyev">Anatoly Solovyev</a></b>$<br/>(born 1948)<br/>cosmonaut, aviator, Hero of the Soviet Union\n</td>\n<td>Solovyev holds the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cumulative_spacewalk_records" title="List of cumulative spacewalk records">world record</a> for the number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">spacewalks</a> (16), and accumulated time spent spacewalking (over 82&#160;hours), which he performed during his five spaceflights. In 1988 he traveled on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-5" title="Soyuz TM-5">Soyuz TM-5</a></i> to the <i><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> and back on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-4" title="Soyuz TM-4">Soyuz TM-4</a></i>. In 1990 he again traveled to <i>Mir</i> and back on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-9" title="Soyuz TM-9">Soyuz TM-9</a></i>, and in 1990 made a similar journey on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-15" title="Soyuz TM-15">Soyuz TM-15</a></i>. In 1995 he got to <i>Mir</i> on Space Shuttle <i><a href="/wiki/STS-71" title="STS-71">STS-71</a></i> and went back on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-21" title="Soyuz TM-21">Soyuz TM-21</a></i>, and in 1997&#8211;98 again traveled to <i>Mir</i> and back on <i><a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-26" title="Soyuz TM-26">Soyuz TM-26</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SolovyevEVA.jpg"><img alt="Solovyev on a spacewalk" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="211" data-file-width="320" decoding="async" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/SolovyevEVA.jpg/120px-SolovyevEVA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/SolovyevEVA.jpg/180px-SolovyevEVA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/SolovyevEVA.jpg/240px-SolovyevEVA.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SolovyevEVA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solovyev on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">spacewalk</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#ffdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Somov" title="Mikhail Somov">Mikhail Somov</a></b>&#167;<br/>(1908&#8211;1973)<br/>geographer, oceanologist, Hero of the Soviet Union\n</td>\n<td>In 1950&#8211;51, Somov headed the second <a href="/wiki/Drifting_ice_station" title="Drifting ice station">drifting ice station</a>, <i>North Pole-2</i>. In 1955&#8211;57, he became the leader of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Soviet_Antarctic_Expedition" title="1st Soviet Antarctic Expedition">1st Soviet Antarctic Expedition</a> on the icebreakers <i><a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena</a></i>. The expedition established the first Soviet Antarctic station, <a href="/wiki/Mirny_Station" title="Mirny Station">Mirny</a>, performed some observations and reconnaissance, and researched the oceanography of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. Somov was also the first Soviet delegate to the international Scientific Committee for Antarctic Research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Named in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3334_Somov" title="3334 Somov">3334 Somov</a> (minor planet).</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LakeVostok-Location.jpg"><img alt="Vostok Station" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="884" data-file-width="1043" decoding="async" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/LakeVostok-Location.jpg/120px-LakeVostok-Location.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/LakeVostok-Location.jpg/180px-LakeVostok-Location.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/LakeVostok-Location.jpg/240px-LakeVostok-Location.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LakeVostok-Location.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vostok_Station" title="Vostok Station">Vostok Station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfffdf;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Stadukhin" title="Mikhail Stadukhin">Mikhail Stadukhin</a></b>*<br/>(?&#8211;1666)<br/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Cossack" title="Siberian Cossack">Siberian Cossack</a> leader\n</td>\n<td>In 1643, accompanied by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a>, Stadukhin led a group of Cossacks from  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigirka" title="Indigirka">Indigirka</a> to the east by the Arctic coast. They discovered the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a> and founded <a href="/wiki/Srednekolymsk" title="Srednekolymsk">Srednekolymsk</a> there. In 1649 he followed by sea the traces of Dezhnyov\'s and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedot_Popov" title="Fedot Popov">Fedot Popov</a>\'s expedition to the east, which started earlier in 1648 (and reached the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>). He learned from the captive natives that two of Dezhnyov\'s <a href="/wiki/Koch_(boat)" title="Koch (boat)">kochi</a> had been wrecked and the crews killed by the natives. Later Stadukhin found the connection of the Kolyma watershed to that of the <a href="/wiki/Anadyr_River" title="Anadyr River">Anadyr</a> and thus explored the land way to the <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukchi Peninsula</a>, where he found Dezhnyov in 1650. In 1651 Stadukhin set off south and discovered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penzhin_Bay" title="Penzhin Bay">Penzhin Bay</a> of the northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Okhotsk_Sea" title="Okhotsk Sea">Okhotsk Sea</a>. He also may have explored the western shores of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfisher_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-rfisher-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kolymarivermap.png"><img alt="Kolyma River" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kolymarivermap.png/120px-Kolymarivermap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kolymarivermap.png/180px-Kolymarivermap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kolymarivermap.png/240px-Kolymarivermap.png 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kolymarivermap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a></div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#dfdfff;">\n<th scope="row">\n</th>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Steller" title="Georg Wilhelm Steller">Georg Wilhelm Steller</a></b>^<br/>(1709&#8211;1746)<br/>botanist, zoologist, physician\n</td>\n<td>In 1734 Steller moved from <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> to work at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Saint Petersburg Academy of Sciences">Saint Petersburg Academy of Sciences</a>. He traveled trough Siberia, researching its nature, and in 1740 reached <a href="/wiki/Okhotsk" title="Okhotsk">Okhotsk</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamchatka" title="Kamchatka">Kamchatka</a>. He joined <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a> on the voyage to <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. The expedition landed in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kayak_Island" title="Kayak Island">Kayak Island</a> in 1741, staying only long enough to take on fresh water. During this time Steller became the first European naturalist to describe a number of North American plants and animals, including the <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_jay" title="Steller\'s jay">Steller\'s jay</a>. On the return journey the expedition was shipwrecked on <a href="/wiki/Bering_Island" title="Bering Island">Bering Island</a>. Here Bering died, and almost half of the crew perished from scurvy. Despite the hardships, Steller studied the flora and fauna of the island in great detail. He collected the only existing detailed observations of the now extinct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steller_sea_cow" title="Steller sea cow">Steller sea cow</a>, a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirenian" title="Sirenian">sirenian</a> mammal. In the spring the crew constructed a new vessel and returned to Kamchatka, where Steller continued his research. He died on the journey to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>, but his journals were published by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Simon_Pallas" title="Peter Simon Pallas">Peter Simon Pallas</a> and were later used by other explorers, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_Cook" title="Captain Cook">Captain Cook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><br/><br/><span style="font-size:85%;">Naned in honor: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steller%27s_sea_lion" title="Steller\'s sea lion">Steller\'s sea lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_eider" title="Steller\'s eider">Steller\'s eider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_sea_ape" title="Steller\'s sea ape">Steller\'s sea ape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_sea_eagle" title="Steller\'s sea eagle">Steller\'s sea eagle</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steller_sea_cow" title="Steller sea cow">Steller sea cow</a>.</span>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg"><img alt="Steller\'s jay" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg/120px-Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg/180px-Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg/240px-Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stellers_jay_-_natures_pics.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_jay" title="Steller\'s jay">Steller\'s jay</a></div></div></div></div><div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Extanstellersseacowea.jpg"><img alt="Steller\'s sea cow" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="381" data-file-width="1316" decoding="async" height="35" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Extanstellersseacowea.jpg/120px-Extanstellersseacowea.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Extanstellersseacowea.jpg/180px-Extanstellersseacowea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Extanstellersseacowea.jpg/240px-Extanstellersseacowea.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Extanstellersseacowea.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Extinct <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_sea_cow" title="Steller\'s sea cow">Steller\'s sea cow</a> drawn by Steller</div></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="T">T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
